==1890s==

* 1890 On January 24, a gas explosion destroyed a home in [[Columbus, Ohio]], attracting a crowd of onlookers. While people were still gathered to look at the ruins of the home, a second gas explosion happened in a nearby home. The second explosion caused 4 deaths, and there were 32 injuries from both explosions.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dispatch.com/content/stories/local/2012/01/24/natural-gas-explosion-kills-four-injures-32.html|title=Columbus Mileposts - Jan. 24, 1890: Natural-gas explosion kills four, injures 32|author=Gerald Tebben|work=The Columbus Dispatch|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1895 On April 25, a woman in [[Wilkinsburg, Pennsylvania]] was investigating the smell of gas in a basement, while using a portable lantern. A series of explosions then followed, injuring that woman, and another woman, and damaging 4 homes. The gas leak was caused by gas being diverted into an older, defective gas main in the area.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive-free/pdf?res=950DE7D61130E333A2575AC2A9629C94649ED7CF | work=The New York Times | title=NATURAL GAS EXPLOSION; Houses Wrecked and Burned in Wilkinsburg, a Suburb of Pittsburg -- Two Women Severely Injured | date=April 29, 1895}}</ref>

* 1929 On July 22, two oil company patrolmen were killed by an explosion of a gas pipeline near [[Castaic, California]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=BlUiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9aMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5307,2163869&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=San Jose News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1930 On April 4, gas leaked into the sewer system in [[New York City, New York]], and later exploded. 6 people were injured, 5,000 were evacuated from nearby buildings, and telephone cables were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=MaVVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BUANAAAAIBAJ&pg=4090,2428747&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Rochester Evening Journal and the Post Express - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1930 A runaway horse smashed a wagon of lumber against a crude oil pipeline in [[Ripon, Wisconsin]] on May 24. The oil ignited and spread to nearby oil tanks, causing a blaze that destroyed a number of buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=7rNFAAAAIBAJ&sjid=P70MAAAAIBAJ&pg=5405,1576502&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald and Times-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1930 Excavation in [[Fairport, New York]] caused a major gas explosion on July 30. 3 people were killed, 10 were injured, and a 4 family house was damaged by the blast and following fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Tt9PAAAAIBAJ&sjid=s1QDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4928,3455313&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Evening Independent - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1931 4 campers near [[Kilgore, Texas]] were burned to death when they were surrounded by gas from a pipeline leak that caught fire on April 17. The flames also spread to brush and timber in the area, preventing rescuers from reaching the bodies for 3 hours.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=U75FAAAAIBAJ&sjid=h70MAAAAIBAJ&pg=4523,2631824&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1936 On February 19, a worker inside a sewer in [[Utica, New York]] ignited natural gas that had leaked into the sewer system. An explosion was triggered, and the following fire burned for more than 24 hours. 4,000 people were evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=puNBAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4akMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2245,1876242&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1936 On November 21, a pipeline serving a loading dock in [[Port Arthur, Texas]], ruptured and ignited. The burning oil killed 3 people, and injured 6 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VDcxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=-E8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=4028,3277719&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Prescott Evening Courier - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1937 An oil pipeline being repaired by gas welding exploded near [[Pryor, Oklahoma]] on January 26. 2 of the repair crew, and 4 wives of the repairmen were killed by the explosion and following fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=wgVRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Eb8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=3854,5051262&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1937 On February 5, a gas main thought to be damaged by flooding exploded in [[Louisville, Kentucky]]. At least 15 were injured, and a major fire swept through the area.<ref>[https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1961&dat=19370206&id=EmstAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bYsFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3804,6571119 ]{{dead link|date=January 2016}}</ref>
* 1937 At 3:17&nbsp;p.m. on March 18, 1937, with just minutes left in the school day and more than 500 students and teachers inside the building, a natural gas explosion leveled most of New London High School in Rusk County, Texas. Odorless natural gas had leaked into the basement and ignited, killing 298 children, most in grades 5 to 11. Dozens more later died of injuries. As a result of this disaster, Texas passed laws requiring that natural gas be mixed with a malodorant to warn of a gas leak.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://aoghs.org/oil-amanac/new-london-texas-school-explosion/ |title=New London Texas School Explosion &#124; |website=Aoghs.org |date=1937-03-18 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1937 On July 21, a gasoline explosion and fire hit a Phillips Pipeline pump station near [[Jefferson City, Missouri]], injuring a truck driver there.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1893&dat=19370721&id=r1IfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=J9IEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3606,2184414|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1939 On December 12, a pipeline being tested ruptured for {{convert|40|mi|km}}, near [[Wichita Falls, Texas]], injuring one person.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=3wZCAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QqoMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1967,2209102&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref
* 1940 A gas compressor plant exploded in [[Braintree, Massachusetts]] on April 4, killing four people and injuring 12 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=oDgmAAAAIBAJ&sjid=RU0DAAAAIBAJ&pg=7148,2546543&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=St. Petersburg Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1940 On August 29, a newly hired crew of repairmen were working on fixing a pipeline leak near [[Buffalo, Oklahoma]], when the pipeline exploded and started a fire. Five of the crew were killed, 10 others were burned, and 10 horses burned to death.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=WOJXAAAAIBAJ&sjid=RvUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1608,6231997&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Ft4-AAAAIBAJ&sjid=BU0MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1878,5305168&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1942 On October 5, a crude oil pipeline broke near [[Wichita, Kansas]], spilling crude oil into the [[Little Arkansas River]]. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19421005&id=B2heAAAAIBAJ&sjid=KWENAAAAIBAJ&pg=5411,6462968&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1943 On January 18, a grass fire near [[Tyler, Texas]] spread to a leak in an 8-inch diameter natural gas pipeline. The gas leak was initially small, but grew quickly, until the gas flames were about {{convert|200|ft|m}} high. Gas service was cut to 28,000 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=D4I9AAAAIBAJ&sjid=bzUMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3105,368888&dq=gas+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Bonham Daily Favorite - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1943 On May 17, flooding destroyed part of the "[[Big Inch]]" pipeline in [[Arkansas]], causing nearly a week of shut down to build a bypass around the damaged area. There were no injuries reported.
* 1943 On August 14, the recently built "[[Big Inch]]" crude oil pipeline developed a leak near [[Lancaster, Pennsylvania]], delaying the first batch of crude oil from that pipeline from reaching [[Philadelphia, Pennsylvania]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F10710FF3B581B7B93C7A81783D85F478485F9|title=LEAK IN 'BIG INCH' DELAYS OIL TO EAST -  Petroleum Passes Phoenixville, Pa., Then Line Has Break in Lancaster County - Article - NYTimes.com|date=15 August 1943|work=nytimes.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1943 On September 5, the "[[Big Inch]]" pipeline ruptured and burned near [[Lansdale, Pennsylvania]], with burning crude oil spilling into a creek, and destroying over 100 trees. The creek had to have 2 temporary earth dams built on it to stop the burning crude from spreading further. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1368&dat=19430906&id=9EMxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TA0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=4094,3052916|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1943 On December 4, the "[[Big Inch]]" started leaking near [[Okeana, Ohio]]. There were no injuries reported.<ref>[https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2206&dat=19431204&id=vwQtAAAAIBAJ&sjid=0tMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5918,575781 ]{{dead link|date=January 2016}}</ref>
* 1944 The "[[Big Inch]]" crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Connellsville, Pennsylvania]] on February 24, with the crude spill killing fish along a {{convert|12|mi|km|adj=on}} stretch of the Laurel Hill creek.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=_aQkAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sWkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6268,1993581&dq=big+inch+pipeline&hl=en|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1946 A crew working to connect a new gas main in [[Peru, Illinois]] on July 4, when the old gas main exploded, killing 5 of the work crew, and injuring 7 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=UQ8yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=auQFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2206,5373935&dq=gas+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Berkeley Daily Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1947 On November 30, an explosion hit a natural gas compressor station for a gas storage facility in [[Marion, Michigan]]. One worker was killed, and 6 others were injured, and gas service was interrupted in the area. 
* 1948 On February 28, crude oil spilled from a ruptured pipeline leading to storage tank in [[Oklahoma City, Oklahoma]]. Some teen boys in the area saw crude oil bubbling out of [[manhole cover]]s, and thought that igniting the oil would be a good idea. This caused a string of sewer explosions, causing manhole covers to fly {{convert|10|ft|m}} into the air.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=AptRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hmoDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6151,5706514&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1948 On March 18, the 20&nbsp;inch diameter "[[Little Big Inch]]" natural gas transmission pipeline near [[Petersburg, Indiana]] exploded and burned, throwing pieces of the pipe as far as {{convert|300|ft|m}} away from the blast point. 3 homes were destroyed by the fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=vUoKAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DUsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6541,3789077&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KysbAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JE0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=1757,1294833&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1948 A crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Linden, New Jersey]] on September 7, coating roads in the area in oil.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F40E17FD3E59157A93CAA91782D85F4C8485F9|title=PIPELINE LEAK REPAIRED -  Crude Oil Covers Large Area Near Homes in Jersey - Article - NYTimes.com|date=8 September 1948|work=nytimes.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1948 On October 18, vapors from a leaking butane pipeline at a refinery in [[Texas City, Texas]] spread out along a nearby highway, causing a number of cars to stall. The gas then exploded, killing 4 people, and seriously burning 17 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Qfw0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=deUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6953,1951404&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lrc.fema.gov/starweb/lrcweb/servlet.starweb?path=lrcweb/STARLibraries1.web&search=SUB%3Dtexas%20city%20explosion%201947|title=Lessons learned: a career firefighter thanks NFPA, and the author thanks a mentor [in "NFPA JOURNAL"] |accessdate=June 16, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120311165156/http://www.lrc.fema.gov/starweb/lrcweb/servlet.starweb?path=lrcweb%2FSTARLibraries1.web&search=SUB%3Dtexas%20city%20explosion%201947 |archivedate=March 11, 2012 |df= }}</ref>
* 1948 On November 19, a "[[Big Inch]]" gas pipeline pumping station had 2 explosions and caught fire near [[Seymour, Indiana]], causing $3,000,000 in damage, and injuring 17 workers at the station. Flames reached 300 feet high.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1144&dat=19481120&id=fGYcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Jk4EAAAAIBAJ&pg=5810,1888970|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=HZJZAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BUkNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5526,133546&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Painesville Telegraph - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 On January 18, the "[[Big Inch]]" gas transmission pipeline ruptured and burned near [[Batesville, Indiana]]. The cause was an electrical arc at a compressor station. One worker at the compressor station had facila burns.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19490119&id=62c0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=t8YEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3863,957890|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 A section of the "[[Little Big Inch]]" exploded and burned in [[North Vernon, Indiana]] on March 4, burning a mother and her infant. It was the fourth explosion on that pipeline in Indiana that year.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nYNIAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IoMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5756,727865&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 A road grader operator was seriously burned when his grader hit a 6-inch gas pipeline west of [[Mankato, Kansas]] on November 17.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=l0ZiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Q3cNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3055,4275635&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 On December 8, an explosion and fire occurred at a compressor station for a 24-inch natural gas pipeline in [[Centralia, Missouri]]. Flames could be seen for {{convert|150|mi|km}} away.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nxMpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=3dYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1313,5596122&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 A leaking gas line caused an explosion at a packing plant in [[Sioux City, Iowa]] on December 14. Eighteen workers were killed, and almost 100 injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=3lssAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MssEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3333,5082775&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1949 On December 15, a 22-inch natural gas pipeline exploded and burned near [[Carthage, Tennessee]], injuring two people. Flames shot {{convert|1,000|ft|m}} into the air.<ref>[https://archive.is/20120714052649/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QMoqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7cwFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4038,5125860&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en ] {{dead link|date=June 2017}}</ref>
* 1949 In [[Detroit, Michigan]] a high pressure gas main went "out of control" on December 15,  when a new pressure regulator was being installed, leading to a number a large gas explosions. Police evacuated the area before the explosions, but, six people were injured, and 5 stores destroyed.<ref>[https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2206&dat=19491215&id=pp8yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=EuoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3972,7808004 ]{{dead link|date=January 2016}}</ref>

==1950s==
* 1950 On March 13, an overhead pipeline at a refinery in [[Martinez, California]] leaked, causing flammable fumes to spread onto a highway. An automobile ignited the fumes, killed a woman, and injuring 2 other in vehicle. 3 autos were also burned.<ref name="google">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=x45IAAAAIBAJ&sjid=24MMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2449,2832098&dq=pipeline+explosion+g:locus&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1950 3 different explosion on the [[Big Inch]] gas transmission pipeline near [[Colonia, New Jersey]] were announced on April 11 to be from [[hydrostatic testing]] of that pipeline for weaknesses.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9D05E1DB143DE03BBC4A52DFB266838B649EDE | work=The New York Times | title='EXPLOSIONS' ARE MYTHS; Merely Water Eruption in Tests of Pipelines in Jersey | date=April 12, 1950}}</ref>
* 1950 The "[[Big Inch]]" gas pipeline exploded and burned on July 1, near [[Beallsville, Ohio]]. A house and a barn were destroyed by the fire.<ref name="google2">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=TJgcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rWQEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4508,13823&dq=big+inch+pipeline&hl=en|title=Sarasota Herald-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9402E0D81638E73ABC4B53DFB166838B649EDE | work=The New York Times | title=Pipeline Blast Investigated | date=July 3, 1950}}</ref>
* 1950 Three workers were killed in an underground vault in [[Los Angeles, California]] on August 22, when a gas main exploded. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/421264981.html?dids=421264981:421264981&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:AI&type=historic&date=Aug+23%2C+1950&author=&pub=Los+Angeles+Times&desc=Three+Killed+in+Explosion+of+Downtown+Gas+Main&pqatl=google | title=Three Killed in Explosion of Downtown Gas Main | date=August 23, 1950}}</ref>
* 1950 On September 7, a new natural gas pipeline exploded near [[Big Rapids, Michigan]]. Two barns were destroyed by the following fire, that was seen for 50 miles.<ref name="google3">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=_gtGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wecMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2207,5962333&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1950 A brand new natural gas transmission pipeline exploded, while initial pressure was building up, on September 20 near [[Wadley, Texas]]. About 300 yards of the pipe were ripped out of the ground.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=980CE6D8133DE03BBC4951DFBF66838B649EDE | work=The New York Times | title=Explosion Rips Gas Pipeline | date=September 21, 1950}}</ref>
* 1950 On November 24, a newly built 30-inch natural gas pipeline ruptured for nearly {{convert|3,000|ft|m}}, causing a fire that destroyed 2 homes under construction near [[King of Prussia, Pennsylvania]].<ref name="google4">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=pVZdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xFsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1216,2435826&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Washington Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1951 Two men welding on a crude oil pipeline at an oil Terminal in [[Kansas City, Kansas]] were severely burned on January 7, when a nearby valve failed, spraying them with crude oil that ignited. Both later died of their burns.<ref name="google5">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=vw8pAAAAIBAJ&sjid=3tYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5247,620245&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1951 On January 10, two gas explosions, 3 hours apart, hit [[McKees Rock, Pennsylvania]], injuring 8 people, igniting a fire, and causing widespread damage.<ref name="google6">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=wGIbAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bk0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=1379,3923275&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1951 On February 9, natural gas leaked from a gas line into a sewer system in [[Jefferson, Greene County, Pennsylvania|Jefferson, Pennsylvania]]. The gas was involved in 3 different home explosions, causing other homes to burn. 2 people were killed, 8 others injured, and, 6 homes destroyed.<ref name="google7">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19830813&id=HHxiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Z3cNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2500,2655687|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1951 A gas main pressure regulator failed in [[Rochester, New York]] on September 21, causing a series of explosion that last for 4 hours. 3 people were killed, and 30 homes were destroyed.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://select.nytimes.com/gst/abstract.html?res=FA0E13F93D5C117B93C0AB1782D85F458585F9 | work=The New York Times | title=30 HOMES WRECKED, 3 KILLED IN BLASTS; Gas Mains Explode for 4 Hours in Suburb of Rochester 5,000 Persons Routed 30 HOMES WRECKED, 3 KILLED IN BLASTS Gas Regulator Failed Struck by Steps Woman's Clothes Afire Seismograph Shows Shocks Workman Killed by Cave-In | date=September 22, 1951}}</ref>
* 1951 A Halloween Parade on October 31 in [[Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania]] was interrupted by 4 gas main explosions. 29 people were injured.<ref name="google8">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=TRhRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xtAMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4258,3040299&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1951 A 12-inch temporary gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Cranberry Township, Butler County, Pennsylvania|Cranberry, Pennsylvania]] on November 27, causing a {{convert|200|ft|m|adj=on}} high flame that could be seen for a number of miles away. The explosion was heard for 10 miles around. A pipeline compressor station under construction at the site was destroyed. A nearby Elementary school was relocated following the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.post-gazette.com/pg/11076/1132421-54.stm|title='Fiery torch' lit night in Cranberry|work=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette}}</ref><ref name="google9">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=pW9IAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sw8EAAAAIBAJ&pg=4530,3680264&dq=pipeline+explosion+g:locus&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1952 On May 17, a brand new valve being added to the 20 inch "[[Little Inch]]" gas transmission pipeline split open near [[Marietta, Pennsylvania]], knocking down pipeline company workers, 2 of whom were seriously injured. There was no fire.<ref name="google10">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eM0_AAAAIBAJ&sjid=ClgMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1194,4831381&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1952 On July 9, a gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[York, Pennsylvania]].<ref name="google11">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1913&dat=19520709&id=VfVGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4fMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3938,623061|title=Lewiston Evening Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1952 A pipeline explosion killed 2 men near [[Ackerly, Texas]] on July 17.
* 1952 Four men working on an 8-inch gas pipeline near [[Mount Pleasant, Michigan]] were burned when that pipeline ruptured as they raised it for reconditioning on September 26.<ref name="google12">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VzkiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=D6wFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5108,3178307&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Owosso Argus-Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1952 On October 18, a 26-inch gas pipeline, a branch of the "[[Big Inch]]" pipeline, started leaking at an insulated flange in [[Liberty Corner, New Jersey]]. A road was closed during the leak.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F00E17FD3A5B117A93CBA8178BD95F468585F9 | work=The New York Times | title=GAS INVADES LIFE AT LIBERTY CORNER; But Folk of Old Jersey Village Wait Calmly for Mending of Break in Pipeline | date=October 19, 1952}}</ref>
* 1952 On December 29, twelve persons were injured in a blast that shook the Lawndale district of [[Los Angeles, California]], when a ditching machine broke a gasoline-carrying pipeline and touched off a fiery explosion.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/424944471.html?dids=424944471:424944471&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:AI&type=historic&date=Dec+30%2C+1952&author=&pub=Los+Angeles+Times&desc=12+Injured+in+Explosion+of+Gasoline&pqatl=google | title=12 Injured in Explosion of Gasoline | date=December 30, 1952}}</ref>
* 1953 Five square miles of east of [[Boston, Massachusetts]] was evacuated on September 9 from a pipeline leaking about {{convert|1,000,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline.<ref name="google13">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=9mEpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=VIEFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5457,1189575&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Schenectady Gazette - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1953 On September 10, a gas explosion in [[Cleveland, Ohio]] killed one person and injured 50 others.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/baltsun/access/1686706612.html?FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:AI&type=historic&date=Sep+11%2C+1953&author=&pub=The+Sun+%281837-1985%29&desc=Cleveland+Gas+Blast+Kills+Woman%2C+Injures+50+Persons&pqatl=google | title=Cleveland Gas Blast Kills Woman, Injures 50 Persons | date=September 11, 1953 | work=The Sun}}</ref>
* 1953 A 30-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded on October 18 near [[Uniontown, Pennsylvania]], causing a massive fire that burned 5 miles of cornfields. There were no injuries reported.<ref name="google14">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YB5aAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cksNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5138,1480118&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1953 A US Air Force T-33 trainer jet crashed into a natural gas pipeline bridge over the [[Mississippi River]] on November 24 near [[Greenville, Mississippi]], rupturing and igniting the pipeline.<ref name="google15">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iIpWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Z0ENAAAAIBAJ&pg=4630,3488063&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1954 On January 17, a [[Panhandle Eastern]] gas transmission pipeline exploded in [[Lucas County, Ohio]], causing some nearby residents to evacuate. a crater 60 feet long, 10 feet deep, and 8 feet wide. Two other explosion had occurred on this pipeline in the previous 2 years in Lucas County, but a Panhandle Eastern representative said the 3 explosions were just a coincidence.<ref name="google16">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19540118&id=FEdOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fgAEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3392,1086191|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1954 A 40- to 50-year-old LP gas distribution line was blamed for causing an explosion in [[Goldsboro, North Carolina]] on April 12 that killed 5 people, injured 15 others, and demolished 3 buildings.<ref name="google17">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KlBgAAAAIBAJ&sjid=W3ENAAAAIBAJ&pg=6706,589983&dq=propane+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Star-News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 On February 15, a 20-inch Cities Service pipeline exploded south of [[Lawrence, Kansas]], ejecting a 20-foot section of pipeline. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19550216&id=mdlFAAAAIBAJ&sjid=w-cMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4053,2749402|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1955 The "[[Big Inch]]" gas pipeline exploded and burned near [[Roseville, Ohio]] on March 7. Flames reached {{convert|400|ft|m}} high, and {{convert|8|acre|m2}} of brush & timber burned.<ref name="google18">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=7hdUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tzkNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4781,2989734&dq=big+inch+pipeline&hl=en|title=St. Joseph News-Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 On March 9, a pipeline construction crew of 4 were killed while trying to move a pipeline for the building of a Toll road in [[Chesterton, Indiana]]. Two other pipeline workers were injured, and a school a quarter mile away was evacuated.<ref name="google19">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=7xdUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tzkNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4747,3085315&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=St. Joseph News-Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 A burst pipeline at a Refinery in [[Sunburst, Montana]] contaminated groundwater and soil in the area. Despite pumping out over {{convert|182,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline, pollution from the accident remained. In 2004, local residents and a school district won a Lawsuit for payments for damages.<ref name="greatfallstribune">{{cite web|url=http://www.greatfallstribune.com/news/stories/20040819/localnews/1075244.html|title=Texaco must pay Sunburst $41M - greatfallstribune.com|publisher=greatfallstribune.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="toxipedia">{{cite web|url=http://toxipedia.org/display/toxipedia/Sunburst%27s+Texaco+refinery|title=Sunburst&#39;s Texaco refinery - Toxipedia|publisher=toxipedia.org|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 A bulldozer ruptured and ignited a gas pipeline in [[Brookshire, Texas]]. Flames reached {{convert|250|ft|m}}, and the bulldozer operator was killed.<ref name="google20">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=PNUzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IOsFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5938,1185243&dq=ruptured+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Miami News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 On August 10, a gas leak in [[Ashtabula, Ohio]] was ignited by electrical equipment or lightning, causing a restaurant to explode. 21 people were killed, 15 more were injured, and 6 buildings destroyed.<ref name="google21">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=5y1kAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5XsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6842,1721328&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=The Calgary Herald - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 A gas pipeline being tested in [[Detroit, Michigan]] exploded and burned on September 7, injuring one person, and destroying 50 cars.<ref name="google22">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=CaVHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sv4MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1072,825942&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=Meriden Record - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 On October 10, a crew cleaning the outside of a natural gas pipeline with a heavy rubber ball ruptured a coupler, causing an explosion and fire east of [[Orleans, Indiana]]. Two members of the crew were killed, and 3 others were injured.<ref name="google23">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=N-IrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=D2YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3953,736357&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1955 A drag line operation in a gravel pit in [[Irving, Texas]] ruptured an 8-inch diameter gasoline pipeline on November 30. Gasoline spread out over about {{convert|10|acre|m2}}, then exploded and burned. 1 home was destroyed, but the family living there was away at the time of the explosion.<ref name="google24">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=uSBYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sPYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7216,6007452&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1956 On February 11, a corroded gas line from a gas main leaked, causing an explosion that killed 3 people at a meat packing plant in [[Toledo, Ohio]].<ref name="google25">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=G_MeAAAAIBAJ&sjid=1U0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=5271,3726082&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1956 A trench digging machine being used in building a freeway cut into a gasoline pipeline in [[West Los Angeles, California]] on February 27. At least 3 people were burned, with 9 homes, a warehouse, and a laundry catching on fire.<ref name="google26">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=JOE0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=_YcDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3705,5750752&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1956 On April 26, a new 26 inch gas transmission was being pressure tested near [[Moab, Utah]] with gas exploded, then burned, causing damage to a utility pole, and damaging a half mile of the pipeline. Mines in the region were shut down due to the lack of power. There were no injuries.<ref name="google27">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1338&dat=19560421&id=EvtXAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xfYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5677,2859128|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1956 A butane pipeline ruptured on October 16, forcing 25 families to evacuate from flammable fumes near [[Greenwich, Ohio]]. Trains were also stopped in the area, until the fumes dissipated. There were no injuries.<ref name="google28">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=HKIyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=FOwFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6614,5236&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Miami News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 On January 16, an explosion and fire occurred at a natural gas compressor station in [[Liberal, Kansas]], killing 3 workers at that station. 11 other workers were injured, and the fire burned for 2 hours. The shut down of this gas pipeline from the explosion affected customers as far away as Ohio in sub-zero weather conditions.<ref name="google29">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=GAJGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=yc8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=5583,2958581&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Portsmouth Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google30">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ayhcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bVUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2188,531629&dq=pipeline+explosion+g:locus&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 Two explosion from a natural gas main killed 3 people in [[Peoria, Illinois]] on January 17. 7 others were injured, and a home and a 2-story building were leveled.<ref name="google31">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eawpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5vYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2471,3738111&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 On January 23, the "[[Little Inch]]" gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[York, Pennsylvania]], causing flames reaching 200 feet high. There were no injuries.<ref name="google32">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=fawpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5vYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5792,4876970&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 A leaking gas main in [[Reno, Nevada]] led to three explosions on February 6. 2 people were killed, 42 others injured, and 5 buildings were destroyed.<ref name="google33">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=aX5HAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MXwMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4086,3548933&dq=gas+main+fire&hl=en|title=Warsaw Times - Union - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 On June 3, a 26-inch natural gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Ellinwood, Kansas]], destroying a farm house. One person was injured.<ref name="google34">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=jv5XAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9_YDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7140,222686&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 On October 18, a 16-inch gas transmission pipeline burst 30 miles from [[Spokane, Washington]], shutting down gas delivery to the Spokane area. A family near the rupture had to take cover.<ref name="google35">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QapfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=jzIMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2821,5990257&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Lewiston Morning Tribune - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1957 On December 5, a gas line in the basement of a store that was being worked on in [[Villa Rica, Georgia]], exploded. 13 people were killed in the explosion and following fire. At least 6 stores were destroyed.<ref name="google36">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=LTJaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QEwNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2954,4453700&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=St. Joseph Gazette - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 A natural gas metering station in [[Kimberly, Idaho]] exploded on February 17, killing two pipeline company workers, injuring another worker, and destroyed the metering building. There was no fire.<ref name="google37">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=8_lTAAAAIBAJ&sjid=2jgNAAAAIBAJ&pg=784,634871&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Sunday News-Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google38">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VolWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JucDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5461,5588353&dq=pipeline+explosion+g:locus&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 On June 1, gas leaking from a pipeline near [[Big Spring, Texas]] was ignited and exploded, killing 3 fishermen and seriously burning another fisherman.<ref name="google39">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=JQIdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4YoEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3902,62384&dq=killed+when+he+struck+a+pipeline&hl=en|title=Sarasota Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 A truck missed a curve on a road and crashed into a gas transmission pipeline compressor station near [[Kings Mountain, North Carolina]] on September 16. There was an explosion and fire, and the 2 men in the truck were killed.<ref name="google40">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=TV1gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wXENAAAAIBAJ&pg=5200,2714152&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Star-News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 On October 4, a gasoline pipeline was ruptured by a bulldozer in [[Hobbs, New Mexico]]. The gasoline ignited, injuring 3 people, damaging 6 homes, and threatened a number of other homes for a time.<ref name="google41">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=kPRVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cuIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3846,647380&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google42">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QPsnAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5Q8EAAAAIBAJ&pg=2674,3144088&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 On November 9, a jet fuel pipeline ruptured near the [[Blue Creek (Idaho)|Blue Creek]] in Idaho. Fuel flowed down the creek, and later ignited, damaging one home and destroying 6 bridges. Several were sicked by the fumes from incident.<ref name="google43">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=CDFWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=teYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7170,3675418&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google44">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=aEBYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=B_cDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7216,2207583&dq=pipeline+explosion+g:locus&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1958 A leaking and burning gas line under a street lead to several explosions at a Hotel in [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]], on December 14. 7 people were killed and 23 others injured.<ref name="google45">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=MDEaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uyUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5669,2658429&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1959 On April 29, a 20-inch pipeline owned by Laurel Pipeline ruptured near [[Hollidaysburg, Pennsylvania]] spilling thousands of gallons of gasoline onto fields a streams. Earthen dams were built to reduce the amount of gasoline spilling into fishing streams. The pipeline had been recently built.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19590429&id=6zoyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7uQFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6849,2123134|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1959 On May 22, a [[Buckeye Partners]] oil pipeline ruptured in [[Sylvania, Ohio]], spouting up in the lawn of one homeowner.<ref name="google46">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19590522&id=8vITAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9AAEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3164,852915|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1959 A worker on gas transmission pipeline was closing a valve, when it exploded near [[Newton, Pennsylvania]] on September 25. The worker was killed, and another worker was injured.<ref name="google47">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YwIqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=kSYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5410,2177289&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1959 On October 8, a 10-inch propane pipeline burst in [[Austin, Texas]]. 400 families had to be evacuated, due to the explosion & fire hazard. Eventually, the fumes dissipated without incident. The rupture was caused by a weak section of pipe.<ref name="google48">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=l4piAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rXcNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1049,3659911&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Washington Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

==1960s==

* 1960 Transwestern Pipeline Co.'s gas line 58 miles northwest of Roswell N.M. suffered an 8.1 mile brittle fracture during testing of the 30-inch X56 pipeline. It failed at about 850&nbsp;psi.<ref>
Oil & Gas Journal April 25, 1960 - Vol 58 No. 17</ref>
* 1960 An estimated 125,000 persons in southwest Missouri were without gas in subfreezing temperatures for several days due to a ditch-digging machine rupturing a pipeline.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/baltsun/access/1701383552.html?FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:AI&type=historic&date=Jan+22%2C+1960&author=&pub=The+Sun+%281837-1985%29&desc=125%2C000+LEFT+WITHOUT+FUEL+IN+MISSOURI&pqatl=google | title=125,000 Left Without Fuel In Missouri | date=January 22, 1960 | work=The Sun}}</ref>
* 1960 On Saturday, March 19, a leaking 1 1/2 inch gas line lead to gas migrating through a sewer line, from a church into a school, in [[Wauseon, Ohio]]. The gas later exploded, damaging the school and injuring six.  Classes were not in session at that time.<ref name="google49">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19600322&id=F2ZRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=-gAEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7141,6255426|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1960 In July, excavation work in [[Merrill, Wisconsin]] causes a gas leak and gas explosion that killed 10 people.<ref name="google50">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KTcaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9xAEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5167,828174&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1960 A ditching machine used in laying a water main hit an 8-inch natural gas pipeline in [[Sarasota, Florida]] on October 5. 9 People were injured in the following explosion and fire.<ref name="google51">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=FXkcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=KmUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7380,1060319&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Sarasota Herald-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1960 On October 27, a 16-inch gas transmission pipeline near [[Checotah, Oklahoma]] exploded while it was being worked on to repair a leak. 2 of the repair crew died, and 4 others were injured.<ref name="google52">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=v29DAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JK4MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1347,1621086&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Altus Times-Democrat - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1960 On December 12, a leaking 8-inch pipeline at a tanker dock in [[Richmond, California]] spilled gasoline into the [[San Francisco Bay]].<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F20917FC3D541A7A93C1A81789D95F448685F9 | work=The New York Times | title=FIRE PERIL IN COAST BAY; Gasoline From Pipeline Break Surrounds Two Vessels | date=December 13, 1960}}</ref>
* 1960 A 30-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned at a gas sub station in [[Huntington, West Virginia]] on December 19. Windows were broken, 1 homes was damaged, and brush burned, but there were no injuries.<ref name="google53">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YNddAAAAIBAJ&sjid=6V4NAAAAIBAJ&pg=4428,776370&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Washington Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1961 On January 4, a gas pipeline failure near [[Waynesburg, Pennsylvania]] ignited, causing a fire that was widely seen in the area. There were no injuries.<ref name="google54">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=EsRWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=40ENAAAAIBAJ&pg=5975,1153855&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The News-Dispatch - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1961 On February 22, a pipeline exploded and burned in a refinery in [[Borger, Texas]], killing 9 members of a construction crew, and burning another crewman.<ref name="google55">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=kWQtAAAAIBAJ&sjid=lYkFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2367,3226209&dq=phillips+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Schenectady Gazette - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1961 The main City of [[Miami, Florida]] Garage was destroyed by a gas explosion on February 23. The blast was caused by a ditch digging machine being used in the garage hitting and rupturing a 2-inch gas pipe. One person was seriously burned by the blast, and 2 fire fighters were injured fight the fire that followed the blast.<ref name="google56">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=AWlVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wD4NAAAAIBAJ&pg=3738,4005810&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Miami News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1961 A [[Transcontinental Pipeline]] 36-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded near [[Laurel, Mississippi]] on June 18. 10 people were injured, and one home was destroyed from flames that went hundreds of feet in the air. A crater {{convert|30|ft|m}} long and {{convert|20|ft|m}} deep was created by the failure.<ref name="google57">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Oj5QAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IFcDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2604,2966218&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Evening Independent - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9403E6DB113FE13ABC4152DFB066838A679EDE | work=The New York Times | title=Ten Hurt in Pipeline Blast | date=June 19, 1961}}</ref>
* 1961 A 26-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Trapp, Kentucky]] on September 10. 22 people suffered various burn injuries.<ref name="google58">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=8WpVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=2z4NAAAAIBAJ&pg=3645,5039444&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Miami News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="centralkynews">{{cite web|url=http://articles.centralkynews.com/2011-09-14/winchestersun/30157958_1_gas-line-explosion-vaughn-burns|title=Gas line explosion injured 22 in Trapp 50 years ago - Central Kentucky News|publisher=articles.centralkynews.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="lex18">{{cite web|url=http://www.lex18.com/news/woman-reflects-on-pipeline-explosion-from-50-years-ago|title=Woman Reflects On Pipeline Explosion From 50 Years Ago &#124; LEX18.com|publisher=lex18.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

There were no injuries.<ref name="google60">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yQJdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BVoNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3543,2844843&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=St. Joseph Gazette - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

There were no injuries or damage.<ref name="google61">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=mUYqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sE4EAAAAIBAJ&pg=7267,3005942&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1962 Gas leaking from a 10-inch natural gas transmission pipeline exploded on February 20 in [[Portage, Ohio]], injuring 6 people and destroying a home.<ref name="google62">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=-gFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LQEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5401,1393923&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

Nearby schools were impacted.<ref name="google63">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19620424&id=ygwwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LwEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6139,2249555|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1962 On June 14, a backhoe ruptured a gas transmission pipeline near [[Idaho Falls, Idaho]]. The escaping gas exploded and ignited later on while a crew was trying to repair the line. One of the crew was killed, and 5 others injured in the fire.<ref name="google64">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ieQuAAAAIBAJ&sjid=C0oDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3816,3304230&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Deseret News Salt Lake Telegram - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1962 On August 2, a natural gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Clearwater, Florida]], next to US Highway 19, forcing that road's closure for a time. There were no injuries reported. Investigators found the line had previous mechanical damage as a cause of the failure.<ref name="google65">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VQcTAAAAIBAJ&sjid=EgUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1611,292896&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Ocala Star-Banner - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google66">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nXpPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fFIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6901,1637801&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=St. Petersburg Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1962 A 30-inch gas transmission failed on August 3 in [[Kansas City, Kansas]]. The gas flowed for 10 minutes before exploding and igniting. An 8-inch gas distribution pipeline was also ruptured, 11 homes were destroyed, and 23 others were damaged. At least one person was injured.<ref name="google67">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=FD4yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=W-UFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6099,2495364&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1962 On September 11, an 8-inch propane/LPG pipeline was ruptured by road building equipment near [[Eatonton, Georgia]]. One of the road workers was overcome and asphyxiated by the propane fumes. Propane fumes followed the [[Oconee River]] for {{convert|10|mi|km}} into Lake Sinclair.<ref name="google68">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=tetMAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZDEDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6958,1257654&dq=propane+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Rome News-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

There were no injuries.<ref name="google69">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1913&dat=19621017&id=r74gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=yWkFAAAAIBAJ&pg=1675,4473894|title=Lewiston Evening Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1963 On January 2, a gas transmission pipeline ruptured, due to a defective weld, in [[San Francisco, California]]. * 1965 On January 6, a house in [[Garnett, Kansas]] was destroyed by an explosion, and later on gas was found leaking from a 2-inch gas line in the street front of it, and was suspected as the cause. A young boy was killed. * 1965 On January 21, an 8-inch [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline propane transmission pipeline {{convert|15|mi|km}} east of [[Jefferson City, Missouri]] leaked. The propane spread along the ground, and exploded several hours later, scorching an area over a mile wide. A girl being dropped off at a school bus stop was severely burned and later died, and 2 other people were burned.<ref name="google85">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=20IrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XNQEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2031,850342&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Nevada Daily Mail - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1965 A 32-inch gas transmission pipeline, north of [[Natchitoches, Louisiana]], belonging to the [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] exploded and burned from [[Stress corrosion cracking]] (SCC) on March 4, killing 17 people. At least 9 others were injured, and 7 homes 450 feet from the rupture were destroyed. This accident, and others of the era, led then-President [[Lyndon B. Johnson]] to call for the formation of a national pipeline safety agency in 1967. The same pipeline had also had an explosion on May 9, 1955, just {{convert|930|ft|m}} from the 1965 failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/louisiana/53/natchitoches,-la-gas-pipeline-explosion,-mar-1965|title=Natchitoches, LA Gas Pipeline Explosion, Mar 1965|work=GenDisasters ... * 1965 On August 21, a 9-year-old girl was killed and eight people were injured in a [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline explosion in western [[Van Wert County, Ohio]]. The explosion threw up flames that could be seen from {{convert|40|mi|km}} away and scorched a {{convert|100|acre|km2|adj=on}} area of farmland. A home about 800 yards away was shifted off of its foundation, and half a mile of railroad ties set on fire. The girl was killed in her bed in a house 300 yards from the blast site. The rest of her family was injured. Investigators said the explosion was caused by gas leaking from an 8-inch pipeline, and was apparently ignited by a spark from a passing train.<ref name="google91">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yaEyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BusFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5966,1540001&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Miami News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thevwindependent.com/news/2015/08/elgin-propane-gas-explosion-remembered-50-years-later/|title=Elgin propane gas explosion remembered|work=The VW independent}}</ref>

The danger of fire or explosion forced evacuations of residents in a {{convert|2|sqmi|km2|adj=on}} area. * A survey by the [[Federal Power Commission]] of 51 gas pipeline companies show that between January 1, 1950, and June 30, 1965 showed that gas transmission pipeline failures had killed 64 people and injured another 222. of the fatalities, 35 were gas pipeline company workers or contractors, and 29 were members of the public.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F30C1FF6385B1A7B93C0AB178AD85F438685F9 | work=The New York Times | first=Gene | last=Smith | title=NADER STRESSES PIPELINE SAFETY; Explosion in Queens Viewed as Having Far-Reaching Impact on Gas Group JOHNSON PLEA PRAISED Crusader Urges That Entire Industry Keep Up Lines, 'Just as Roads Do' | date=January 22, 1967}}</ref>
