* 1967 A leaking gas main in the Jamaica section of [[New York City, New York]] caught fire on January 13. 2 pieces of [[FDNY]] equipment responding to the gas leak report were burned, as well as numerous buildings. The fire spread to 13 alarm size, with 63 fire companies being used to control the situation. 17 homes were destroyed. The cause of the leak was the failure of a moisture scrubbing "drip pot" on the pipeline.<ref name="google100">{{cite book|title=Responding to Routine Emergencies|author=Montagna, F.C.|date=1999|publisher=Fire Engineering|isbn=9780912212814|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=jqRIRCyWSRgC|page=86|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google101">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=f3BIAAAAIBAJ&sjid=I1wDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7067,2414862&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=St. Petersburg Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google102">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=8zhWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7ugDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6242,4456137&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1967 Manufacturers Light and Heat Company announced they were requesting to the Federal Power Commission permission to allow a new pipeline to replace 73.5 miles of older pipeline, which was having 200 to 450 leaks a year in Eastern Pennsylvania.<ref name="google103">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=1kkmAAAAIBAJ&sjid=SP8FAAAAIBAJ&pg=1009,1979679&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Gettysburg Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1967 On May 16, a pile driver ruptured a propane pipeline in [[Dearborn, Michigan]]. The escaping gas caught fire, with 2 construction workers being killed, and 4 others seriously burned.<ref name="google104">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=HFYlAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5asFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4949,1632474&dq=propane+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Owosso Argus-Press - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1967 A leaking pipeline released {{convert|30000|oilbbl|m3}} of JP-4 grade jet fuel in [[Wilmington, California]] on June 30. There was no fire.<ref name="google105">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=1QlSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=8DQNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6819,430892&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Press-Courier - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1967 On August 5, a leaking gas main forced 5 homes to be evacuated in [[Queens, New York]].<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F00D1FF73D5C177A93C4A91783D85F438685F9 | work=The New York Times | title=Gas Leak in Queens | date=August 6, 1967}}</ref>
* 1967 On August 10, a gas main that had been capped the day before leaked natural gas into a concession stand in [[Bamberg, South Carolina]]. An explosion of the gas was likely caused by an electrical spark, but the 6:40&nbsp;am time likely prevented any injuries.<ref name="google106">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1876&dat=19670811&id=9nssAAAAIBAJ&sjid=yswEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4182,1742904|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1967 A road construction machine ruptured an 18-inch [[Plantation Pipeline]] on September 25 in [[Akron, Alabama]], spilling more than 5,000 gallons of gasoline. The gasoline had to be burned off to eliminate it.<ref name="google107">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1817&dat=19670927&id=Yg4fAAAAIBAJ&sjid=I5sEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7162,4640244|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 On the night of January 8, a City Water crew in [[Reading, Pennsylvania]] snagged a 3/4 inch gas line, causing it to pull out of a gas main 14 feet away. About 2 hours later, there was an explosion that destroyed 2 nearby semidetached homes, killing 9 people in those structures.<ref name="ntsb">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1971/PSS711.pdf|date=14 December 2012|title=Special study of effects of delay in shutting down failed pipeline systems and methods of providing rapid shutdown|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 A petroleum products pipeline was discovered to be leaking on January 27, near [[Kokomo, Mississippi]]. Damage to cotton crops and water wells was discovered soon afterward.<ref name="findlaw">{{cite web|url=http://caselaw.findlaw.com/ga-court-of-appeals/1060181.html|title=PLANTATION PIPELINE COMPANY v. ROYAL INDEMNITY COMPANY - FindLaw|publisher=caselaw.findlaw.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* '''[[Richmond, Indiana explosion]]''': On April 6, 1968, natural gas leaking from a pipeline in [[Richmond, Indiana]] built up in a sporting goods store and exploded. Gunpowder in that store exploded later on. 42 people were killed, 150 were injured, and 15 buildings destroyed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gendisasters.com/data1/in/explosions/richmond-gasexplosion-apr1968.htm|title=Indiana|publisher=}}</ref><ref name="google108">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19680408&id=hi8xAAAAIBAJ&sjid=lgEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7348,6721892|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 On April 15, gasoline odor was detected at a drinking fountain in [[Glendale, California]]. The water well that fed the fountain was determined to be contaminated from an 8-inch pipeline that was leaking. Between 100,000 and {{convert|250,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline were leaked into the local groundwater.<ref name="google109">{{cite book|title=Leak Prevention and Corrective Action Technology for Underground Storage Tanks|author=Gangadharan, A.C.|date=1988|publisher=Noyes Data Corporation|isbn=9780815511632|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Okl1P0IBNfAC|page=250|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 On May 29, a bulldozer ruptured a 1-inch gas service line at a children's nursery in [[Hapeville, Georgia]]. The bulldozer operator was unable to find the shutoff valve for the gas line, and shortly after there was an explosion and fire. Seven children and two adults were killed, and three children were seriously injured in the accident.<ref name="ntsb.gov">{{cite web | url =https://app.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1971/PSS711.pdf | title =REPORT NUMBER NTSB-PSS-71-1 - SPECIAL STUDY OF EFFECTS OF DELAY IN SHUTTING DOWN FAILED PIPELINE SYSTEMS AND METHODS OF PROVIDING RAPID SHUTDOWN - Approved DECEMBER 30, 1970 | last1 = | first1 = | author-link1 = | last2 = | first2 = | author-link2 = | date =1971-02-02 | year = | website = | publisher =[[National Transportation Safety Board]] | access-date =2016-01-18 | subscription = }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/georgia/12237/hapeville-ga-broken-gas-main-explodes-may-1968|title=Hapeville, GA  Broken Gas Main Explodes,  May 1968|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1968 An 8-inch propane pipeline rupture in a landslide ruptured near [[Plainfield, Ohio]] on June 1. 4 different vehicles later drove into the vapor cloud, causing them to stall. One of the vehicle drivers tried to restart their vehicle, igniting the vapor cloud. 2 people were killed, 3 others injured by burns, and 7 buildings and 7 vehicles were destroyed.<ref name="ntsb" /><ref name="ntsb.gov"/><ref name="google110">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=RZNPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=aVIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4398,3315317&dq=little+big+inch+leak&hl=en|title=The Bryan Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 On July 26, a worker was burned by a natural gas fire while working on a [[Sunoco]] gas pipeline in [[Gettysburg, Pennsylvania]].<ref name="google111">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2202&dat=19680727&id=sDkmAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cP4FAAAAIBAJ&pg=3062,2957474|title=Gettysburg Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 A contractor laying a new pipeline broke an old pipeline in [[Norwalk, Ohio]] on August 7, spilling gasoline for 4 hours into the [[Huron River (Ohio)|Huron River]].<ref name="google112">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=tyZPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oQEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3358,6833494&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 On August 22, a 16-inch gasoline pipeline ruptured at [[General Mitchell Field]], spilling almost {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline, and forcing closure of one runway. Previous damage to the pipeline by heavy equipment working in the area was identified as the cause of the rupture.<ref name="google113">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=EG0jAAAAIBAJ&sjid=UigEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4028,2541514&dq=gasoline+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google114">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=sAcqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DCgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4708,3550001&dq=gasoline+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 A coal company digging machine hit an 8-inch LPG pipeline in [[Fulton County, Illinois]] on September 3, killing one person and injuring 4 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/midamericapipeli00netc#page/16/mode/2up|title=Mid-America Pipeline System liquefied petroleum gas pipeline rupture and fire, Donnellson, Iowa, August 4, 1978|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1968 2 teen boys shooting a rifle ignited gasoline leaking from a petroleum pipeline pumping station near [[Midland, Pennsylvania]] on November 3. A large brush fire ensued. Both boys had moderate burns. A stuck relief valve on the pipeline was the cause of the leakge.<ref name="google115">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KURAAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DLMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2495,631166&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google116">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=K0RAAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DLMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4087,890463&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1968 A MAPCO LPG pipeline, near [[Yutan, Nebraska]] ruptured on December 5. Repair crews responded to the pipeline rupture, and thought LPG vapors were dispersed, but ignited the vapor cloud by driving into it. Five repairmen were killed. After the accident, the Nebraska State Fire Marshal ordered MAPCO to reduce its operating pressure, and to hydrostatic retest {{convert|52|mi|km}} of that pipeline. During the tests, 195 longitudinal seams failed.<ref name="ntsb.gov"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/nebraska/16567/yutan-ne-gas-pipeline-explosion-dec-1968|title=Yutan, NE  Gas Pipeline Explosion,  Dec 1968|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1968 On December 18, a 30-inch gas pipeline exploded and burned at a gas processing plant in [[Gibson, Louisiana]]. One plant worker was injured.<ref name="google117">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=5-dHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Hv8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=4249,7176960&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Morning Record - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 On January 3, a gas explosion hit under a [[Manhattan]] borough street in [[New York City, New York]], followed by a number of other gas explosions. 300 families were evacuated, and streets were cracked for 4 blocks. Difficulties of interconnected gas mains caused a 7 delay in shutting down the gas in the area.<ref name="ntsb.gov"/>
* 1969 On January 13, a [[Buckeye Partners]] 22-inch crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Lima, Ohio]], spilling 1,000 to 2,000 barrels of oil on a street and into the sewer system. 8,500 people were evacuated. The crude caught fire, damaging the sewerage treatment plant. Cracks from welding were blamed for the failure.<ref name="ntsb"/><ref name="google118">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=kdBOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=CQIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4267,2126544&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F5071FFE3E59147493C6A8178AD85F4D8685F9 | work=The New York Times | title=10,000 EVACUATED IN OHIO OIL FLOOD; Fuel, Leaking From a Lima Pipeline, Causes Fires | date=January 14, 1969}}</ref>
* 1969 A leaking crude oil pipeline caused a slick {{convert|35|mi|km}} long in the Dry Creek near [[Greybull, Wyoming]] on February 24.<ref name="google119">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=cLZWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fOkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4837,1893118&dq=marathon+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 A 10-inch pipeline carrying aviation gasoline was ruptured by explosives on March 17 in [[Canyon, California]] The fuel caught fire shortly after that.<ref name="google120">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=xekrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tgUGAAAAIBAJ&pg=1385,5869510&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 On April 18, a gas explosion destroyed a home in [[Bowling Green, Kentucky]], killing 2 children. Damage by a contractor to the gas lines and gas mains in the area was suspected as the cause.<ref name="google121">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1696&dat=19700129&id=uu4aAAAAIBAJ&sjid=lUYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7144,3975241|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 On May 6, a gas pipeline in [[Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania]], that had been moved, was undergoing pressure testing when a cap on it blew off, hitting and rupturing another nearby gas pipeline. That pipeline exploded and burned, killing 1 worker, injuring 9 other workers, and damaging 3 homes.<ref name="google122">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=DYNiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cXcNAAAAIBAJ&pg=890,717328&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 The overpressure of a low pressure natural gas distribution system in [[Gary, Indiana]] caused numerous small fires and explosions. A gas company worker's errors allowed much higher than normal gas pressure in a gas distribution system. 56 square blocks were evacuated, 7 people were injured, 6 homes destroyed, and 19 other homes damaged. Later, The National Transportation Safety Board called for upgraded gas pipeline safety standards.(June 3, 1969)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR1969.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report 1969 (not numbered)|publisher=}}</ref><ref name="google123">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=4XssAAAAIBAJ&sjid=2cwEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5745,783969&dq=gary+gas+explosion&hl=en|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9E0CE3DD153AEF31A2575BC1A9649C946190D6CF | work=The New York Times | title=Gas Pipeline Safety Called Inadequate | date=February 18, 1970}}</ref>
* 1969 On September 9, a converted natural gas pipeline running at 789 psi near [[Houston, Texas]] ruptured, causing a massive fire. Construction work downstream of the accident led to a pressure build up that caused the rupture. 7 people were injured, 13 homes were destroyed, and 11 other homes damaged. Some of the homes were within 25 feet of the pipeline. The closest valves on this pipeline took 90 minutes to close.<ref name="ntsb.gov"/><ref name="google125">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=T94jAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TygEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7474,4746423&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 On September 23, a bulldozer being used as part of high tension power line construction hit a gas transmission pipeline in [[Proctor, West Virginia]]. The gas exploded and burned, injuring 6 of the electrical line construction crew. Another bulldozer had also hit a gas pipeline in the same area some months before, killing another worker.<ref name="google126">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19690924&id=euhdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=H18NAAAAIBAJ&pg=3775,3161026|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1969 On November 19, telephone company contractors installing an underground cable hit a 10-inch gas pipeline in [[Vandyne, Wisconsin]]. Gas at 750&nbsp;psi escaped, and ignited about 45 minutes later, killing one of the contractors, and injuring 3 others.<ref name="ntsb"/>
* 1969 On December 25, a land leveler ruptured a 22-inch natural gas transmission pipeline in [[Hermiston, Oregon]]. Gas at 600&nbsp;psi sprayed from the pipeline. A warning sign about the existence of the gas pipeline was {{convert|10|ft|m}} away from the rupture site.<ref name="google127">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=dnozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=N-EDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2889,6351586&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
==19701974==

* 1970 On January 11, a home exploded in [[Bowling Green, Kentucky]], killing a man. Contractor damage to a gas line was suspected.<ref name="google121"/>
* 1970 On January 17, workers from [[Buckeye Partners]] ignited a fire to burn off petroleum from a leaking pipeline near [[Warren, Ohio]]. The fire grew out of control for several hours, requiring 100 firefighters to help contain the blaze. One pipeline employee was injured.<ref name="google128">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19700118&id=OylPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tgEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1926,5231114|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 A leak 2 inch natural gas main exploded in [[Houma, Louisiana]] on January 24, killing 2 gas company workers, one firefighter, injuring 28 others, and demolishing half a block of downtown buildings. The workers were attempting to repair the gas line.<ref name="ntsb.gov"/><ref name="google129">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=MexKAAAAIBAJ&sjid=HyMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5066,5057982&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Press-Courier - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google130">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=j55YAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hvgDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5784,3867032&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 On February 5, a jet fuel pipeline leaked, and contaminated 50 to 60 acres of farm and pasture land near [[Lakeland, Florida]]. Some wildlife was killed, and a small fire broke out in the fuel.<ref name="google131">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=rZVPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=SgUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5676,5906974&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Ocala Star-Banner - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google132">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=g_IsAAAAIBAJ&sjid=KGYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6098,2140761&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Sarasota Herald-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 An 8-inch pipeline broke near [[Wauseon, Ohio]] on April 19, spilling Number 2 fuel oil into the [[Maumee River]], and endangering the water supply for several cities for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19700420&id=xyYxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uQEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5162,5777967|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1970 Early on September 2, residents of Jacksonville, Maryland, detected gasoline odors and noticed gasoline in a small creek flowing beneath a nearby road. Because fumes were still present in the late afternoon of September 2, a resident notified [[Colonial Pipeline]] at 6:19&nbsp;p.m. about the situation. About 12 hours later, on the morning of September 3, an explosion and fire occurred in a ditch in which contractor personnel for Colonial were manually digging to further expose the pipeline & catch gasoline trickling from the ground. Five persons were injured, none fatally. The NTSB later pointed out that workers had failed to use a flammable vapor percent detector during the work. The leak point was found 4 days later. The failure resulted in a release of 30,186 gallons (718 barrels) of gasoline and kerosene.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR7102.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-71-02|publisher=}}</ref><ref name="google133">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=FaRRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vhAEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3600,500912&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 On September 7, a pipeline leaked thousands of gallons of gasoline onto farmland near [[Ontario, Oregon]]. Roads were closed in the area until the gasoline was removed.<ref>[https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=oggxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LeEFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5894,1738316&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en ]{{dead link|date=January 2016}}</ref>
* 1970 The [[1970 Propane vapor cloud explosion in Port Hudson]]. On December 9, 1970, a [[Phillips Petroleum Company]] [[propane]] pipeline leaked, in [[Franklin County, Missouri]]. The leak led a to propane cloud explosion, with a force estimated up to 50 tons of [[Trinitrotoluene|TNT]]. The NTSB cited past external and internal corrosion issues, and poor welds on the uncoated pipeline as concerns.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-72-008|title=Safety Recommendation P-72-008|publisher=}}</ref><ref name="google134">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=p2UfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=w9QEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2640,4723914&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 Explosion of a 30-inch 1100&nbsp;psi inlet natural gas pipeline, bringing offshore natural gas into a gas drying plant in southern Louisiana. Two plant personnel were killed. Rupture was at a junction of a 12-inch gas line to the 30-inch main line. (December 1970)
* 1970 A restaurant owner opened a gas line valve in [[New York, New York]], not knowing that part of the gas line was open and unconnected. The gas in the building exploded, killing 15 people, & injuring more than 60 others. (December 11, 1970)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-71-005|title=Safety Recommendation P-71-005|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1970 On December 17, a Mid-Valley pipeline leaked, spilling 250,000 gallons of crude oil onto that companies' land in [[Dayton, Ohio]]. There were no injuries or fire.<ref name="google135">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19701218&id=XvcjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5QEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=705,4309813|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1970 On December 28, a 12-inch pipeline ruptured in [[Jackson, Washington County, Wisconsin|Jackson, Wisconsin]], spilling {{convert|200|oilbbl|m3}} of fuel oil into a wildlife sanctuary.<ref name="google136">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=AIhQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uhEEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6691,892684&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1971 A faulty valve on a 3-inch natural gas pipeline was suspected of causing a gas leak that resulted in 3 separate explosions, including a house explosion in [[Lambertville, New Jersey]] that killed 7 people.
* 1971 On April 17, a road grader hit a gas transmission pipeline in [[Mississippi]], result in fatal burns to the grader operator. Later, it was found the pipeline only gad 5 to 6 inched of soil cover in the area.<ref name="openjurist">{{cite web|url=http://openjurist.org/507/f2d/658/wideman-v-mississippi-valley-gas-company|title=507 F2d 658 Wideman v. Mississippi Valley Gas Company &#124; OpenJurist|publisher=openjurist.org|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1971 On June 5, an ammonia pipeline failed near [[Floral, Arkansas]], releasing 80 tons of ammonia. A 6-year-old boy had to be hospitalized, cattle were killed or blinded, and 10,000 acres of trees had leaf scorching from the ammonia. Delays were made in notifying Arkansas State Department of Pollution Control and Ecology.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=F30D12FE355B137A93C4A9178CD85F458785F9 | work=The New York Times | title=Gas Leak Scars Arkansas Forest; Delay in Reporting Is Studied | date=July 6, 1971}}</ref>
* 1971 2 gas explosions occurred in [[North Richland Hills, Texas]], on October 4. Gas migrated into 2 homes from leaking gas pipes.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-72-034|title=Safety Recommendation P-72-034|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1971 A gas company repair crew was overcome in a service vault on November 17, in [[Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania]]. 2 workmen were overcome initially, and 4 others attempting to rescue them were also overcome by gas asphyxiation. All 6 died.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-72-025|title=Safety Recommendation P-72-025|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1972 On January 7, a huge explosion and fire occurred on a 24-inch gas transmission pipeline west of [[Centerville, Iowa]]. The fire was visible for far around. There were no injuries or major property damage.<ref name="google137">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=XopiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rncNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6503,849199&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1972 The second pipeline leak in a month into the [[Tippecanoe River]] in [[Indiana]] on a Buckeye Pipeline company (now [[Buckeye Partners]] ) line hit on January 12. The Buckeye Pipeline was owned by the bankrupt [[Penn Central Railroad]], preventing money from being spent on repairs. One EPA official stated "they know they have a leaky system".<ref name="google138">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=P2JjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Om0NAAAAIBAJ&pg=1522,2133488&dq=buckeye+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Rochester Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

* 1972 On June 15, a crew was welding on a gas main in [[Bryan, Ohio]] that had been shut off, when someone inadvertently opened a valve that fed gas into that main. The gas ignited, and exploded, serious injuring 2 workers.<ref name="google146">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nJZPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=RFIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4233,1138092&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Bryan Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1972 A 12-inch diameter high pressure propane pipeline, near [[Butler, Alabama]], was ruptured by a road grader. A short time after the line was ruptured, a car drove into the vapor cloud. The car stalled, and trying to restart it was suspected to have ignited the vapor cloud, killing four people. (June 20, 1972)<ref name="phmsa.dot.gov"/><ref name="google147">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=CQ8fAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JpwEAAAAIBAJ&pg=7034,2937516&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/alabama/12986/butler-al-gas-line-explosion-june-1972|title=Butler, AL  Gas Line Explosion,  June 1972|publisher=}}</ref>

Later, it was discovered that the pipeline company had increased pressure on the pipeline before the rupture to make up for an earlier pipeline shut down.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.flickr.com/photos/pingnews/451584343/|title=Public Domain: Documerica: Texas-New Mexico Pipeline Burst, 1972 by David C. * 1973 On January 10, an abandoned farm near [[Bellingham, Washington]] was coated in crude oil when a Trans-Mountain 16 inch pipeline failed. * 1973 A cracked gas main leaked in [[Adamsville, Alabama]], on February 7. The escaping gas exploded, killing 3 people and injuring 2 others. A string of other gas main cracking incidents occurred in this city, killing one other person, and injuring t2 others.<ref name="ntsb9">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1973/P73_1.pdf|date=18 October 2004|title=P73_1|author=National Transportation Safety Board Safety Recommendation Document|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>

* 1973 On February 22, in [[Austin, Texas]], a 19-inch natural gas liquids (NGL) pipeline ruptured, due to an improper weld. A passing truck appeared to set off a vapor cloud explosion and fire. * 1973 On May 2, a Yellowstone Pipeline 10-inch line ruptured in [[Murray, Idaho]], causing a mist of diesel fuel to cover homes and trailers. About 170,000 gallons of fuel were spilled. Some of the fuel reached a nearby creek. * 1973 In the summer, a pipeline ruptured in [[Diamond, Louisiana]]. * 1973 On November 13, a [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline leaked, spilling gasoline into [[Marion Township, Berks County, Pennsylvania]] creek.<ref name="google168">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1955&dat=19731114&id=SpghAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NJoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3123,2913445|title=Reading Eagle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1973 On December 4, a pipeline break releases {{convert|31000|oilbbl|m3}} of oil near [[Argyle, Minnesota]]. The cause was a failure in a longitudinal weld.<ref name="businessnorth.com">{{cite web | url =http://www.businessnorth.com/exclusives.asp?RID=3219 | title =BusinessNorth Exclusives - Alberta-Superior pipeline takes center stage in world climate debate | last1 =Thomas | first1 =Richard | author-link1 = | last2 = | first2 = | author-link2 = | date =2009-10-27 | year = | website = BusinessNorth.com | publisher =BusinessNorth | archive-url =https://web.archive.org/web/20141102001542/http://www.businessnorth.com/exclusives.asp?RID=3219 | archive-date =2014-11-02 | access-date =2016-01-18 | subscription = }}</ref>
* 1973 On December 6, a pump station on an ammonia pipeline near [[Conway, Kansas]], was started against a closed valve, and the pipeline failed in a previously damaged section. Two persons who drove through the ammonia vapors were hospitalized; several rural residents were evacuated from the area; and {{convert|89,796|USgal|L}} of anhydrous ammonia were lost.<ref>{{cite web | url =http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P74_50_58.pdf | title =Safety Recommendation P-74-050-58 | last1 = | first1 = | author-link1 = | last2 = | first2 = | author-link2 = | date =1974-11-11 | year = | website = | publisher =[[National Transportation Safety Board]] | access-date =2016-01-18 | subscription = }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-74-050|title=Safety Recommendation P-74-050|publisher=National Transportation Safety Board|date=1985-08-19}}</ref>
* 1974 A 22-inch natural gas transmission pipeline failed in [[Prairie du Rocher, Illinois]] on January 2. The resulting fire caused no serious damage, but 7,000 people in the area were left without gas heating for several subfreezing days.<ref name="google169">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=EbQsAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ywkEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2492,457896&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Star-News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 On January 25, a pipeline failed near [[Liberty, Texas]], spilling about 200 barrels of oil into the [[Trinity River (Texas)|Trinity River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1891&dat=19740125&id=ubsfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ttcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3907,3733836|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1974 On March 2, a 30-inch gas pipeline failed at 797 pounds pressure inside a 34-inch casing pipe under a road near [[Monroe, Louisiana]]. 10 acres of forest were burned, but there were no injuries or deaths. A substandard girth weld was the cause. The failure of automatic valves on the pipeline to close upon a pressure drop were also cited in contributing to the size of the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P75_1_4.pdf |format=PDF |title=Probable Cause |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1974 A gas transmission pipeline ruptured near [[Farmington, New Mexico]] on March 15, killing a family of 3 in a truck driving nearby when the gas ignited. Corrosion along the longitudinal seem weld of the pipe section caused the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_2.pdf |format=PDF |title=Safety Recommendations |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1974 A gas line in a commercial building in [[New York, New York]], was ruptured by falling equipment in a basement on April 22. The escaping gas later exploded, injuring more than 70 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_9A_11.pdf |format=PDF |title=Safety Recommendations |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1974 A previously damaged gas main ruptured in [[Philadelphia, Pennsylvania]] on May 3, causing an explosion that killed 2, and caused extensive damage to 4 row homes. Earlier plumbing work was suspect to have caused the gas line damage.<ref name="google170">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=IMotAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cpoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4111,2543650&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Reading Eagle - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 On May 21, a 6-inch gas-gathering pipeline, ruptured at the edge of a rural road south of [[Meridian, Mississippi]]. Three vehicles entered the area which contained the escaping gas, and stalled near the rupture. The gas ignited at 10:05&nbsp;p.m., and five persons died as a result. The 3 vehicles were destroyed and {{convert|40|acre|m2}} of woodland were burned. Although less than 4 years old, the 6-inch pipe had corroded internally and had been embrittled by hydrogen.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_5.pdf|title=P76_5<!-- Bot generated title -->|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1974 A 30-inch [[Transcontinental Pipeline]] gas transmission pipeline failed and gas ignited near [[Bealeton, Virginia]], on June 9, from hydrogen stress cracking. Failure alarms at the nearest upstream gas compressor station did not activate, and the pipeline failure was first noticed by a compressor station employee happening to see the large fire from the pipeline rupture.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P75_7_11.pdf|title=P75_7_11<!-- Bot generated title -->|publisher=}}</ref><ref name="google171">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=9_VNAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DosDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1996,2624507&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 In July, A Lakehead 34 inch pipeline burst near [[Bemidji, Minnesota]], spilling between 125,000 and 210,000 gallons of crude oil.<ref name="google172">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19740715&id=zVoaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=6SgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4245,2494258|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 On August 13, an ammonia pipeline failed near [[Hutchinson, Kansas]] after a pump station was started against a closed valve. 3 police officers were treated for ammonia inhalation; approximately 200 persons were evacuated from the area of the vapors; trees, lawns, shrubbery, and crops were chemically burned; and an estimated 11,000 fish were killed. It was found that this pipeline had exceeded the maximum operating pressure before failure.<ref name="ntsb18">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1974/P74_28.pdf|date=18 October 2004|title=P74_28|author=National Transportation Safety Board Safety Recommendation Document|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 September 3, a contractor working to install curb and gutter in the community of [[Dale (CDP), Wisconsin|Dale, Wisconsin]] pulled a gas line apart underneath the town's bank. Gas seeped into the bank's basement and exploded, destroying the bank and the neighboring post office. A bank manager preparing to open the bank for the afternoon was killed, and another resident was seriously injured.<ref name=":0">{{Cite book|title=The History of Dale (Poker Flat) and Medina (Young's Corner) Wisconsin|last=Zehner|first=David J.|publisher=Jon Habermann|year=1989|isbn=|location=Neenah, Wisconsin|pages=|asin=B00072ETMG}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.newspapers.com/image/84916188/|title=4 Sep 1974, Page 28 - The La Crosse Tribune at Newspapers.com|website=Newspapers.com|access-date=2016-05-20}}</ref>
* 1974 On September 14, a propane pipeline to an underground storage cavern failed in [[Griffith, Indiana]]. The propane later caught fire. 1,000 residents were evacuated during the incident.<ref name="google173">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=84JHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cnwMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2745,1744478&dq=propane+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 A 12-inch gas gathering pipeline exploded and burned near [[Meta, Kentucky]] on November 24. There were no injuries reported. Acts of previous vandalism against the pipeline company had happened before.<ref name="google174">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=O9seAAAAIBAJ&sjid=t0YEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4400,4031817&dq=gasline+blast&hl=en|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google175">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=-xJGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ENEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4261,2574835&dq=gathering+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Portsmouth Times - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
* 1974 A crew repairing a leaking crude oil pipeline near [[Abilene, Texas]], were overcome by sour crude oil fumes on December 1. Six of the repair crew died. The leak was cause by improper welding.<ref name="ntsb19">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1976/P76_30_35.pdf|date=18 October 2004|title=P76_30_35|author=National Transportation Safety Board Safety Recommendation Document |accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="google176">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iWdHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=gnwMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4557,14305&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|publisher=news.google.com|accessdate=18 October 2014}}</ref>
== 19751979 ==
* 1975 A Mid-Valley Pipeline crude oil pipeline at [[Lima, Ohio]], ruptured after a valve was accidentally closed against a pumping pipeline, on January 17. The spraying crude oil ignited, killing a Terminal Operator.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_16.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=June 22, 1976 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1975 On January 23, a propane chiller at a MAPCO facility exploded violently during maintenance work on it, near [[Iowa City, Iowa]]. 2 workers were killed and 3 others injured by the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=gApRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xcAMAAAAIBAJ&pg=7095,3134271&dq=mapco+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 A gas transmission pipeline exploded and gas burned in [[Mediapolis, Iowa]] on January 27. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9C00E1DF133AE03BBC4051DFB766838E669EDE | work=The New York Times | title=Pipeline Blast in Iowa | date=January 28, 1975}}</ref>
* 1975 In March, a leak was discovered in a 14-inch petroleum products pipeline in [[Mecklenburg County, North Carolina]]. [[Plantation Pipeline]] began efforts to recover the spilled petroleum. From that time through June 1983, approximately 2,022 barrels of spilled petroleum products were recovered from standpipes at the leak site. Remediation efforts stopped in October 1984. Later tests raised questions on the possibility of not all of the spill products were recovered.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lawskills.com/case/ga/id/297/08/index.html |title=Browse Caselaw |publisher=Lawskills.com |date= |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1975 A 12-inch crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Harwood, Missouri]], on March 26. Heavy rain slowed the cleanup.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=LUMrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZtQEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5027,5448845&dq=texaco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Nevada Daily Mail - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 A natural gas liquids (NGL) pipeline ruptured due to previous mechanical damage, at [[Devers, Texas]]. 4 people were killed in a following vapor cloud fire. The pipeline had been damaged when a valve was installed on the pipeline. (May 12, 1975)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_42.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=August 5, 1976 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1975 An explosion in June 1975 at a home in [[East Stroudsburg, Pennsylvania]], was caused by natural gas leaking into the home from an open main in the middle of the street. One person was killed. In 1973, workers hired by the gas company had falsified records showing the main had been closed.<ref name="poconorecord1">{{cite web|url=http://www.poconorecord.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=/20110227/FEATURES/102270335/-1/NEWSMAP|title=1968: Gas line explosion destroys Roseto home|work=poconorecord.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 On June 11, a leaking pipeline for the [[Alyeska Pipeline Service Company]] was found to have spilled about 60,000 gallons of crude oil at a construction camp in [[Alaska]]. That pipeline had been noticed leaking before, but, previous repair efforts had failed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eWZYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=8vcDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3857,3322190&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 An LPG pipeline ruptured near [[Romulus, Michigan]], due to previous mechanical damage to the pipeline, and over pressurization from operator error, caused by closing a valve against a pumping pipeline, at a storage facility. Nine people were injured in the following vapor cloud fire. Flames {{convert|500|ft|m}} high engulfed a {{convert|600|ft|m|adj=on}}-diameter area, destroyed four houses and damaged three others, burned 12 vehicles, and consumed {{convert|2389|oilbbl|m3}} of propane. (August 2, 1975)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-76-058 |title=Safety Recommendation P-76-058 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=V6MhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=mZkFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5210,483573&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Reading Eagle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 An ammonia pipeline ruptured in [[Texas City, Texas]] on September 3. 47 people needed medical treatment for ammonia exposure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19750905&id=qRJZAAAAIBAJ&sjid=VUYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=7046,685830|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1975 On September 7, a gas gathering pipeline failed due to internal and external corrosion near [[Kilgore, Texas]]. Unodorized natural gas liquids from leak were ignited by an automobile, killing 5 people.<ref name="ReferenceC">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB-78-01.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Reports - Brief Format : Issue 1 |date=1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1975 On September 19, flooding along the [[Amite River]] in [[Louisiana]] caused a 12-inch propane pipeline to break, releasing about 743,000 gallons of propane.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://dms.ntsb.gov/pubdms/search/document.cfm?docID=299977&docketID=44911&mkey=67002 |title=Document 1 Materials Lab Factual Report 07-122 Filing Date May 22, 2008 61 page(s) of Text (PDF) Photos |publisher=Dms.ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1975 On October 13, employees at a gas processing plant at [[Goldsmith, Texas]] heard leak gas, and investigated. Before the leak could be found, a 12-inch pipeline there exploded, killing 3 of the crew, injuring 2 others, and causing extensive plant damage.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>
* 1975 On December 18, a failed pressure relief device caused cracks in storage tanks supporting the [[Trans-Alaskan Pipeline System]], leaking about 600,000 gallons of crude oil in [[Prudhoe Bay, Alaska]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=vdsjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GSkEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6865,4269519&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1976'''
* 1976 On January 7, a repair crew working on natural gas gathering compressor station at [[Cedardale, Oklahoma]], opened the wrong valve in an attempt to increase gas flow. Natural gas & Natural Gas Liquids flow out of an open 12-inch pipeline, and were ignited by an open flame heater. 5 of the crew were killed, and 2 seriously burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-76-026 |title=Safety Recommendation P-76-026 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1976 On January 10, a gas leak at the Pathfinder Hotel in [[Fremont, Nebraska]], exploded, killing 23 people. A compression coupling on a gas line had pulled apart, causing gas to leak into the Hotel's basement.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-76-003 |title=Safety Recommendation P-76-003 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1976 A [[MAPCO]] LPG/NGL pipeline ruptured near [[Whitharral, Texas]], leading to vapor cloud fire that killed one, severely burning 4 others who later died, destroyed two homes, and burned an area about 400 yards wide. A Low Frequency Electric Resistance Weld (LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]]) seam failure is suspected for the failure. From January 1968 to the date of the Whitharral accident, 14 longitudinal pipe seam failures had occurred on that pipeline system, which resulted in 6 other fatalities, and the loss of over {{convert|60000|oilbbl|m3}} of LPG.(February 25, 1976)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_22_25.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=June 14, 1976 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/node/16862 |title=Whitharral, TX Gas Line Explosion, Feb 1976 &#124; GenDisasters ... Genealogy in Tragedy, Disasters, Fires, Floods |publisher=.gendisasters.com |date=1976-02-26 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=5VVOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=3_gDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3071,2499657&dq=mid+america+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1976 An improperly assembled compression coupling failed on a gas distribution line in [[Phoenix, Arizona]] on February 8, causing a house explosion that killed 2 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_17_19.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=May 20, 1976 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1976 On March 2, an 18-inch [[Gulf Oil]] pipeline failure spilled about 21,000 gallons of crude oil into the Wisner Wildlife Area in [[Louisiana]]. There were no initial reports of wildlife being affected.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=19760303&id=MPNLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=de0DAAAAIBAJ&pg=4323,829415|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1976 On March 16, a 6-inch ARCO pipeline failed near [[Tilden Township, Pennsylvania]], spilling gasoline into a stream.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1955&dat=19760317&id=jxFXAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WUMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6838,4112779|title=Reading Eagle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1976 On March 27, a two-story building in [[Phenix City, Alabama]], exploded and burned from a gas leak. The explosion and fire killed the six persons in the building. The NTSB found that gas at 20-psig pressure had leaked from a cracked, 3-inch cast iron gas main.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_67_72.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=October 2, 1976 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1976 A front loader hit a Standard Oil of California (now [[Chevron Corporation]]) 8-inch petroleum products pipeline in [[Los Angeles, California]], during a road widening project along [[Venice Boulevard]]. 9 people were killed, a plastic factory was destroyed, and other serious property damage occurred. (June 16, 1976)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_87_90.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=January 31, 1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=evgLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=t1gDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5557,335390&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Evening Independent - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* On August 8, a house exploded from gas migrating through the soil, from a broken 4 inch gas main, in [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]]. 26 minutes later, gas then exploded in another house, causing a brick wall & part of the street to collapse. 2 firefighters were killed, 14 people injured, and 4 buildings destroyed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/Investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR7702.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-77-02 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1976 A road grader hit a 20-inch gas transmission pipeline near [[Calhoun, Louisiana]]. Six people were killed in the ensuing fire, 6 families were left homeless, and a mobile home and 2 houses were destroyed. (August 9, 1976)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-76-074 |title=Safety Recommendation P-76-074 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=OiRXAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hkMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5762,3395836&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The News-Dispatch - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1976 On August 13, a flash fire in the basement of a house in [[Bangor, Maine]], occurred while a gas company crew was checking for the cause of low gas pressure at the home. The fire killed one gas company employee, burned two other employees, and caused minor damage to the house. One of the crew was using a match to light the basement of the home, and another crew member was smoking when the fire started.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P76_101.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=January 17, 1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1976 On August 29, an explosion and fire destroyed a house at [[Kenosha, Wisconsin]]. Two persons were killed, four persons were injured, and two adjacent houses were damaged. The destroyed house was not served by natural gas. However, natural gas, which was escaping at 58 psig pressure from a punctured 2-inch plastic main located {{convert|39|ft|m}} away, had entered the house through a 6-inch sewer lateral that had been bored through to install the gas line.<ref name="ReferenceC"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-76-083 |title=Safety Recommendation P-76-083 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1976 On September 10, sewer work and heavy equipment caused soil subsidence on a 6-inch cast iron gas pipe in [[Blue Island, Illinois]], resulting in the pipe breaking in 4 places. Gas then migrated into a building, that later exploded, killing 1 person, and, injuring 10 others.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>
* 1976 On November 28, an 8-inch [[Sunoco]] pipeline began leaking in [[Toledo, Ohio]], spilling about 1,000 barrels of gasoline, forcing a major road closure. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19761129&id=ZhBPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=agIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5658,2451152|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1976 An explosion and fire at a gas pipeline compressor station in [[Orange Grove, Texas]] killed one plant worker, and injured another on December 6.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=sDwcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xVoEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5022,1626941&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1977'''
* 1977 On January 2, a gas pipeline ruptured and burned near [[Nursery, Texas]]. Some power poles were destroyed, but there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=dyoPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cIUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7032,502206&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 On January 5, in [[Fairview, Bergen County, New Jersey|Fairview, New Jersey]], a circumferential break on a 6-inch cast iron gas pipe. The released gas then migrated under frozen soil & a sidewalk, into an area under the floor of a building. The gas later was ignited by an unknown source, causing an explosion that killed 1 person, injured 13 others, and destroyed 3 buildings.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>
* 1977 In [[Baltimore, Maryland]] on January 13, a 4-inch cast iron gas line suffered a circumferential break. The gas migrated under frozen soil and pavement into nearby rowhouses, and was likely ignited by an oil burned motor. One person was killed.<ref name="ReferenceC"/> 
* 1977 On January 18, an 18-inch steel gas main failed and leaked into an electrical and telephone conduit in [[New Bedford, Massachusetts]]. Three explosion followed, destroying 5 buildings, and breaking windows nearby. Improper pipeline construction techniques were the cause of the failure. There were no injuries.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>    
* 1977 A gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Stockton, California]] on February 4. Another gas pipeline fire had occurred nearby 4 days earlier. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120719085747/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=LEchAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dn8FAAAAIBAJ&pg=6084,1926128&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Gas line blasts interrupts services|website=Archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1977 On May 20, fire broke out at a [[MAPCO]] pipeline pumping stations and Terminal in [[Ogden, Iowa]], threatening 4 propane storage tanks for a time. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2457&dat=19770520&id=7g00AAAAIBAJ&sjid=qCMIAAAAIBAJ&pg=3568,2515323|title=Bangor Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 In June, a [[Williams Partners]] pipeline terminal near [[Lawrence, Kansas]] spilled about 33,600 gallons of gasoline. the next spring, a rancher nearby was still having gasoline entering a creek on his property.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19780404&id=aEMyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=beYFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3582,476614|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 An explosion on July 8 at [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] Pump Station No. 8 kills one worker, injures 5 others, and destroys the pump station. Over $2 million in damage was done. A US House of Representatives Committee later announced the cause was workers not following the proper procedures, causing crude oil to flow into a pump under repair at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=hWQsAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Fs0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=7084,3305419&dq=pipeline-explosion&hl=en|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="AAAAIBAJ 1576">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=l-5cAAAAIBAJ&sjid=0VkNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1576,2892833&dq=killed+when+he+struck+a+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Morning Record and Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P77_37.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=December 13, 1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=JA8gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dGUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4372,1221708&dq=pipeline-fire&hl=en|title=The Lewiston Daily Sun - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 On July 19, the [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] pipeline was shut down for the 4th time in a month, when it was hit in a valve by a front loader. More than {{convert|40,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil was spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=0i4PAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WYUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5538,3708177&dq=gas+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 A 12-inch propane pipeline ruptured near Ruff Creek, in [[Greene County, Pennsylvania]], from [[stress corrosion cracking]], on July 20. The resulting propane vapor cloud ignited, when a truck that was driven into the cloud stalled, then created a spark, when it was restarted. The two men in the truck were killed, as well as 57 head of cattle, along with destruction of power lines and wooded areas. Subsidence of underground coal mines in the area may have hastened the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR7801.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board : Pipeline Accident Report |date=July 20, 1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19770721&id=DOZdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Gl8NAAAAIBAJ&pg=4234,2766736|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 A cast iron gas main broke in [[Cherokee, Alabama]] on July 30. Gas migrated into a home through a recently back filled sewer line trench, and exploded 5 days later.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB-78-01.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Reports - Brief Format : Issue Number 1 - 1977 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1977 In August, a car drove through leaking liquid from a petroleum pipeline in [[Lakewood, California]]. The pooled liquid appeared to be mud, but it exploded and burned, injuring a woman in the car.<ref name="news.google.com">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=oiRLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=riMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4950,3987383&dq=shell+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Press-Courier - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 On August 9, natural gas under 20 psi pressure entered a 6-ounce per square inch gas distribution system in [[El Paso, Texas]], over pressuring 750 gas customer customers. Numerous small fires resulted from this. The cause was an error during gas pipeline replacement.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>
* 1977 On August 15, crude oil spilled at [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] Pump Station No. 9. There was no fire, but a fire or explosion at that station could have shut down that pipeline, since Pump Station No. 8 was out of service from the previous month's accident there. This was the seventh accident on this pipeline since the start up of the Alaska pipeline on June 20, 1977. The NTSB released three recommendations on September 9, 1977, to correct certain design and operating deficiencies in the pump rooms of each station of the Alyeska system.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/Investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR7802.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-78-02|work=ntsb.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120717040558/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=biweAAAAIBAJ&sjid=a74EAAAAIBAJ&pg=1995,2906758&dq=pipeline-fire&hl=en|title=Report faults pipeline|website=archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1977 A gas transmission pipeline exploded, forcing hundreds to evacuate in [[Columbus, Indiana]] on August 26. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive/pdf?res=9E06E6DF143AE63BBC4F51DFBE66838C669EDE | work=The New York Times | title=Gas Pipeline in Indiana Town Explodes; Hundreds Evacuated | date=August 27, 1977}}</ref>
* 1977 On September 5, 2 brothers in a moving truck drove into a vapor cloud from a leak at a gas compressor plant in [[New Cuyama, California]], igniting the cloud. One was killed immediately, and the other died 11 days later.<ref name="news.google.com"/>
* 1977 On September 10, a pipeline rupture spilled {{convert|69,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline into a creek in [[Toledo, Ohio]]. Corrosion of the pipeline caused the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=9gpPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=YAIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2233,2092915&dq=buckeye+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=_ApPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=YAIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5482,3704327&dq=buckeye+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 A gas line inside a building in [[San Francisco, California]] leaked and exploded, injuring 7 and heavily damaging that building. Gas repair crews were working on the line at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=NcRiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hHgNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5093,1889408&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=St. Joseph Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 On October 12, a bulldozer ruptured a propane pipeline near [[Albany, Georgia]], causing nearby train traffic to be halted. The bulldozer engine was left running, nearly igniting the vapors.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=g2tEAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fLIMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1533,2408463&dq=dixie+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Albany Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 On October 30, a bulldozer hit a gas pipeline in [[Shreveport, Louisiana]]. The gas ignited, causing a 100 foot tall flame, injuring 4 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19771031&id=1N8jAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dSkEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3334,7045130|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>  
* 1977 A backhoe being used to install a pipeline hit an adjacent 6-inch propane pipeline on November 21 in [[Hutchinson, Kansas]]. Fire broke out, but there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=HmdAAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uFYMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4762,4003237&dq=propane+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Daily Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 Construction workers punctured a 12-inch gas pipeline in [[Atlanta, Georgia]], with an I-beam on December 1. No fire or explosion followed, but thousands of people were evacuated from nearby buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR7803.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-78-03|work=ntsb.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1977 A compression coupling joint between a plastic and a steel gas line pulled apart in [[Lawrence, Kansas]] on December 15. The gas migrated into 2 buildings, and exploded, killing 2 people, and injuring 3 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/Investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR7804.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-78-04|work=ntsb.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=MboxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QeYFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6888,2848607&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1978'''
* 1978 Earth movement was suspected in causing a gas transmission pipeline to rupture and burn near [[Stevenson, Washington]] on January 23. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=V_xPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wwgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4798,1118815&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 On February 15, a gas pipeline being tested with compressed air exploded at a seam on the pipe in [[Cincinnati, Ohio]] on February 15, injuring 8.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=6_pLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BfkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6824,64269&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 A portion of the [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] pipeline east of [[Fairbanks, Alaska]] was ruptured by an explosive device on February 15. Crude oil spilled in a {{convert|600|ft|m|adj=on}} diameter spot.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=dhNJAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QYMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1891,14355&dq=marathon+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 On February 26, a 16-inch Cities Service Gas pipeline ruptured near [[Lecompton, Kansas]], causing natural gas shortages in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19780227&id=Zk4yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZuYFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3344,3505779|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 An improperly plugged gas line leaked into service vault in [[Oklahoma City, Oklahoma]] at a shopping center, overcoming 5 gas company workers on March 29. Four of the repairmen died of asphyxiation. None of the repair crew had respirators at the job site.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-78-053|title=Safety Recommendation P-78-053|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1978 A gas company crew in [[Mansfield, Ohio]] accidentally tied a high pressure gas main into a low pressure gas main on May 17. Much higher gas flames in gas appliances caused damage in 16 homes, and about 2,000 gas meters were shut off during the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-78-045|title=Safety Recommendation P-78-045|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1978 On June 12, a 10-inch gas pipeline was hit by a construction crew, in [[Kansas City, Missouri]]. Almost 2 hour later, escaping gas ignited, causing burns to 2 men from a crew trying to fix the pipeline leak.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR7805.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1978 A MAPCO LPG pipeline in [[Donnellson, Iowa]] ruptured from past mechanical damage and improper lowering for road improvements. The vapor cloud ignited several minutes after the rupture. Three people were killed and 2 others severely burned. The pipe failed at a dented and gouged area not seen during the original construction, or lowering for road work a few months before. A hydrostatic test on this pipeline after the accident caused failures at 2 other dented & gouged section, and 15 [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failures in 117 miles. (August 4, 1978)<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/details/midamericapipeli00netc|title=Mid-America Pipeline System liquefied petroleum gas pipeline rupture and fire, Donnellson, Iowa, August 4, 1978|publisher=|via=Internet Archive}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/texas/16844/fort-madison-ia-propane-pipeline-explodes-aug-1978|title=Fort Madison, IA  Propane Pipeline Explodes, Aug 1978|work=gendisasters.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/details/midamericapipeli00netc|title=Mid-America Pipeline System liquefied petroleum gas pipeline rupture and fire, Donnellson, Iowa, August 4, 1978|work=Internet Archive|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 On August 7, in [[Lafayette, Louisiana]], natural gas at 15 psig pressure escaped from a corrosion leak in an inactive 1-inch steel service line and migrated beneath a concrete slab and into a building where it ignited. The resulting explosion and fire injured six persons and destroyed the building and its contents.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-074|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-074|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1978 On August 14, a coal digging crew in [[Cairo, Missouri]] hit a MAPCO LPG pipeline with a backhoe. The gas ignited about 2 hours later, as digging crews were still working nearby. 1 worker was burned, along with the backhoe, a bulldozer, and a diesel fuel tank.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1893&dat=19780815&id=xPIhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=jNUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5806,5502186|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 On August 28, natural gas, which had escaped from a circumferential fracture in a socket heat-fusion coupling on a 2-in. polyethylene (PE) main, operating at 40-psig pressure, migrated beneath a one-story house in [[Grand Island, Nebraska]], exploded, and then burned. One person was injured; the house was destroyed; and three adjacent houses were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-012|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-012|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1978 About {{convert|7,600|USgal|L}} of gasoline were spilled in [[Hampton, Pennsylvania]] on August 30. Workers boring for a sewer line had hit a fuel pipeline. Later, the 2 construction firms responsible were fined only $500 each.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=n4BIAAAAIBAJ&sjid=O20DAAAAIBAJ&pg=6977,4457534&dq=buckeye+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=IFodAAAAIBAJ&sjid=A1kEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6832,2705698&dq=buckeye+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 A pipeline feeding a [[Strategic Petroleum Reserve (United States)|Strategic Petroleum Reserve]] storage cavern ruptured in [[Hackberry, Louisiana]] on September 22, causing a large fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=EQ5SAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QjUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5019,5142959&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1978 A 30-inch United Texas Transmission gas pipeline in [[Brookside Village, Texas]] ruptured and exploded, killing five people, and injuring 43 others. Seven mobile homes were also destroyed. The blast was felt 35 miles away. (October 24, 1978)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/texas/16885/brookside-village-tx-gas-pipeline-explosion-oct-1978|title=Brookside Village, TX  Gas Pipeline Explosion,  Oct 1978|work=gendisasters.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1876&dat=19781025&id=PFYsAAAAIBAJ&sjid=q80EAAAAIBAJ&pg=6938,6203711|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 On October 30, a pickup truck with 2 women inside drove into an unseen gas cloud from a leaking gas gathering pipeline in [[Preston, Oklahoma]], triggering explosions and a fire, killing the 2 women. 3 homes were also damaged. Flames from the fire reached 200 feet high.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=105DAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ga0MAAAAIBAJ&pg=4420,4522772&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Frederick Daily Leader - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1978 An [[Amoco]] crude oil pipeline leaked into the Farmington Bay Waterfowl Management Area west of [[Farmington, Utah]] on November 7. About 105,000 gallons of crude were spilled. The rupture was caused by pumping against a valve that had been closed for earlier pipeline maintenance.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=U9pSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WoADAAAAIBAJ&pg=5580,2966936&dq=amoco+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=336&dat=19781208&id=XtpSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IIADAAAAIBAJ&pg=7101,2330229|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1979'''
* 1979 A ruptured 2-inch gas line leaking caused a home to explode in [[Spokane, Washington]] on January 6, killing the homeowner.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iIJUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=mY8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=3151,427800&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On January 16, an explosion and fire destroyed five commercial buildings and damaged several other buildings in [[London, Kentucky]]. Two persons were injured. External corrosion was suspected as the cause. A prearranged pressure increase in the pipeline was also a factor.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-79-009|title=Safety Recommendation P-79-009|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/gasservicecoexpl00netc#page/2/mode/2up|title=Gas Service Co. explosion and fire, London, Kentucky, January 16, 1979|work=archive.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On January 18 in Hocking County, Ohio a high pressure pipeline ruptured, killing a line repairman, and a supervisor.  6 other line repairman were also seriously injured.
* 1979 On February 7, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] stubline ruptured in [[Hamilton, Tennessee]], spilling about 152,000 gallons of petroleum product. The cause was from imprper backfill of soil around the pipeline during its construction.<ref>http://pstrust.org/docs/ops_doc2.pdf |format=PDF |title=1996 Colonial Pipeline Task Force |website=Pstrust.org |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On March 2, at Alyeska Pipeline Service Company, Pump Station #6 located near the Yukon River in Alaska, the topping unit producing turbine fuel experienced a flame out of the flare stack which burns flammable tail gas from the unit.  Automatic ignition apparatus did not function due to the extreme low temperature of -25F.  A safety professional on staff was tasked with climbing the stack and re-igniting the flare manually.  Once ignition was established, and before the safety professional could climb down from the top catwalk platform, station management ordered the combustion blower to be turned on and tail gas pressure to be increased from 3psi to 11psi.  The action resulted in a surge through the knock out drum at the base of the stack, causing residual oil and naphtha to be blown up the stack, covering the top catwalk and approximately the top 60 feet of the stack in burning petroleum.  The safety professional was severely burned and fell through the stack main access ladder components and iron work 115 feet to the ground.  The occurrence did not result in a fatality, however, fire damaged the stack and petroleum contaminated the surrounding base area.{{citation needed|date=October 2014}}
* 1979 An 18-inch natural gas transmission pipeline failed underneath the Florida Turnpike in [[West Palm Beach, Florida]], resulting in a 2-hour road closure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=bAtUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qYwDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1730,3097929&dq=pipeline-explosion&hl=en|title=Boca Raton News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On April 18, a 24-inch natural gas transmission pipeline pulled out of a compression coupling, during a line-lowering project under Iowa State Highway 181, in a rural area, near [[Dallas, Iowa]]. Within seconds, the natural gas ignited and burned a {{convert|900|ft|m|adj=on}} by {{convert|400|ft|m|adj=on}} area. Two cars, a pickup truck, and a trailer housing construction equipment were destroyed. A backhoe was damaged and windows were broken in a nearby farmhouse. Five of the eight injured workers were hospitalized. The gas company's accident records indicated that this 24-inch pipeline had experienced 12 previous failures since it was constructed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-79-020|title=Safety Recommendation P-79-020|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On April 20, a series of explosions, and a fire, struck a [[Sunoco]] pipeline terminal in [[Toledo, Ohio]].
