Some nearby residents fled their homes, and telephone service was disrupted.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19790421&id=6zFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LgMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6370,7962054|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19790420&id=6jFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LgMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6227,7790690|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On May 11, 2 explosions, and a following fire, killed 7 people, injured 19 others, and destroyed 3 buildings, in [[Philadelphia, Pennsylvania]]. Soil erosion under an 8-inch cast iron gas main caused the main to break and release gas.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/philadelphiagasw00netc#page/n3/mode/2up|title=Philadelphia Gas Works natural gas pipeline rupture, explosion, and fire, Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, May 11, 1979|work=archive.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On May 13, a 36-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] ruptured, releasing {{convert|336,000|USgal|L}} of fuel oil that damaged vegetation, and killed fish, near [[Spartanburg, South Carolina]]. Cracks made in the railroad shipping of the pipe before installation were the cause.<ref name=autogenerated2>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8102.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On May 19, tank truck drivers waiting at an [[Amoco]] terminal heard a bang, then saw a 3-foot side stream of gasoline pour down a nearby hillside in [[Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania]]. Train traffic on 2 nearby rail lines had to be stopped during the cleanup.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19790520&id=xOxVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5EANAAAAIBAJ&pg=5318,5174808|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 A "spud" dropped by a pile driving barge in the Gulf of Mexico near [[Pilottown, Louisiana]] ruptured a 4-inch natural gas pipeline on June 5. The escaping gas ignited, and seriously burned the barge. 4 crew members went missing and were presumed dead.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=qgRFAAAAIBAJ&sjid=y7oMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4357,2413019&dq=gas+line+blast&hl=en|title=The Windsor Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On June 10, the pilot of a helicopter reported sighting oil on the surface of the Atigun River near the route of the [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]]'s 48-inch crude oil pipeline. Repair crews found a 7-inch crack which passed through a longitudinal weld. Five days after the first leak, at 3:15&nbsp;p.m. on June 15, the pilot of an Alyeska helicopter on a routine surveillance flight reported a leak north of pump station No. 12 near the Little Tonsina River. A crack near a wrinkle in the pipe was found there. The June 10 spill resulted in a release of approximately {{convert|1500|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil; the June 15 leak resulted in a release of approximately {{convert|300|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil; these losses were estimated by Alyeska personnel at the leak site. The spills were too small to be verified by the Alyeska metering system.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-79-019|title=Safety Recommendation P-79-019|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 A crack in a wrinkled section of the [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] pipeline occurred at Pump Station 12 on June 15 on the south end of that pipeline in southern [[Alaska]]. About 1,000 barrels of crude oil were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=w0k0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=k2cEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6750,384243&dq=pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Sarasota Herald-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1338&dat=19790616&id=ZgNMAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JPkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2867,167613|title=Spokane Daily Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On June 16, operator error at [[Colonial Pipeline]] caused a prior to installation rail shipping induced crack of 36-inch pipeline to rupture in [[Greenville County, South Carolina]]. 395,000 gallons of fuel oil were spilled, causing vegetation, fish, & wildlife kills.<ref name=autogenerated2 />
* 1979 A leaking pipeline released gasoline in [[Granger, Indiana]], causing the evacuation of 400 people on July 3.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=lSBSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bDUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2187,281502&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 An anchor handling boat, PETE TIDE II, damaged an unmarked gas pipeline with a grappling hook offshore from [[New Orleans, Louisiana]]. Two of the crew were missing and presumed dead in the fire that followed. (July 15, 1979)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-015|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-015|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On July 25, an explosion and fire destroyed a duplex apartment house in [[Albuquerque, New Mexico]]. Two persons were killed, and two persons were hospitalized for burns; adjacent houses were damaged. Earlier in the day, a crew from Mountain Bell Telephone Company (Mountain Bell) had been using a backhoe at the intersection of Bridge Boulevard and Atrisco Road to locate a telephone cable. The backhoe snagged a gas service line but the fact that it was pulled from a 1-inch coupling under the house was not discovered at that time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-048|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-048|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 A 34-inch Lakehead (now [[Enbridge]]) pipeline ruptured near [[Bemidji, Minnesota]], leaking {{convert|10700|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil on August 20. The pipeline company initially recovered 60 percent of the spilled oil. Later in 1988, the Minnesota Pollution Control Agency required Lakehead to extract more oil using new technology; removal continued on, with studies still underway in the area.<ref name="businessnorth.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.businessnorth.com/exclusives.asp?RID=3219 |title=Alberta-Superior pipeline takes center stage in world climate debate|accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141102001542/http://www.businessnorth.com/exclusives.asp?RID=3219 |archivedate=November 2, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=JTFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=jAIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6657,2195838&dq=lakehead+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://mn.water.usgs.gov/projects/bemidji/|title=USGS Minnesota Water Science Center|work=usgs.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://mn.water.usgs.gov/projects/bemidji/results/fact-sheet.pdf |format=PDF |title=Ground Water Contamination by Crude Oil near Bemidji, Minnesota |website=Mn.water.usgs.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1979 On August 20, a bulldozer operating near [[Orange, Texas]], was being used to clean a farm drainage ditch. The corner of the blade cut into a propane line, which crossed beneath the ditch. Propane at 350 psig escaped and was ignited within seconds. The resulting fire killed one person, injured another, and caused considerable property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-001|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-001|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QKUyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bucFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5281,5217961&dq=gas+explosion&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 A crude oil pipeline ruptured and spilled oil into a creek new [[Walnut Grove, Missouri]] on August 25. {{convert|2|mi|km}} of the creek were contaminated, and 32,000 fish killed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VOMpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MdYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5714,4966726&dq=shell+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 On September 4, the M/V WHITEFACE struck a high-pressure gas pipeline on Lake Verret, near [[Pierre Part, Louisiana]]. A resulting explosion killed a crewman aboard the vessel.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19790905&id=7uNhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cncNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2832,418249&hl=en|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|website=news.google.com}}</ref>
* 1979 On October 6, an explosion caused by liquefied natural gas (LNG) vapors destroyed a transformer building at the reception facility of the Columbia LNG Corporation, [[Cove Point, Maryland]]. Odorless liquefied natural gas leaked through an inadequately tightened LNG pump seal, vaporized, passed through approximately {{convert|210|ft|m}} of underground electrical conduit and entered the substation building. One person was killed, and one person was seriously injured. Damage to the facility was estimated at about $3 million. The fire hydrants and deluge water spray system were inoperable after the explosion because the water main that supplied the system was broken at a flange above ground inside the substation.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-031|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-031|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On October 24, an explosion and fire destroyed the county clerk's office building and the adjoining courthouse building, gutted a connecting building which was under construction, and damaged the adjacent houses in [[Stanardsville, Virginia]]. Thirteen persons were injured and property was damaged extensively. The following NTSB investigation revealed that natural gas had leaked from a break in a 1&nbsp;1/4-inch coated steel service line, which had been snagged by a backhoe which was being used to dig a footing for an addition to the county clerk's office building.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-010|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-010|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 On October 30, a natural gas explosion and fire demolished a townhouse in [[Washington, D.C.]], and damaged nearby buildings and cars. No one was inside the townhouse at the time, but three persons in a stopped car were injured when debris from the explosion shattered a car window. After the accident, an inspection of the gas service line that served the townhouse revealed that it had been struck by excavating equipment.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-059|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-059|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1979 A natural gas transmission pipeline exploded in [[West Monroe, Louisiana]] on November 11, causing 3 subdivisions to be evacuated, and creating a crater 70 feet wide and 20 feet deep. There were no injuries. A gas pipeline explosion had taken place nearby 8 years before.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=rzBPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=kQIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5519,8471103&dq=gasline+blast&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19791113&id=29ROAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IUoDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1546,6774110|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1979 A 12-inch [[Amoco]] pipeline broke on December 11 near [[Waverly, Missouri]], spilling about 8,400 gallons of crude oil. Temperature changes were blamed for the joint failure on the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1893&dat=19791214&id=1s0fAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vNgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3245,6242086|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1979 On December 16, military police at [[Marine Corps Base Quantico]] discovered fuel oil leaking into the [[Potomac River]], near [[Chopawamsic Island]]. A leaking [[Plantation Pipeline]] 12 inch pipeline was the source, spilling between 5,000 and 10,000 gallons of fuel oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1298&dat=19791217&id=gf9NAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5IsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3413,2686047|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
==1980s==

* 1980 On January 2, crude oil leaked from a fractured 22-inch pipeline, at a levee crossing, in [[Berwick, Louisiana]]. At 9:54&nbsp;a.m., the crude oil ignited. One person was killed, one person was injured, and six homes were either destroyed, or, damaged. The pipeline's monitoring system failed to detect a loss of over {{convert|1800|oilbbl|m3}} of oil. A defective sleeve weld cause the pipeline to fail.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-068|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-068|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1980 On January 30, an 8-inch refined petroleum products pipeline, owned by The Pipelines of Puerto Rico, Inc., was struck and ruptured by a bulldozer, during maintenance work on a nearby waterline, in the Sector Cana of [[Bayamon, Puerto Rico]], about {{convert|10|mi|km}} southwest of San Juan. Gasoline from the rupture sprayed downhill, and ran off into a small creek. About 1 1/2 hours later, the gasoline vapors were ignited by an undetermined source and exploded; the subsequent fire killed one person and extensively damaged 25 houses and other property.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-075|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-075|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1980 On February 21, an explosion and fire destroyed four stores in a shopping complex and severely damaged an adjoining restaurant in [[Cordele, Georgia]]. Of the eight persons who were injured, three died later as a result of their injuries. Property damage was extensive. The NTSB investigation of the accident has revealed that natural gas leaked from a 1-inch steel service line, which had been pulled from a 1-inch compression coupling from a backhoe working in the area, and migrated under a concrete slab floor and into a jewelry store where it was ignited by an unknown source.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-80-039|title=Safety Recommendation P-80-039|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1980 A [[Colonial Pipeline]] Dispatcher ignored established procedures for dealing with a pressure surge, causing a double rupture of a 32-inch steel petroleum products pipeline on March 6. One break, where the pipe had been thinned by corrosion in a casing under a road, caused the release of {{convert|8000|oilbbl|m3}} of aviation-grade kerosene adjacent to route 234 near [[Manassas, Virginia]]. Before being fully contained, the kerosene had flowed into Bull Run River, and had entered the Occoquan Reservoir, a source of drinking water for several northern Virginia communities. The other break, where a crack in the pipe wall initiated during rail shipment of the pipe from the steel mill finally propagated to failure, caused the release of {{convert|2190|oilbbl|m3}} of No. 2 fuel oil near Locust Grove, a rural area in Orange County, near [[Fredericksburg, Virginia]]. Before being fully contained, the fuel oil had flowed into the Rapidan River and then into the Rappahannock River, a source of drinking water for the City of Fredericksburg.<ref name=autogenerated2 /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=tOBLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=nYsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5083,1046089&dq=colonial+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 Sabotage during a labor strike was suspected in a gasoline pipeline explosion in [[Marcus Hook, Pennsylvania]] on March 7. The following fire burned for about 17 hours.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iLhMAAAAIBAJ&sjid=1foDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3641,2952318&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=hBVJAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bYMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3175,3677805&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Youngstown Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On April 16, gasoline at a [[Williams Companies]] pipeline terminal in [[Roseville, Minnesota]], sprayed from the fractured cast-iron base of a station booster pump at 72 psig pressure, vaporized, and exploded after it was ignited by the spark of an electric switch in the mainline pump control room {{convert|50|ft|m}} downwind of the booster pump. One man was killed, 3 others injured, and extensive damage was done to the terminal. About {{convert|3500|oilbbl|m3}} of petroleum products burned and property damage was estimated at $3 million.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-81-017|title=Safety Recommendation P-81-017|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ZxMiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NXUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3766,3075577&dq=pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Day - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On May 27, near [[Cartwright, Louisiana]], an anhydrous ammonia pipeline was struck by a bulldozer, which was being used to prepare a well site, and the pipeline ruptured. Over 100 people were evacuated from the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-82-018|title=Safety Recommendation P-82-018|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1980 On July 23, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] 30 inch line burst in [[Clay City, Kentucky]], spraying dirt and rocks in the area, damaging 2 homes. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1696&dat=19800724&id=INIdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BEcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5346,3341488|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 A road grader ruptured an NGL pipeline in [[Aurora, Colorado]] on August 11. Firefighters had barely evacuated residents in the area when the vapors exploded, burning one firefighter.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=T6kuAAAAIBAJ&sjid=99kFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4354,2261014&dq=phillips+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On September 3, a Mid-Valley Pipeline Co. line was ruptured by pipeline work, in [[Cygnet, Ohio]]. Efforts to contain the crude were unable to prevent some of it from entering the [[Portage River (Ohio)|Portage River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19800909&id=2BJPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=lQIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6324,1775461|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 An oil pipeline ruptured and burned while it was being repaired at an oil storage Terminal in [[Piney Point, Maryland]] on September 12, 1980. One worker was killed, and 5 others injured in the fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=jqIfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=8tUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6395,2080896&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On October 9, a 2-inch compression coupling located on the upstream side of a gas meter set assembly in the boiler room of the Simon Kenton High School in [[Independence, Kentucky]], pulled out of its connection with a 2-inch gas service line. Natural gas at 165-psig pressure escaped through the 2-inch opening and, seconds later, exploded and burned. A basement wall was blown down, an adjacent classroom was damaged, and one student was killed. About 30&nbsp;minutes later, a second explosion occurred, which injured 37 persons and extensively damaged the school. The gas main was being uprated at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-81-001|title=Safety Recommendation P-81-001|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1980 A bulldozer digging a ditch for a new pipeline hit a 16-inch crude oil pipeline near [[San Ysidro, New Mexico]] on October 22. The operator was fatally burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=LqErAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ePwFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6858,4579673&dq=mapco+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On November 17, a one-inch connector on a sour gas gathering pipeline broke near [[Malakoff, Texas]] on November 17. 12 families were evacuated for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1032&dat=19801120&id=3p5lAAAAIBAJ&sjid=FR4QAAAAIBAJ&pg=2163,3625910|title=The Malakoff News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 A pipeline carrying [[naphtha]] ruptured under a street in [[Long Beach, California]], causing a fire that destroyed one home and damaged several others. Two people were injured. Lack of communication of pipeline valve setups, and pressure relief valves set to open at too high a pressure were identified by the NTSB as causes of the accident. (December 1, 1980)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-81-023|title=Safety Recommendation P-81-023|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=-BshAAAAIBAJ&sjid=h2EEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5161,332033&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 A dirt pan machine being used for road construction hit a propane pipeline in [[Sumner, Georgia]] on December 10, causing slight injuries to the dirt pan operator. US Highway 82 and a rail line were closed, and several families evacuated until the vapors dispersed. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=dolEAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZrUMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1315,1899283&dq=dixie+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Albany Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 On December 22, a pipeline carrying jet fuel ruptured in [[Las Vegas Valley|Las Vegas]], [[Nevada]], spilling fuel for 2 hours. Later, the fuel ignited, forcing road closures. One firefighters was overcome by fumes. Between 50,000 and {{convert|100,000|USgal|L}} of jet fuel were spilled. Prior construction in the area was suspected of damaging the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=98YuAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GNsFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2134,5016662&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 A [[Southern California Edison]] pipeline ruptured in [[Carson, California]] on December 23, spilling about 105,000 gallons of crude oil, with some of it reaching the [[Dominguez Channel]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1310&dat=19801226&id=c1hYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7-EDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4275,8280119|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1980 A natural gas pipeline exploded and burned at a gas plant in [[Ulysses, Kansas]] on December 28. There were no injuries<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=J_tNAAAAIBAJ&sjid=jIsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6711,4658602&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1981'''
* 1981 A valve on the [[Trans-Alaska Pipeline System]] broke on January 1, releasing about 42,000 gallons of crude oil, about 115 miles south of [[Prudhoe Bay, Alaska]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=799&dat=19810103&id=U8NPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=BFIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3942,151269|title=The Bryan Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1873&dat=19810104&id=5tYpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=x9EEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2833,1131718|title=Daytona Beach Morning Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 On January 5, a gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Laingsburg, Michigan]], causing a large fire. About a dozen homes nearby were evacuated. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19810102&id=XEZOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rksDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1653,223993|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 On February 13, construction workers severed an ethylene pipeline near [[Beaumont, Texas]], which then exploded and burned. Three people were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1454&dat=19810214&id=LDlOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WhMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5316,3292479|title=Star-News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1981 On April 16, an explosion & fire in a gas feeder line to an underground gas storage facility in [[Columbus Junction, Iowa]] burned down a barn, and damaged other buildings. This was the second explosion at the facility in just over a week, and, the fifth explosion there in 6 years.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19810417&id=r10zAAAAIBAJ&sjid=EPcDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3282,3616502|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 An ammonia pipeline leaked near [[Hutchinson, Kansas]] on July 31, injuring 5 people, including 3 children at a Bible Camp. A {{convert|2|mi|km|adj=on}} radius from the leak was evacuated, including 90 from the Bible Camp.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=e6U_AAAAIBAJ&sjid=WlYMAAAAIBAJ&pg=6124,2465540&dq=ammonia+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Daily Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 On August 25, in downtown [[San Francisco, California]], a 16-inch natural gas main was punctured by a drill that an excavation contractor was using. Escaping natural gas blew upward and carried into the Embarcadero Complex and other nearby buildings. There was no ignition; however, the gas stream entrained an oil containing [[polychlorinated biphenyl]] (PCB). Fall-out affected an eight-square-block area of the city's financial district covering buildings, cars, trees, pedestrians, police, and firemen. Approximately 30,000 persons were safely evacuated from the area in 45&nbsp;minutes. No one was killed or seriously injured, although many persons were sprayed with the PCB oil mist. There were delays in shutting down the gas, due to inaccurate diagrams.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8201.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1981 On September 4, a drilling rig, operated by a crew core-drilling for coal, near [[Belle, West Virginia]], punctured a 12-inch gas transmission line. The pipeline was operating at a pressure of 600 psig. The rig operator was injured, the rig and a truck were destroyed, and an estimated volume of 3,433,000 cubic feet of gas was lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P82_19.pdf |format=PDF |title=Safety Recommendations |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1981 On September 15, during routine maintenance, a pipeline exploded and burned between a gas plant and a petroleum plant in [[Goldsmith, Texas]]. While workers were fighting the fire, another part of the pipeline burst and burned. 6 workers were burned, and another had other injuries. There were a total of 7 fires from 7 pipeline ruptures.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=6GIrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=iNkEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5530,3849000&dq=phillips+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Daily Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=bbwzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=-fYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4982,3503876&dq=phillips+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 A 12-inch diameter pipeline, near [[Ackerly, Texas]], was hit by a rathole drill on September 27, releasing an ethane-propane mix. There was then an explosion & fire that killed 4 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8202.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1981 On November 30, at [[Flatwoods, West Virginia]], gas leaking into a test section of a 26-inch gas transmission pipeline, ignited while a welder engaged in installing an end cap on the east end of a {{convert|180|ft|m|adj=on}}-long section of pipe. The resultant explosion blew off-the end cap, which struck and killed the welder's helper.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-82-012|title=Safety Recommendation P-82-012|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1981 On December 5, hunters near [[Yutan, Nebraska]] tried out a new high power rifle by shooting what they thought was a log in a creek bed. The log was actually an LPG pipeline, and 12 to 16 families needed to be evacuated for their safety from the resulting vapor cloud. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=B_VVAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WuIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4493,1417146&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 On December 9, a pipeline carrying gasoline ruptured near [[Joliet, Illinois]], spilling {{convert|30,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline into the [[Des Plaines River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=cSwdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TaUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5739,3650570&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1981 A 20-inch gas pipeline in [[Ottawa, Kansas]] caused 2 explosions, and a raging fire, that destroyed 2 mobile homes on December 31. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120711103919/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=EQAtAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AM0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=1632,500227&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Reagan Plans to|website=archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19820102&id=Gq4zAAAAIBAJ&sjid=iucFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4560,233832|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1982'''
* 1982 On January 1, a gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Ottawa, Kansas]], destroying 2 mobile homes. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=950&dat=19820102&id=vcNaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7VkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2219,392691|title=The Evening Independent - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 On January 28 at [[Centralia, Missouri]], natural gas at 47 psig entered a low pressure distribution system which normally operated at 0.40 psig after a backhoe bucket snagged, ruptured, and separated a 3/4-inch steel pressure regulator control line at a regulator station. The backhoe, which was owned and operated by the city of Centralia, was being used to clean a ditch located adjacent to the pressure regulator station. The high-pressure gas entering customer piping systems in some cases resulted in high pilot light flames which initiated fires in buildings; while in other cases, the pilot light flames were blown out, allowing gas to escape within the buildings. Of the 167 buildings affected by the overpressure, 12 were destroyed and 32 sustained moderate to heavy damages. Five persons received minor injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-82-030|title=Safety Recommendation P-82-030|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 On March 19, a leaking 3 inch [[Amoco]] pipeline was discovered in a park in [[Salt Lake City, Utah]]. 1,500 square feet of sod near a soccer field was contaminated by oil, and had to be disposed of as toxic waste.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=336&dat=19820323&id=F_0yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WoMDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7065,6172591|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 A [[Mobil]] LPG pipeline was ruptured by road construction in [[North Richland Hills, Texas]] on April 16. 800 to 1,000 nearby residents were evacuated. There was no fire. The construction crew workers said the pipeline was {{convert|5|ft|m}} away from where it was shown on a map they were using.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=kbRQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MuIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5733,3579999&dq=propane+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 A backhoe ruptured a 2-inch gas pipeline in three places in [[Tacoma, Washington]], causing evacuations. There was no fire or explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120717234428/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=f3IhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=f4gFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6518,6457306&dq=lakewood+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Gas leak routs Tacomans|website=archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 On May 14, a bulldozer hit a gas pipeline while digging a reserve pit for an oil well near [[Rush Springs, Oklahoma]], causing a gas fire that injured 9 workers.
* 1982 On May 18, [[Sunoco]] pipeline crews were digging to find their 12-inch pipeline, when they hit it, causing a rupture, and  spilling gasoline east of [[Gettysburg, Pennsylvania]]. Over 20,000 gallons of gasoline were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2202&dat=19820519&id=89pcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=P1gNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1796,1768746|title=Gettysburg Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 A bulldozer hit a [[Colonial Pipeline]] 12-inch petroleum products pipeline near [[Albany, Georgia]] on June 15, spraying the area with fuel oil, which then ignited, resulting in burns that later killed the bulldozer operator. No one had called for a locate of the pipeline before the bulldozer work.<ref name="ntsb.gov">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-82-040|title=Safety Recommendation P-82-040|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 On June 28, a natural gas explosion demolished a house, killed five persons, and critically injured one person in [[Portales, New Mexico]]; the critically injured person died later at a burn treatment center. The gas service line to the house had been damaged 37 days earlier when a contractor's backhoe pulled up the line during conduit excavation work for the local telephone company.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-83-001|title=Safety Recommendation P-83-001|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 A [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] was struck bu equipment by crew working on that pipeline in [[Prichard, West Virginia]] on July 28. 9 people were burned, including a family of 4 who were standing nearby, and 200 feet of a nearby road was burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19820727&id=cZEqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XlgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6909,6921365|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 On August 15, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] stub line failed in [[Floyd County, Georgia]], spilling over 16,000 gallons of gasoline in the area of a subdivision. 15 families were evacuated for a time. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=348&dat=19820817&id=nGgwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qDQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6160,2747860|title=Rome News-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 On September 7, natural gas at 15 psig escaping from the open ends of a 2&nbsp;1/4-inch cast-iron gas main located in a deep, narrow excavation in [[Dublin, Georgia]], was ignited by an unknown source. Four City of Dublin gas department employees who were working in the excavation were critically burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-82-043|title=Safety Recommendation P-82-043|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 A bulldozer being used for highway construction hit a [[Diamond Shamrock]] pipeline on September 10, in [[Roanoke, Texas]], spilling unleaded gasoline. 5 miles of a nearby highway were shut down for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19820911&id=r8FdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JF4NAAAAIBAJ&pg=5987,2742867|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1982 On September 13, a county worker hit an NGL pipeline near [[Leavenworth, Kansas]], causing minor injuries to him when the escaping gas blew him off of the bulldozer. Several families living nearby were evacuated. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19820914&id=q40yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MegFAAAAIBAJ&pg=1235,2747996|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 On October 1, a steel plate, which had been welded by a work crew to cap temporarily the open end of a section of a 22-inch gas transmission pipeline, blew off at an initial pressure of possibly 260 psig. Escaping natural gas from the pipeline, which had accumulated due to a leak in a nearby gate valve, ignited almost immediately and the entire work area and a portion of U.S. Route 65 were momentarily engulfed in flames. Seven persons who were working to replace a section of the pipeline under the road about {{convert|2|mi|km}} south of [[Pine Bluff, Arkansas]], were burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-83-022|title=Safety Recommendation P-83-022|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 On October 29, a crew mechanic working on new gas service lines in [[Burke, Virginia]], was overcome by leaking gas and died.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-83-010|title=Safety Recommendation P-83-010|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 On November 4, a tile plow installing field drainage tile on a farm, located {{convert|4|mi|km}} west of Hudson, Iowa, struck and punctured a well-marked, 20-inch natural gas transmission pipeline. Natural gas escaping at about 820&nbsp;psig ignited immediately, and the ensuing fire killed five persons.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8302.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=zKMyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=_O4FAAAAIBAJ&pg=2556,2256191&dq=pipeline-explosion&hl=en|title=Ottawa Citizen - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1982 On December 8, a five-member crew was working on a gas compressor at [[Bonicord, Tennessee]], when a gas explosion occurred. All five crew members were injured seriously, but were able to evacuate the building. One crew member died later that day, and two others died a few days later.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-83-017|title=Safety Recommendation P-83-017|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1982 A grader working on construction cut into a crude oil pipeline in [[Norman, Oklahoma]] on December 21, causing a fire that severely burned the grader operator.
*'''1983'''
* In January 1983, a pipeline owned by [[Diamond Shamrock]] began to leak into a creek, in [[Lipscomb County, Texas]]. Before the leak was detected and the flow of oil shut down, a period of about two weeks, about 100,000 gallons of crude petroleum were discharged into a creek.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://openjurist.org/756/f2d/392/hamker-v-diamond-shamrock-chemical-co|title=756 F2d 392 Hamker v. Diamond Shamrock Chemical Co - OpenJurist|work=openjurist.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 On February 1, a corroded gas service line caused a natural gas explosion and flash fire that destroyed a house, killed two persons, and injured three persons in [[Pryor, Oklahoma]], and damaged an adjacent house.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-83-029|title=Safety Recommendation P-83-029|website=Ntsb.gov|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1983 A gas pipeline failed and caused a fire, with flames 250 to {{convert|300|ft|m}} tall, near [[Marlow, Oklahoma]] on February 15. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YtRDAAAAIBAJ&sjid=yK8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=6182,3633848&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Durant Daily Democrat - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 An 8-inch LPG pipeline was hit by a rotating auger used for planting trees near [[West Odessa, Texas]]. After several minutes, the escaping LPG at 1,060 psi ignited, killing 5 people and injuring 5 others. Flames went as high as 600 feet into the air.(March 15, 1983)<ref>[http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P84_019.pdf ]{{dead link|date=June 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www3.gendisasters.com/texas/16866/odessa-tx-gas-pipeline-explosion-mar-1983|title=Odessa, TX  Gas Pipeline Explosion,  Mar 1983|work=gendisasters.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=sWBDAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9K0MAAAAIBAJ&pg=5203,1949236&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Daily Leader - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 On March 27, a pump for a petroleum products pipeline broke, causing up to 420,000 gallons of diesel fuel to spill into the Bowie River in [[Collins, Mississippi]].<ref>{{cite news| url=https://www.nytimes.com/1983/03/28/us/around-the-nation-large-diesel-fuel-spill-contained-in-mississippi.html | work=The New York Times | title=AROUND THE NATION; Large Diesel Fuel Spill Contained in Mississippi | date=March 28, 1983}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=_6lOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=g_sDAAAAIBAJ&pg=1646,6237301&dq=pipeline+accident&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 30 to 40 homes were advised to evacuate for several hours in [[Castle Shannon, Pennsylvania]] on May 1, after a [[Mobil]] pipeline leaked gasoline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1144&dat=19830502&id=4Hk0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=GZYEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1642,2423249|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 On May 6, a gas pipeline broke, forcing 100 people to evacuate in [[Cherry Hill, New Jersey]].<ref>{{cite news| url=https://www.nytimes.com/1983/05/07/nyregion/residents-flee-gas-leak.html | work=The New York Times | title=Residents Flee Gas Leak | date=May 7, 1983}}</ref>
* 1983 A 36-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Caldwell, Ohio]] on May 21, destroying two homes, burning 100 acres of vegetation, and closing nearby Interstate 77. There were three minor injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=taYrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=6PwFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2523,4767713&dq=pipeline-explosion&hl=en|title=The Telegraph - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 On June 4, a front loader accidentally dug into the 10-inch Yellowstone Pipeline  petroleum line near [[Coeur d'Alene, Idaho]], spilling over {{convert|20,000|USgal|L}} of unleaded gasoline into a creek, killing everything downstream for 3 miles.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=5OsRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=re4DAAAAIBAJ&pg=3832,3878689&dq=conoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 A 16-inch gas pipeline ruptures and burned near [[Athens, Texas]], on July 19. A nearby section of the same pipeline had ruptured the year before.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=7FllAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5ZMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3133,4769035&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Malakoff News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* '''[[East Boston gas surge]]''': On September 23, gas service pressure surged up in a section of [[Boston, Massachusetts]]. 3 major structure fires, numerous smaller fires, and an explosion at a restaurant followed. There was no serious injuries. A flooded gas regulator vault was the cause.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1984/P84_10.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007194444/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1984/P84_10.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1983 On October 10, a bulldozer ruptured a gas pipeline serving the [[Lake Park, Iowa]] area, causing gas supply shortages in the area. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1907&dat=19831012&id=u3dhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4NgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1902,630812|title=The Daily Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 18 people inside a supermarket in [[South Charleston, West Virginia]] on October 17 were hurt, when gas from a leaking Columbia Gas line exploded. One Columbia Gas worker was also hurt. The lack of communication from the Columbia crew working on the gas line to the store Manager was cited as a contributing factor.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1320&dat=19840724&id=GUBWAAAAIBAJ&sjid=2-kDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5143,2914308|title=Gainesville Sun - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1983 A Mid-Vally crude oil pipeline exploded and burned, at a pipeline terminal, in [[Lima, Ohio]] on December 25. The fire spread to a holding tank, forcing nearby residents to evacuate.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1310&dat=19831226&id=Kw5WAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NeIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6871,7007888|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''1984'''
* 1984 On January 15, a leak was discovered in an 8-inch pipeline belonging to [[Plantation Pipeline]] in [[Floyd County, Georgia]]. Over 300 gallons of gasoline and diesel fuel had spilled into creek. A hayfield nearby was also damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=348&dat=19840119&id=5QQuAAAAIBAJ&sjid=0TQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5895,2566145|title=Rome News-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1984 An 8-inch NGL pipeline near [[Hurst, Texas]], was hit by a front loader, and the escaping gases ignited, causing burns to the equipment operator. (February 28, 1984)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_1_3.pdf|title=SAFETY RECOMMENDATION(S)  |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007214600/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_1_3.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1984 On March 25, a resident in [[Missouri City, Texas]] discovered gasoline leaking from an 8-inch [[Exxon]] products  pipeline. About 1,000 residents in the area were evacuated for a time, and, some of the gasoline entered a nearby creek.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19840326&id=3YEzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=1TIHAAAAIBAJ&pg=4800,2871184|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1984 On March 27, a pipeline rupture destroyed a home, and, damaged 4 other buildings, in [[Mont Belvieu, Texas]]<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1915&dat=19851106&id=DjdSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=SzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2572,997517&hl=en|title=The Day - Google News Archive Search|website=news.google.com}}</ref>
* 1984 On April 24, a contractor installing plastic drainage pipe on a farm near [[Rock Rapids, Iowa]] hit a petroleum products pipeline, spilling about 4,000 gallons of diesel fuel.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1907&dat=19840426&id=xmYrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=99gEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4622,1951865|title=The Daily Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1984 On June 19, six employees of a contractor working for Washington Gas Light Company (WGL) in Rockville, Maryland, were using mechanical saws to cut a section of 22-inch steel pipeline when residual gas at atmospheric pressure in the isolated section of the pipeline was ignited. A flash fire ensued, and four contractor employees who were operating the saws and a WGL superintendent were burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_4_5.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622081045/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_4_5.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* On August 14, a Plantation Pipeline line leaked near [[Ladysmith, Virginia]], creating a gasoline mist in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1298&dat=19840814&id=OeVLAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TosDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5737,2989529|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1984 Two natural gas pipelines exploded and burned near [[Falls City, Texas]].<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=DM&p_theme=dm&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0ED617821DE33D3C&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=TWO GAS PIPELINES EXPLODE |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1984 On September 24, a failed gas main of ABS plastic caused an explosion and fire in [[Phoenix, Arizona]]. 5 people died and 7 others injured in the accident. Liquid in the pipe had caused it to break down.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8501.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1984 A tugboat hit and ruptured a gas pipeline on the [[Houston Ship Channel]] on October 16. There were no injuries, but the Channel was closed for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=BL49AAAAIBAJ&sjid=GTYMAAAAIBAJ&pg=4899,1287767&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Mid Cities Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1984 Fast moving water in the [[Cado Creek]] near [[Durant, Oklahoma]] led to 2 pipelines being ruptured on October 27 & 28. One pipeline was owned by [[Mobil]], the other pipeline was owned by [[Total S.A.]]. About {{convert|1500|oilbbl|m3}} of petroleum were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120722104916/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=wIVJAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4AsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3526,10717976&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Broken oil pipeline dumps 1,500 gallons into wildlife refuge|website=archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1984 A [[Williams Companies]] 6 inch pipeline ruptured on November 18 in [[New Brighton, Minnesota]], causing a spill of 40,000 to 50,000 gallons of jet fuel in an industrial area. There were no injuries.<ref>[https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=is9JAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fgsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6143,7111052&dq=minnesota+pipeline+leak&hl=en ]{{dead link|date=June 2017}}</ref>
* 1984 On November 25, a 30-inch gas transmission pipeline, constructed in 1955 and operating at 1,000&nbsp;psig pressure, ruptured at a location about three miles (5&nbsp;km) west of [[Jackson, Louisiana]]. Gas blowing from the rupture fractured the pipe into many pieces and created a hole in the earth about {{convert|90|ft|m}} long, {{convert|25|ft|m}} wide, and {{convert|10|ft|m}} deep. The escaping gas was quickly ignited by one of several potential sources of ignition. The resulting fire incinerated an area extending from the rupture about {{convert|950|ft|m}} north, {{convert|500|ft|m}} south, and {{convert|180|ft|m}} to the east and to the west. Within this sparsely populated area, five persons involved with the pipeline construction work were killed, and 23 persons were injured. Additionally, several pieces of construction equipment were damaged extensively. Lack of proper ground support under the pipeline when a nearby section of that pipeline was upgraded and replaced was identified as a factor in the failure.<ref name=autogenerated1>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR-86-01-SUM.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident / Incident Summary Reports |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.louisianapersonalinjurylawyerblog.com/2010/04/west_feliciana_parish_pipeline.html|title=Safety Recommendations |archive-url=https://archive.is/20130127235257/http://www.louisianapersonalinjurylawyerblog.com/2010/04/west_feliciana_parish_pipeline.html |dead-url=yes |archive-date=January 27, 2013 |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |df= }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=by1JAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ln8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=2714,7384643&dq=family+killed+by+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1985===
* 1985 Natural gas from a leaking line traveled through soil, and caused a massive gas explosion in [[El Paso, Texas]] on January 8. Eleven people were injured, 2 homes were destroyed, and 88 other homes were damaged by the blast.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yq1HAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XH8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=6997,2634025&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On January 26, a leaking propylene pipeline in [[Baytown, Texas]] forced the evacuation of 600 people. There was no explosion or fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ofpRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZjQNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4555,1910638&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Mid Cities Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On February 5, a gas triggered explosion and fire destroyed 12 newly constructed condominiums in [[Twin Lakes, Wisconsin]]. A cracked gas main was the source of the gas leak, and nearby sewer work was suspected of damaging the gas line. Two firefighters were hurt extinguishing the fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19850207&id=QW4aAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ISoEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3887,5134080|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On February 22, 1985, a police patrolman on routine patrol smelled strong natural gas odors in [[Sharpsville, Pennsylvania]]. A gas serviceman was ordered to the scene. Before the serviceman arrived at the site of the reported leak, the Sharpsville Inn, and a connecting building, exploded and burned, killing two persons. Firefighters arriving on scene moments later encountered a second, smaller explosion, which injured one firefighter. The delay in the gas serviceman getting to the incident was a contributing factor.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8502.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1985 On April 5, lightning caused a computer malfunction with [[Colonial Pipeline]], resulting in a pipeline rupture that sent at least 126,000 gallons of gasoline into the [[Yellow Leaf Creek]] in [[Talladega County, Alabama]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=SjYdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sqUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6786,1884210&dq=colonial+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1891&dat=19850408&id=YbgfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rNcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3042,1547057|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On April 18, fumes from an NGL pipeline, under repair near [[Baxter Pass, Colorado]], killed one pipeline repair worker, & injured 9 others. During a lawsuit dealing with this accidents, it was claimed "The "safety" procedures used were crude at best, as the workers without lifelines were directed to hold their breath and go down into the ditch for about 30 seconds to work, before coming back out of the ditch for air."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19850419&id=EschAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5p0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=1925,4504430|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://law.justia.com/cases/wyoming/supreme-court/1988/122028.html|title=Wessel v. Mapco, Inc.|work=Justia Law|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A 30-inch diameter gas pipeline operating at about 960 psi, weakened by atmospheric corrosion, ruptured, and tore out about {{convert|29|ft|m}} of the carrier pipe, blew apart about {{convert|16|ft|m}} of a 36-inch casing pipe, blasted an opening across Kentucky State Highway 90, and cut out a pear-shaped crater approximately {{convert|90|ft|m}} long, {{convert|38|ft|m}} wide, and {{convert|12|ft|m}} deep near [[Beaumont, Kentucky]]. 5 people were killed in one home, and 3 injured. The fireball from the incident could be seen 20 miles away.(April 27, 1985)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_6.pdf |title=Safety Recommendations|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622080222/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_6.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=-PQrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AW0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=3025,7574446&dq=family+killed+by+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On May 10, a [[Mohave County, Arizona]] road crew hit a 2-inch gas pipeline while reinstalling a fallen stop sign, in [[Butler, Arizona]]. During repairs to the gas line, a flash fire ignited, injuring 2 fire fighters, and a Southern Union Gas Co. worker.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=943&dat=19850512&id=XsZPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=g1MDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5490,1172063|title=Mohave Daily Miner - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 Workers on the extension of the North Dallas Tollway ruptured a 12-inch gasoline pipeline on June 19, causing a massive gasoline spill along a creek bed north of [[Dallas, Texas]]. The gasoline later ignited. One person had moderate injuries, several office buildings were damaged by fire, and some automobiles were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KdA9AAAAIBAJ&sjid=RjcMAAAAIBAJ&pg=6652,8009279&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Mid Cities Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On June 20, a telephone cable installing crew broke a 10 gas gathering pipeline, in [[Paradise, Texas]], releasing gas, that ignited 20 seconds later. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19850621&id=PiZSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vTUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4134,2361312|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On July 23, in a rural area about {{convert|8|mi|km}} south of [[Kaycee, Wyoming]], a girth weld cracked during a pipeline re-coating project on a 23-year-old, 8-inch pipeline. The cracked girth weld allowed the release, atomization of, and ignition of aircraft turbine fuel under 430 pounds pressure, killing one person, burning six other persons, and destroying construction equipment.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-86-012 |title=Safety Recommendation P-86-012 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eZozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LYQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5815,3641705&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=336&dat=19850724&id=eZozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LYQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5815,3641705|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A gasoline leak of up to {{convert|42,000|USgal|L}} from a ruptured 10-inch pipeline ignited, on August, 2 in [[Indianapolis, Indiana]], causing a {{convert|200|ft|m|adj=on}} high fireball that killed three people, and injured 3 others working to clean up the spill along a creek.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9C07E4D91038F930A3575BC0A963948260|title=AROUND THE NATION -    3 WORKERS KILLED BY FIRE IN INDIANA GASOLINE SPILL - NYTimes.com|date=3 August 1985|work=nytimes.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=H9FGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=_HsMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5329,298801&dq=ammonia+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On August 22, a vessel was being filled with Liquefied Natural Gas (LNG), when it burst, leading to a flash fire that burned 6 people, at a gas facility in [[Pinson, Alabama]].<ref name=autogenerated1 />
* 1985 On September 23, a 12-inch diameter gasoline pipeline fitting was hit by a backhoe, and sprayed about {{convert|35,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline {{convert|45|ft|m}} into the air in [[Staten Island, New York]]. There were evacuations, but no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YQshAAAAIBAJ&sjid=d3IFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2854,2186745&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Schenectady Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A Texas Eastern Transmission Corp. natural gas pipeline exploded near Hillsboro in [[Fleming County, Kentucky]] on October 26. There were two injuries reported.<ref name="google6683">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=BoQ_AAAAIBAJ&sjid=Q1UMAAAAIBAJ&pg=6683,125730&dq=pipeline+accident&hl=en|title=Portsmouth Daily Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=G7JcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pFgNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4759%2C284017|title=Portsmouth Daily Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On November 1, a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline exploded and burned near [[Rowenna, Pennsylvania]], shooting flames 200 feet into the air, and causing dozens of residents to evacuate. A gas metering station and pressure regulator were also damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19851102&id=JU8gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bsgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5086,157952|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1985 On November 28, Olympic Pipeline spilled about 31,000 gallons of jet fuel at [[SeattleTacoma International Airport]], due to a valve being left open. The fuel entered a storm drain, that led to the [[Des Moines River]], killing fish and wildlife for 2.5 miles. Later, the company was fined $15,000 for the spill by the Washington Department of Ecology.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19851130&id=1rUzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oTIHAAAAIBAJ&pg=3234,3647862|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1345&dat=19860131&id=J_5LAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wPkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3474,3370169|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On December 6, a natural gas explosion and fire destroyed the River Restaurant in [[Derby, Connecticut]]. Gas escaping from a broken gas main at a pressure of about 1&nbsp;pound per square inch had escaped, migrated into the restaurant basement, ignited, exploded, and burned. Of the 18 persons inside the restaurant at the time, 6 were killed and 12 were injured; 1 passerby and 1 firefighter were also injured. After the accident the street adjacent to the restaurant was excavated where a 24-inch sewer system had just been installed; An 87-year-old, 3-inch, cast-iron natural gas main was found broken.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_16.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation  |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007142959/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_16.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov/cast_iron/|title=Page has moved|work=dot.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On December 5, a Central Florida Pipeline products line burst in [[Lake Alfred, Florida]], spilling about 40,000 gallons of gasoline. The landowner affected later sued the pipeline for failure to remove contaminated soil. There were no injuries or fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1346&dat=19870201&id=_ahOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dvsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2352,91805|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A water Department crew hit the cap of an illegal tap into a Four Corners crude oil pipeline on December 18, near [[Cabazon, California]]. About 47,000 gallons of crude were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19851219&id=xI9TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=soYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3315,3379748|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1986===
* 1986 On January 31, a 14-inch [[Sunoco]] pipeline began leaking gasoline in [[Mercer County, New Jersey]], which then spilled into the [[Delaware and Raritan Canal]]. The spilled gasoline exploded and burned along a 2,500 foot portion of the canal. People were evacuated from homes, and a nearby church.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19860201&id=wK5dAAAAIBAJ&sjid=o10NAAAAIBAJ&pg=3826,10669|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On February 10, construction crew cut through a gas pipeline in [[Lakeland, Florida]], resulting in about 175 people being evacuated from mobile homes and businesses for 2 hours. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1346&dat=19860211&id=k7cwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pvsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6485,4338007&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 A 30-inch Texas Eastern gas pipeline ruptured, due to corrosion, near [[Lancaster, Kentucky]]. 3 people had serious burns, and 5 others had lesser injuries. External corrosion made worse by difficulties of [[Cathodic protection]] in rocky soil was the cause. A senior vice president for operations and engineering with Texas Eastern Gas Pipeline Co., said tests on the Garrard County line last September showed the line needed immediate replacement. It was the third explosion on the Texas Eastern pipeline system in Kentucky in the previous 10 months, leading the Kentucky PSC to call for pressure reductions on the Texas Eastern system.(February 21, 1986)<ref name="google6683"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_14.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007143228/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_14.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yzAqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WUcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3876,3756877&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Park City Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 An 8-inch high-pressure petroleum pipeline ruptured in [[Muskegon County, Michigan]] on February 22, spilling gasoline into creeks.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mlive.com/opinion/muskegon/index.ssf/2011/01/editorial_citizens_must_keep_p.html|title=Editorial: Citizens must keep pressure on for monitoring, safety|work=MLive.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On February 24, a natural gas transmission pipeline split for 40 feet along its longitudinal seam in [[Case, Arkansas]]. Examining the pipe after the accident revealed lack of fusion, a known issue with LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] pipe used there. The pipeline has experienced 3 other such seam failures on that pipeline since 1975.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1987/PAR8702.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=July 16, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622103738/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1987/PAR8702.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1986 A backhoe snagged a natural gas distribution line in [[Fort Worth, Texas]], causing a break that leaked gas into an unoccupied building. Later, that building exploded, injuring 22 people, destroying the unoccupied building, and damaging 40 other buildings. 57 automobiles in the unoccupied building were damaged or destroyed. (March 12, 1986)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_29_33.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622095948/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_29_33.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1986 A new water main was being installed in [[Chicago Heights, Illinois]] on March 13. While excavating, an active gas service line was snagged. Gas company crews responded to the wrong site, causing delays in getting the leaking gas line shut down. Just as crews finished closing the valve on the leaking line, a nearby house exploded, and began to burn; One of the two persons inside that house was killed, and the other was injured. Two neighboring houses were damaged, and one gas company employee, two construction crew members, and four persons in the general area, were injured by the explosion and subsequent fire. Although gas company personnel arrived on the scene approximately 10&nbsp;minutes before the explosion and shut off the gas at the meter, neither they nor the contractor's crew had made an effort to warn or evacuate the residents of the house.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_35_38.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007163131/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_35_38.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1986 A gravel company endloader ruptured a Lakehead Pipeline crude oil pipeline on April 12 near [[Elgin, Illinois]], spill about 525,000 gallons of crude, and causing a "geyser" of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=HN&p_theme=hn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB0964F5939AD84&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date%3AD&s_trackval=GooglePM|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130129211248/http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=HN&p_theme=hn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB0964F5939AD84&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date%3AD&s_trackval=GooglePM|deadurl=yes|title=Suburban Chicago Newspapers - Search Results|date=29 January 2013|archivedate=29 January 2013|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1986 A backhoe ruptured an Olympic Pipeline line on May 8, south of [[Seattle, Washington]]. About 1,974 barrels of diesel fuel were spilled, with some of it entering the [[Green River (Duwamish River)|Green River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1345&dat=19860512&id=hkJYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=z_kDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3867,2803687|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1986 On May 14, a 6-inch [[Amoco]] pipeline, damaged by some type of arcing, leaked about 380 barrels of gasoline in [[Elmhurst, Illinois]]. Some of the gasoline fumes exploded in a nearby home, causing serious damage. Concerns about the lack of evacuations were raised later on. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1986-05-22/news/8602060804_1_pipeline-amoco-evacuation | work=Chicago Tribune | first=Neil H | last=Mehler | title=Probe Urged In Elmhurst Gasoline Leak | date=May 22, 1986}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266230|title=May 14, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On June 28, a pipeline ruptured and spilled diesel fuel into [[Trail Creek (Lake Michigan)|Trail Creek]] in [[Michigan City, Indiana]]. The fuel later ignited. Thousands of fish were killed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=56tUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tDsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2711,2893734&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Rochester Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 Early on July 8, a [[Williams Companies]] petroleum products pipeline ruptured in [[Mounds View, Minnesota]]. Gasoline at 1,434 psi sprayed a residential area around 4:20&nbsp;am local time, then ignited. A woman and her 7-year-old daughter suffered fatal burns, at least two others were injured, and many homes damaged or destroyed. Confusion by the pipeline company led to a delay in shutting down the pipeline. Electrical resistance welded ([[Electric resistance welding|ERW]]) seam failure caused the rupture. Prior to this accident, this pipeline, installed in 1957, had 16 seam failures during hydrostatic testing, and 7 seam failures during operations until 1984. In 1984, 16 more seams failed during a hydrostatic test. Problems with cathodic protection were also noted before the 1986 accident. During a hydrostatic test of this pipeline following the accident, 3 ERW seams failed. Studies of available data by OPS staff in early 1988 showed that ERW seams have been involved in 145 service failures in both hazardous liquid and natural gas pipelines since 1970 to early 1988, and that of these failures, all but 2 occurred on pipe manufactured prior to 1970.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8702.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board : Pipeline Accident Report |date=July 8, 1986 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.startribune.com/local/12564991.html |title=July 9, 1986: Gasoline pipeline explodes in Mounds View|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150427142920/http://www.startribune.com/local/12564991.html |archivedate=April 27, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Advisory%20Bulletin%20Files/xALN-88-01.pdf |format=PDF |title=Alert Notice : Recent findings relative to factors contributing to operational failures of pipelines constructed with ERW prior to 1970. |website=Phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.startribune.com/templates/Print_This_Story?sid=12564991|title=July 9, 1986: Gasoline pipeline explodes in Mounds View|work=startribune.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="mycommittees.api.org">{{cite web|url=http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/electricresistanceweldfailures.pdf |format=PDF |title=Electric Resistance Weld Pipe Failures on Hazardous Liquid and Gas Transmission Pipelines |website=Mycommittees.api.org |accessdate=2016-01-18 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304094851/http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/electricresistanceweldfailures.pdf |archivedate=2016-03-04 |df= }}</ref>
* 1986 A [[Southern Natural Gas]] transmission pipeline failed and burned, in a compressor station, near [[Prattville, Alabama]], on July 12. The fire spread by melting flange gaskets on 2 other gas transmission pipelines in the station. 4 homes and several cars were destroyed in the following fire, with flames reaching {{convert|300|ft|m}} high. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Z5ItAAAAIBAJ&sjid=F8kEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4307,1957194&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On July 22, a leak at an underground propane storage facility in [[Petal, Mississippi]] exploded, causing a massive fire, injuring 14 people, and forcing 200 people to evacuate. A crater 260 feet in diameter and 37 feet deep was made by the explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=e_QaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Y0cEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5337,4268109&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=qbBOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cPsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7010,2867730&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.osha.gov/pls/imis/establishment.inspection_detail?id=101557098|title=Inspection Detail|work=osha.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 Between 800 and 1200 residents were evacuated in [[East Chicago, Indiana]], after a gasoline tank at a pipeline Terminal ruptured on September 4. 28 people were overcome by gasoline fumes.
