There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=W49TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oIYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4801,1802743&dq=phillips+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 A CENEX 8 inch petroleum products pipeline failed near [[Billings, Montana]] on September 4, spilling gasoline, and causing the evacuation of nearby businesses. About 29,400 gallons of gasoline spilled. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ekJYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=zPkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7003,1306572&dq=yellowstone+pipeline+leaks&hl=en|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="projects.propublica.org">{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266320|title=Sept. 4, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="projects.propublica.org"/>
* 1986 On September 4, a tank failed at a [[Phillips Petroleum Company]] facility in [[East Chicago, Indiana]], forcing 800 to 1,200 residents near by to evacuate, and spilling 55,000 barrels of gasoline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19860905&id=W49TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oIYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4801,1802743|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On September 8, an [[Amoco]] gas condensate pipeline failed under the [[Red River of the South|Red River]] near [[Dexter, Texas]]. Fumes from the leaking pipeline sent 14 people to hospitals for treatment.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=F5I9AAAAIBAJ&sjid=4DUMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5284,272093&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Bonham Daily Favorite - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsok.com/leak-in-pipeline-blamed-for-fumes/article/2159247|title=Leak in Pipeline Blamed for Fumes|work=NewsOK.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 In October, a 21-inch long crack on an 14-inch [[Sunoco]] petroleum products pipeline in [[King of Prussia, Pennsylvania]] spilled about 220,000 gallons of gasoline, forcing evacuations, including about 900 students from a middle school. The failure was near a previously repaired area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19861011&id=iXRiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=E3cNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5709,1578649|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266349|title=Oct. 7, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19861008&id=pV4tAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TtoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3177,1690511|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On November 13, a gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Stinnett, Texas]], killing one person. The pipeline has been installed in 1982.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266387|title=Nov. 13, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On December 6 in the early morning hours a 30-inch natural gas pipe line exploded on the north edge of the [[Ross Barnett Reservoir]] (Pelahatchie Bay) in Mississippi, near [[Jackson, Mississippi|Jackson]]. There were no casualties. The blast was seen by airline pilots as far away as Houston TX and Nashville TN.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://thereznews.blogspot.com/2011/01/explosion.html|title=Ross Barnett Reservoir|work=thereznews.blogspot.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On December 25, an [[Amoco]] pipeline ruptured, and spilled furnace oil into the [[Des Plaines River]] near [[Chicago, Illinois]]. About 429 barrels of furnace oil were spilled. External corrosion was the cause of the pipeline failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=pblQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qvMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5006,3701180&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Lewiston Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266426|title=Dec. 25, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1987===
* 1987 On January 30, natural gas leaking from a pipeline under repair in [[Colorado Springs, Colorado]], ignited, sending flames 45 feet into the air, and injuring four people.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.apnewsarchive.com/1990/Other-Recent-Pipeline-Accidents-With-AM-Pipeline-Explosion/id-4ddc2e27adf7538512f63be3a726e138|title=Other Recent Pipeline Accidents With AM-Pipeline Explosion|work=apnewsarchive.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A petroleum pipeline ruptured and burned, near [[Corsicana, Texas]] on March 12, forcing the closure of an Interstate highway, and cause some evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KShAAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uVgMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3718,5358666&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A work crew burning the remains of a house near [[Ladysmith, Virginia]] ruptured a nearby petroleum products pipeline with a bulldozer on March 26, igniting diesel fuel from the line. 2 of the worker were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=zzgwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hIsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3925,888188&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On April 4, an LPG pipeline exploded at a Terminal in [[Iowa City, Iowa]]. Due to the fire spreading to a pipeline for nearby underground gas storage, residents within a 2 1/2 mile radius of the Terminal were evacuated for a time. The fire burned until April 20. The cause was an [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure in a pipeline. During a hydrostatic test of that pipeline, 20 more pipeline segment seams failed.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ASFRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=K88MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1518,670078&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=DCFRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=K88MAAAAIBAJ&pg=3030,3587912&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 In [[Odessa, Texas]], on April 18, a crude oil pipeline burst into flames, destroying nine mobile homes and two cars. The fire started under a mobile home on Andrews Highway. The Texas Railroad Commission stated that gases within the crude corroded and weakened the 10-inch 60-year-old pipe. When the line split, it spewed oil into the fire, fueling the blaze and causing dense black smoke that choked firefighters and bystanders.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oaoa.com/75th_anniversary/article_47fdc83a-5332-11e5-bca5-7717d7feedac.html|title=1987: Meet Baby Jessica, economy improves|work=Odessa American|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A [[Mobil]] pipeline ruptured near [[Lebec, California]] on June 8, spilling about 2,500 barrels of crude oil. The failure was from external corrosion of the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266572|title=June 8, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1987 On June 11, a "rock ripper" at a construction site punctured a 32-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] petroleum products pipeline in [[Centreville, Virginia]]. Gasoline sprayed from the rupture, but there was no fire. More than {{convert|15,500|USgal|L}} of gasoline were released. Thirteen emergency response personnel suffered from exposure to the gasoline fumes.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1996/SIR9602.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101205073217/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1996/SIR9602.pdf |archivedate=December 5, 2010 }}</ref>
* 1987 An [[Amoco]] pipeline failed in [[Florence, Michigan]] on June 11, spilling 24,000 barrels of petroleum.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266574|title=June 11, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On June 12, a petroleum products pipeline ruptured near [[Harwood, North Dakota]]. 289 barrels of fuel oil were spilled. There were no injuries. Investigation showed this pipeline failed at a low frequency Electric Resistance Welding ([[Electric resistance welding|ERW]]) seam. Further testing after this accident lead to 5 other LF-ERW failures along this pipeline in Minnesota and North Dakota.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf|title=VIA CERTIFIED MAIL (RETTJRI). RECEIPT REOUESTED |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028014558/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266577|title=June 12, 1987 - ProPublica|work=Propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1987 Construction equipment hit a LPG/NGL pipeline near [[Rochester, Iowa]] on June 26, killing one person, and injuring 2 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266589|title=June 26, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 3, a Yellowstone Pipeline Company line failed from an unspecified flaw in the pipe, in [[Montana]]. About 162,000 gallons of petroleum product were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266597 |title=July 3, 1987 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1987-07-03 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 24, a fishing vessel, working in shallow waters off of [[Empire, Louisiana]], the Fishing vessel Sea Chief, struck and ruptured an 8" natural gas liquids pipeline operating at 480 psi. The resulting explosion killed two crew members. Divers investigating found that the pipe, installed in 1968, was covered with only 6" of soft mud, having lost its original {{convert|3|ft|m|adj=on}} cover of sediments.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epd.gov.hk/eia/register/report/eiareport/eia_1252006/html/eiareport/Part2/Section13/Sec2_13_AnnexB.htm|title=EIA Report - Part 2 Section13 Annex B|work=epd.gov.hk|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 23, a construction crew working on an Interstate 90 project east of [[Coeur d'Alene, Idaho]] struck the 10-inch diameter Yellowstone Pipeline, causing a leak that sprayed out over 27,000 gallons of gasoline. The pipeline was supposed to have 30&nbsp;inches of soil cover, but had only 2&nbsp;inches of cover. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=o5ZMAAAAIBAJ&sjid=svoDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5890,1950592&dq=yellowstone+pipeline+leaks&hl=en|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266613|title=July 23, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On August 5, gas leak on a busy road in [[Wilmington, North Carolina]] suddenly ignited, while gas company workers were trying to plug that leak, burning them and firefighters on standby. 19 people were burned, with a Fire Department Assistant Chief later dying from the burns he received.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.starnewsonline.com/article/20120110/ARTICLES/120119970/-1/news38?Title=Firefighters-raise-money-for-local-memorial#fb-root |title=Firefighters raise money for local memorial |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266628 |title=Aug. 5, 1987 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1987-08-05 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1987 On September 8, 3 pipeline workers were hurt, when a butane pipeline they were working on exploded near [[Kemah, Texas]].<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/><ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1987-09-10/news/mn-7201_1_pipeline-blast | work=Los Angeles Times | title=3 Hurt in Pipeline Blast | date=September 10, 1987}}</ref>
* 1987 4 pipeline workers were hurt while working on a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline in [[Martin, Kentucky]] on October 19. A rubber seal inside a steel collar failed, allowing 2 sections of pipeline to separate. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=266&dat=19871029&id=xR8uAAAAIBAJ&sjid=h9wFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3343,7204741|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1988===
* 1988 On January 5, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] mainline ruptured, spilling about 100,000 gallons of home heating oil in [[Deptford, New Jersey]]. The cause of the pipeline failure was corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://articles.philly.com/1988-01-15/news/26282729_1_oil-pipeline-colonial-pipeline-pipeline-burst|title=Deptford To Check Process Behind Pipeline's Permit|work=philly-archives|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pipelinesafetytrust.com/docs/ops_doc2.pdf |format=PDF |title=1996 Colonial Pipeline Task Force : Final Report |website=Pipelinesafetytrust.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1988 The rupture of a large interstate gas line at Pocono Ridge development in [[Lehman Township, Pike County, Pennsylvania|Lehman Township, Pennsylvania]], left a crater about {{convert|8|ft|m}} deep and ejected a {{convert|6|ft|m|adj=on}} section of pipe over the treetops before it landed 50&nbsp;yards away. One hundred thirty people were evacuated. No one was injured.<ref name="poconorecord1"/>
* 1988 On January 18, a natural gas explosion destroyed the building housing the K&W Cafeteria and the lobby of the Sheraton Motor Inn at [[Winston-Salem, North Carolina]]. Two adjoining motel wings suffered structural damage. Of the four persons in the lobby/cafeteria building at the time of the explosion, three sustained minor injuries. The fourth person sustained a fractured ankle. One motel guest also sustained minor cuts.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1988/P88_10.pdf |title=Safety Recommendation|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007170305/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1988/P88_10.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1988 On February 8, an offshore pipeline near [[Galveston, Texas]], that may have been damaged by an anchor, ruptured, spilling about {{convert|15576|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil into the Gulf.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gomr.boemre.gov/PDFs/1989/89-0102.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120316112409/http://www.gomr.boemre.gov/PDFs/1989/89-0102.pdf |archivedate=March 16, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266825|title=Feb. 8, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On February 17, a [[Sunoco]] pipeline near [[Pleasant Township, Seneca County, Ohio]] ruptured, spilling over 200,000 gallons of [[toluene]], with about 173,000 gallons of it being lost. 4,200 people had to evacuate their homes for a time.  The cause was previous third party damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19880224&id=aj5QAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5g0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=7048,3828963|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266843|title=Feb. 17, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19880313&id=hFBPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=6gIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1808,2576831|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On March 19, 130 people were evacuated from their homes, after a vehicle hit a valve on a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline in [[Hempfield, Pennsylvania]]. There was no gas ignition.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1129&dat=19880321&id=l9RRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=8m0DAAAAIBAJ&pg=3650,6512245|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On April 9, a 20-inch crude oil pipeline failed in a [[Peoria County, Illinois]] subdivision. About {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} of crude were spilled, contaminating 2 private lakes.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=gqFdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=51wNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6734,2215943&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A backhoe hit a 10 gas pipeline in [[Springfield, Massachusetts]], on April 18. Two Interstate freeways were shut down, and, 125 to 150 people were evacuated for a time from bearby businesses.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1928&dat=19880419&id=uDspAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fWUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3091,3674834|title=The Lewiston Daily Sun - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1988 A Kaneb Pipeline Terminal had a spill of 20,000 gallons of gasoline, on April 26, in [[Milford, Iowa]]. Operator error was given as the cause of the spill.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1907&dat=19880525&id=pVsrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qdgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1360,5277238|title=The Daily Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266898|title=April 26, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A pair of MAPCO LPG/NGL pipelines failed in an explosion south of [[Topeka, Kansas]], on July 22. 200 nearby residents had to be evacuated, and there was serious damage to US Route 75 nearby from the explosion & following fire. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam selective corrosion failure in one of the pipelines caused the failure.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=S4oyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uOYFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5501,4570580&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On August 31, a gas company crew struck and ruptured a fitting on a 4-inch plastic gas main in [[Green Oaks, Illinois]]. While the crew was attempting to excavate a nearby valve to shut off the flow of gas, the backhoe struck an unmarked power cable. The gas ignited and four gas company employees were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/recs/letters/1989/P89_7_8.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100612084408/http://www.ntsb.gov/Recs/letters/1989/P89_7_8.pdf |archivedate=June 12, 2010 }}</ref>
* 1988 A crude oil pipeline ruptured, spilling about 132,000 gallons of crude oil in [[Encino, California]] on September 10. The crude flowed into storm drains, and then into the [[Los Angeles River]]. Electrical interference to [[Cathodic protection]] from other pipelines was suspected to have cause the corrosion that caused the failure. The crude oil pipeline was on top of a steel water pipeline, which would directly interfere with Cathodic protection efforts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120723163831/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=jEYjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5csFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6111,2547117&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en |title=Pipe leak slimes river|website=Archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/59890837.html?dids=59890837:59890837&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Sep+15%2C+1988&author=&pub=Los+Angeles+Times+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=Local+News+in+Brief+Exterior+Corrosion+Blamed+in+Oil+Leak&pqatl=google | title=Local News in Brief Exterior Corrosion Blamed in Oil Leak | date=September 15, 1988}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/59804933.html?dids=59804933:59804933&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Oct+21%2C+1988&author=MICHAEL+CONNELLY&pub=Los+Angeles+Times+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=2+Legislators+Question+Oil+Pipeline+Reliability&pqatl=google | first=Michael | last=Connelly | title=2 Legislators Question Oil Pipeline Reliability | date=October 21, 1988}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/61362416.html?dids=61362416:61362416&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Jul+14%2C+1991&author=MYRON+LEVIN%3B+TRACEY+KAPLAN&pub=Los+Angeles+Times+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=Mobil+Hopes+to+Stem+Flow+of+Pipeline%27s+Problems+Environment%3A+Repeated+oil+spills+embarrass+the+firm+but+also+make+a+92-mile+replacement+conduit+easier+to+sell.&pqatl=google | first=Myron | last=Levin | title=Mobil Hopes to Stem Flow of Pipeline's Problems Environment: Repeated oil spills embarrass the firm but also make a 92-mile replacement conduit easier to sell | date=July 14, 1991}}</ref><ref name="articles.latimes.com">{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1991-07-18/news/we-3568_1_pipeline-safety | work=Los Angeles Times | first1=Myron | last1=Levin | first2=Tracey | last2=Kaplan | title=Out With Old Mobil Pipeline, but Will New Line Be Better? : Environment: New pipeline's coating is state-of-the-art. But it remains to be seen if it can avoid leakage problems that made its predecessor a dismal performer | date=July 18, 1991}}</ref>
* 1988 On September 16, a natural gas explosion in Overland Park, Kansas, involved gas leaking from corrosion holes in the customer-owned line. Gas migrated underground to the house and was ignited. The house was destroyed and the four residents were injured.<ref name="ReferenceB">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/_layouts/ntsb.research/Recommendation.aspx|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=May 8, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150528231014/http://www.ntsb.gov/_layouts/ntsb.research/Recommendation.aspx |archivedate=May 28, 2015 }}</ref>
* 1988 On October 9, third party damage to a Yellowstone Pipeline Company line caused the line to fail, near [[Garrison, Montana]]. About 260,000 gallons of petroleum products were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267027 |title=Oct. 9, 1988 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1988-10-09 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1988 On October 11, corrosion caused a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] LPG pipeline to fail, in [[Martin County Texas]]. One person was killed.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print</ref>
* 1988 On November 8, corrosion of a 14-inch underground pipeline owned and operated by the [[Shell Oil Company]], a predecessor of Shell Pipeline Corporation (Shell), resulted in the release of an estimated {{convert|120,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline. A pool of gasoline about {{convert|450|ft|m}} by {{convert|50|ft|m}} appeared among fields of corn and soybeans. The site of the release was in Limestone Township in Kankakee County, about {{convert|4|mi|km}} west of [[Kankakee, Illinois]]. Approximately 2,100 people live within a {{convert|1|mi|km|adj=on}} radius of the November 1988 release point.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.atsdr.cdc.gov/HAC/pha/pha.asp?docid=609&pg=1#back|title=ATSDR-PHA-HC-Shell Oil Pipeline Spill-p1|work=cdc.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On November 18, thousands of air travelers were temporarily stranded after a construction crew at [[San Francisco International Airport]] accidentally ruptured an underground jet fuel pipeline. The break, which spilled 50,000 gallons before the pipeline was shut down, cut off fuel supplies to all three of the airport's airline terminals. More than 200 flights were disrupted, officials said.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SJ&s_site=mercurynews&p_multi=SJ&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB72EDDCFCB2B2A&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=San Jose Mercury News (CA) - November 19, 1988 - 1A Front : FUEL ACCIDENT DELAYS JETS AT S.F. AIRPORT |website=Nl.newsbank.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1988 On November 25, a natural gas explosion and fire in Kansas City, Missouri, involved a break in a customer owned service line, at a threaded joint that was affected by corrosion. One person was killed and five persons injured in the explosion that severely damaged the residence.<ref name="ReferenceB"/>
* 1988 A mower hit a propane pipeline & ruptured it in [[Friendswood, Texas]] on November 28. About 4,836 barrels of propane were lost. 2 people were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267072|title=Nov. 28, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A [[Koch Industries]] and [[Ashland Oil]] subsidiary 16 inch crude oil pipeline failed near [[Dellwood, Minnesota]], spilling about {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} of crude on a farm. Snow complicated the cleanup. The leak occurred late December 1, but was not discovered until early December 2. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam fatigue crack caused the failure.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=PD&s_site=twincities&p_multi=SP&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB5D8018D83D82B&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=December 3, 1988 |title=PIPELINE RUPTURES, SPILLING CRUDE OIL |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=PD&s_site=twincities&p_multi=SP&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB5D803B2A21399&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=December 4, 1988 |title=PIPELINE PLACED BACK IN SERVICE |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1988 On Dec. 11, a natural gas pipeline outside [[Carthage, Texas]], exploded and burned, forcing residents of two nearby subdivisions to evacuate. No injuries were reported.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/>
* 1988 A 22-inch [[Shell Oil Company]] crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Vienna, Missouri]] on December 24, spilling more than {{convert|860,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil into the [[Gasconade River]]. A pipeline worker in Oklahoma failed to notice the pipeline's plummeting pressure gauges for at least two hours. 1,000 workers at a brewery were idled for 3 days, due to the pollutionof the breweries' water source. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam defect in the pipe was determined to be the cause of the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.columbiamissourian.com/stories/2010/06/21/missouri-residents-recall-gasconade-river-oil-spill/|title=Missouri residents recall Gasconade River oil spill |archive-url=https://archive.is/20130119130634/http://www.columbiamissourian.com/stories/2010/06/21/missouri-residents-recall-gasconade-river-oil-spill/ |dead-url=yes |archive-date=January 19, 2013 |accessdate=February 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SL&p_theme=sl&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB04C03916EEDAA&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM | work=St. Louis Post-Dispatch | title=Shell Says Pipeline Had Defect | date=February 11, 1989}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/assmentoftheperformanceofoldererwpipelines.pdf |format=PDF |title=An Assessment of the Performance and Reliability of Older ERW Pipelines |website=Mycommittees.api.org |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1908&dat=19890420&id=HkQrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LtUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3599,1516440|title=The Nevada Daily Mail - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1989===
* 1989 A [[Texaco]] crude oil pipeline ruptured on January 24 in [[Winkler County, Texas]] spilling over {{convert|23000|oilbbl|m3}} of oil. {{convert|6|acre|m2}} of land were covered in oil, and groundwater was contaminated.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=jCsEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA157&lpg=PA157&dq=texaco+pipeline+spill+june+1989&source=bl&ots=r90DKVtYKy&sig=kTlgb4BY5XTvMdx9g2HsJ3c7jqA&hl=en&ei=EV05TYjBMM_pgQeuu8TYCA&sa=X&oi=book_result&ct=result&resnum=1&sqi=2&ved=0CBYQ6AEwAA#v=onepage&q=texaco%20pipeline%20spill%20june%201989&f=false|title=Texas Monthly|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267116|title=Jan. 24, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On January 25, a 12-inch pipeline owned by Delhi Gas Pipeline exploded and burned near [[Lolita, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890126&id=IzVSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5324,4526753|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1989 On February 10, a natural gas explosion and fire in [[Oak Grove, Jackson County, Missouri|Oak Grove, Missouri]], involved the failure of a customer owned service line at a threaded joint. Two persons were killed and their house was destroyed in the explosion.<ref name="ReferenceB"/>
*1989 A leaking gas distribution line caused an explosion in [[Topeka, Kansas]] on March 25, killing one person. This was the latest in a string of gas distribution line failures that lead to an NTSB investigation into the regional gas company. 600,000 gas services lines were replaced as a result of the investigation.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=xcsfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=l9gEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1290,351942&dq=gathering+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A 34-inch Lakehead Pipeline ruptured on March 28, near [[Sanders, Minnesota]], spilling 300 barrels of crude oil, of which 270 were recovered.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&p_theme=mn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EFE47EB0D0FD286&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=Star Tribune Archives |website=Nl.newsbank.com |date=1989-03-28 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1989 On April 10, a [[Dow Chemical Company]] NGL pipeline in [[Amber Township, Michigan]] was being purged, by passing a plastic pipeline pig propelled by compressed air. Iron sulfide residue inside the pipeline reacted, causing an explosion that burst 20 holes through the pipeline. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19890414&id=5BRQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=61UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2787,1143511|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19890419&id=Y-8LAAAAIBAJ&sjid=61UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3754,1462156|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* '''[[San Bernardino train disaster]]''': On May 25, 1989, a [[Calnev Pipeline]] petroleum products pipeline failed, when cleanup performed after the train derailment caused damage to a petroleum products pipeline, spraying nearby homes with gasoline, which ignited shortly after the failure. Two people were killed, 31 were injured, 18 automobiles were destroyed, and 15 homes were damaged or destroyed in following fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1989/P89_5_6.pdf |title=Safety Recommendation|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007170536/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1989/P89_5_6.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.trainweb.org/KernJunction/cross.htm|title=The story behind "The Cross at the Loop"|work=trainweb.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1989-06-10/local/me-1370_1_pipeline-safety-calnev-san-bernardino | work=Los Angeles Times | first1=Kenneth | last1=Reich | first2=Marcida | last2=Dodson | title=Pipeline That Triggered Fire Reactivated : Judge in Santa Ana Says He Lacks Jurisdiction to Halt Flow | date=June 10, 1989}}</ref>
* 1989 An [[Amoco]] 6 inch crude oil gathering pipeline ruptured, near [[Craig, Colorado]] on June 2, spilling {{convert|10,000|USgal|L}} of crude into the [[Yampa River]]. Federal maintenance oversight of gathering pipelines ended in 1985.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=gP8gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=PXMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4382,1324930&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Day - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1982&dat=19890604&id=-IZGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=zTMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5648,248796|title=The Evening News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On June 6, a road grader hit a Conoco LPG pipeline, in [[Laclede COunty, Texas]]. One person was killed.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print</ref>
* 1989 A [[Mobil]] petroleum gathering pipeline spilled about 40 barrels of light oil into [[Lake Texana]] near [[Edna, Texas]] on June 27. The failure was caused by corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890627&id=gjlSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3218,5793078|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890628&id=gzlSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1851,5959427|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On July 13, an [[Enbridge]] pipeline failed in [[Pembina County, North Dakota]], resulting in 31,300 barrels of crude oil being spilled, and about $2.4 million in damages & cleanup.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267223|title=July 13, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On July 24, excavation equipment hit a petroleum products pipeline in [[Kansas City, Kansas]] neatI-70. About 693,000 gallons of product were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267231|title=July 24, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A bulldozer hit a petroleum products pipeline in a stream bed in [[Salem, Oregon]] on September 13. Gasoline entered a creek, killing fish, and forcing evacuations. About 23,000 to 30,000 gallons of gasoline were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1310&dat=19990803&id=y91WAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pusDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5128,544608|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267266|title=Sept. 13, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On October 3, the United States menhaden' fishing vessel NORTHUMBERLAND, owned and operated by the Zapata Haynie Corporation (vessel owner), was backing and maneuvering in 9 to {{convert|11|ft|m}} of water when the stern of the vessel struck and ruptured an offshore 16-inch natural gas transmission pipeline. Natural gas under 835 pounds per square inch pressure was released. An undetermined source on board the vessel ignited the gas, and within seconds, the entire vessel was engulfed in flames. The fire on the vessel burned until 4:30&nbsp;a.m. on October 4, when it burned itself out. Leaking gas from the pipeline also continued to burn until the flow of gas subsided and the fire self-extinguished about 6&nbsp;a.m. on October 4. Eleven of fourteen crew members died as a result of the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9002.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Brief |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1989 An explosion at a valve in a natural gas processing station on October 25 near [[Evanston, Wyoming]] kills one worker, and injures 4 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=2oFUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Wo8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=1977,6997775&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On November 16, propane from a storage cavern for a pipeline escaped and ignited in [[Jasper, Missouri]], forcing 1,000 people to evacuate. A rail line and a highway were also closed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nlFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AwMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6857,6112793&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A farmer hit a propane pipeline near [[Butler, Illinois]] on December 8, forcing evacuation of that town. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=hNwhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=v2MEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5684,186244&dq=phillips+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On December 18, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] petroleum pipeline failed near [[Locust Grove, Orange County, Virginia|Locust Grove, Virginia]]. {{convert|212,000|USgal|L}} of kerosene spilled into the Rapidan and Rappahannock Rivers. On New Year's Eve, following a rapid thaw and heavy rains, containment dams broke and kerosene flowed downstream toward [[Fredericksburg, Virginia]]. Fish and game were killed, the City's water supply was cut off, and drinking water had to be hauled from Stafford County for seven days. The failure was caused by cracking caused during railroad shipping of the pipe before being installed. This was the seventh major leak from Colonial Pipeline in Virginia since 1973.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.vce.org/LoosePages/OutofSight/localgovpipeline5.html|title=Out Of Sight, Out Of Mind V|work=vce.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/washingtonpost/access/72360010.html?dids=72360010:72360010&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Jan+03%2C+1990&author=Brooke+A.+Masters&pub=The+Washington+Post+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=There%27s+%60Trouble+With+That+Pipeline%27%3BKerosene+Spill+Near+Fredericksburg+Is+Latest+of+Seven+Leaks&pqatl=google | first=Brooke A. | last=Masters | title=There's 'Trouble With That Pipeline';Kerosene Spill Near Fredericksburg Is Latest of Seven Leaks | date=January 3, 1990}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1298&dat=19900915&id=KbFYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NosDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2506,3104471|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On December 29, shock waves from an explosion ruptured a 30-inch gas transmission pipeline operating at 350 psi in the [[Hell Gate]] section of [[New York City, New York]]. The rupture was 11 feet long, and escaping gas ignited, killing 2 people, injuring one other person, and destroying 2 buildings and 50 automobiles.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/texaseasterntran00netc#page/62/mode/2up|title=Texas Eastern Transmission Corporation natural gas pipeline explosion and fire, Edison, New Jersey, March 23, 1994|work=archive.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 New York City Con Edison Steam Pipe explosion, rupture killing three people in the 3rd Ave./Gramercy Park area.
===1985===
* 1985 Natural gas from a leaking line traveled through soil, and caused a massive gas explosion in [[El Paso, Texas]] on January 8. Eleven people were injured, 2 homes were destroyed, and 88 other homes were damaged by the blast.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yq1HAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XH8MAAAAIBAJ&pg=6997,2634025&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On January 26, a leaking propylene pipeline in [[Baytown, Texas]] forced the evacuation of 600 people. There was no explosion or fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ofpRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ZjQNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4555,1910638&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Mid Cities Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On February 5, a gas triggered explosion and fire destroyed 12 newly constructed condominiums in [[Twin Lakes, Wisconsin]]. A cracked gas main was the source of the gas leak, and nearby sewer work was suspected of damaging the gas line. Two firefighters were hurt extinguishing the fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19850207&id=QW4aAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ISoEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3887,5134080|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On February 22, 1985, a police patrolman on routine patrol smelled strong natural gas odors in [[Sharpsville, Pennsylvania]]. A gas serviceman was ordered to the scene. Before the serviceman arrived at the site of the reported leak, the Sharpsville Inn, and a connecting building, exploded and burned, killing two persons. Firefighters arriving on scene moments later encountered a second, smaller explosion, which injured one firefighter. The delay in the gas serviceman getting to the incident was a contributing factor.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8502.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1985 On April 5, lightning caused a computer malfunction with [[Colonial Pipeline]], resulting in a pipeline rupture that sent at least 126,000 gallons of gasoline into the [[Yellow Leaf Creek]] in [[Talladega County, Alabama]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=SjYdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sqUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6786,1884210&dq=colonial+pipeline&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1891&dat=19850408&id=YbgfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=rNcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3042,1547057|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On April 18, fumes from an NGL pipeline, under repair near [[Baxter Pass, Colorado]], killed one pipeline repair worker, & injured 9 others. During a lawsuit dealing with this accidents, it was claimed "The "safety" procedures used were crude at best, as the workers without lifelines were directed to hold their breath and go down into the ditch for about 30 seconds to work, before coming back out of the ditch for air."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19850419&id=EschAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5p0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=1925,4504430|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://law.justia.com/cases/wyoming/supreme-court/1988/122028.html|title=Wessel v. Mapco, Inc.|work=Justia Law|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A 30-inch diameter gas pipeline operating at about 960 psi, weakened by atmospheric corrosion, ruptured, and tore out about {{convert|29|ft|m}} of the carrier pipe, blew apart about {{convert|16|ft|m}} of a 36-inch casing pipe, blasted an opening across Kentucky State Highway 90, and cut out a pear-shaped crater approximately {{convert|90|ft|m}} long, {{convert|38|ft|m}} wide, and {{convert|12|ft|m}} deep near [[Beaumont, Kentucky]]. 5 people were killed in one home, and 3 injured. The fireball from the incident could be seen 20 miles away.(April 27, 1985)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_6.pdf |title=Safety Recommendations|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622080222/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1985/P85_6.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=-PQrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AW0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=3025,7574446&dq=family+killed+by+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On May 10, a [[Mohave County, Arizona]] road crew hit a 2-inch gas pipeline while reinstalling a fallen stop sign, in [[Butler, Arizona]]. During repairs to the gas line, a flash fire ignited, injuring 2 fire fighters, and a Southern Union Gas Co. worker.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=943&dat=19850512&id=XsZPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=g1MDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5490,1172063|title=Mohave Daily Miner - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 Workers on the extension of the North Dallas Tollway ruptured a 12-inch gasoline pipeline on June 19, causing a massive gasoline spill along a creek bed north of [[Dallas, Texas]]. The gasoline later ignited. One person had moderate injuries, several office buildings were damaged by fire, and some automobiles were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KdA9AAAAIBAJ&sjid=RjcMAAAAIBAJ&pg=6652,8009279&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Mid Cities Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On June 20, a telephone cable installing crew broke a 10 gas gathering pipeline, in [[Paradise, Texas]], releasing gas, that ignited 20 seconds later. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19850621&id=PiZSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vTUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4134,2361312|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On July 23, in a rural area about {{convert|8|mi|km}} south of [[Kaycee, Wyoming]], a girth weld cracked during a pipeline re-coating project on a 23-year-old, 8-inch pipeline. The cracked girth weld allowed the release, atomization of, and ignition of aircraft turbine fuel under 430 pounds pressure, killing one person, burning six other persons, and destroying construction equipment.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/_layouts/ntsb.recsearch/Recommendation.aspx?Rec=P-86-012 |title=Safety Recommendation P-86-012 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eZozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LYQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5815,3641705&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=336&dat=19850724&id=eZozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LYQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5815,3641705|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A gasoline leak of up to {{convert|42,000|USgal|L}} from a ruptured 10-inch pipeline ignited, on August, 2 in [[Indianapolis, Indiana]], causing a {{convert|200|ft|m|adj=on}} high fireball that killed three people, and injured 3 others working to clean up the spill along a creek.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9C07E4D91038F930A3575BC0A963948260|title=AROUND THE NATION -    3 WORKERS KILLED BY FIRE IN INDIANA GASOLINE SPILL - NYTimes.com|date=3 August 1985|work=nytimes.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=H9FGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=_HsMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5329,298801&dq=ammonia+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Times-Union - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On August 22, a vessel was being filled with Liquefied Natural Gas (LNG), when it burst, leading to a flash fire that burned 6 people, at a gas facility in [[Pinson, Alabama]].<ref name=autogenerated1 />
* 1985 On September 23, a 12-inch diameter gasoline pipeline fitting was hit by a backhoe, and sprayed about {{convert|35,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline {{convert|45|ft|m}} into the air in [[Staten Island, New York]]. There were evacuations, but no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=YQshAAAAIBAJ&sjid=d3IFAAAAIBAJ&pg=2854,2186745&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Schenectady Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A Texas Eastern Transmission Corp. natural gas pipeline exploded near Hillsboro in [[Fleming County, Kentucky]] on October 26. There were two injuries reported.<ref name="google6683">{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=BoQ_AAAAIBAJ&sjid=Q1UMAAAAIBAJ&pg=6683,125730&dq=pipeline+accident&hl=en|title=Portsmouth Daily Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=G7JcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pFgNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4759%2C284017|title=Portsmouth Daily Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On November 1, a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline exploded and burned near [[Rowenna, Pennsylvania]], shooting flames 200 feet into the air, and causing dozens of residents to evacuate. A gas metering station and pressure regulator were also damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19851102&id=JU8gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=bsgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5086,157952|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1985 On November 28, Olympic Pipeline spilled about 31,000 gallons of jet fuel at [[SeattleTacoma International Airport]], due to a valve being left open. The fuel entered a storm drain, that led to the [[Des Moines River]], killing fish and wildlife for 2.5 miles. Later, the company was fined $15,000 for the spill by the Washington Department of Ecology.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19851130&id=1rUzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oTIHAAAAIBAJ&pg=3234,3647862|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1345&dat=19860131&id=J_5LAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wPkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3474,3370169|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On December 6, a natural gas explosion and fire destroyed the River Restaurant in [[Derby, Connecticut]]. Gas escaping from a broken gas main at a pressure of about 1&nbsp;pound per square inch had escaped, migrated into the restaurant basement, ignited, exploded, and burned. Of the 18 persons inside the restaurant at the time, 6 were killed and 12 were injured; 1 passerby and 1 firefighter were also injured. After the accident the street adjacent to the restaurant was excavated where a 24-inch sewer system had just been installed; An 87-year-old, 3-inch, cast-iron natural gas main was found broken.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_16.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation  |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007142959/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_16.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov/cast_iron/|title=Page has moved|work=dot.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 On December 5, a Central Florida Pipeline products line burst in [[Lake Alfred, Florida]], spilling about 40,000 gallons of gasoline. The landowner affected later sued the pipeline for failure to remove contaminated soil. There were no injuries or fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1346&dat=19870201&id=_ahOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dvsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2352,91805|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1985 A water Department crew hit the cap of an illegal tap into a Four Corners crude oil pipeline on December 18, near [[Cabazon, California]]. About 47,000 gallons of crude were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19851219&id=xI9TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=soYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3315,3379748|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
===1986===
* 1986 On January 31, a 14-inch [[Sunoco]] pipeline began leaking gasoline in [[Mercer County, New Jersey]], which then spilled into the [[Delaware and Raritan Canal]]. The spilled gasoline exploded and burned along a 2,500 foot portion of the canal. People were evacuated from homes, and a nearby church.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19860201&id=wK5dAAAAIBAJ&sjid=o10NAAAAIBAJ&pg=3826,10669|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On February 10, construction crew cut through a gas pipeline in [[Lakeland, Florida]], resulting in about 175 people being evacuated from mobile homes and businesses for 2 hours. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1346&dat=19860211&id=k7cwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pvsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6485,4338007&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 A 30-inch Texas Eastern gas pipeline ruptured, due to corrosion, near [[Lancaster, Kentucky]]. 3 people had serious burns, and 5 others had lesser injuries. External corrosion made worse by difficulties of [[Cathodic protection]] in rocky soil was the cause. A senior vice president for operations and engineering with Texas Eastern Gas Pipeline Co., said tests on the Garrard County line last September showed the line needed immediate replacement. It was the third explosion on the Texas Eastern pipeline system in Kentucky in the previous 10 months, leading the Kentucky PSC to call for pressure reductions on the Texas Eastern system.(February 21, 1986)<ref name="google6683"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_14.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007143228/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1986/P86_14.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=yzAqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WUcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3876,3756877&dq=sun+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=Park City Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 An 8-inch high-pressure petroleum pipeline ruptured in [[Muskegon County, Michigan]] on February 22, spilling gasoline into creeks.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mlive.com/opinion/muskegon/index.ssf/2011/01/editorial_citizens_must_keep_p.html|title=Editorial: Citizens must keep pressure on for monitoring, safety|work=MLive.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On February 24, a natural gas transmission pipeline split for 40 feet along its longitudinal seam in [[Case, Arkansas]]. Examining the pipe after the accident revealed lack of fusion, a known issue with LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] pipe used there. The pipeline has experienced 3 other such seam failures on that pipeline since 1975.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1987/PAR8702.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=July 16, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622103738/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1987/PAR8702.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1986 A backhoe snagged a natural gas distribution line in [[Fort Worth, Texas]], causing a break that leaked gas into an unoccupied building. Later, that building exploded, injuring 22 people, destroying the unoccupied building, and damaging 40 other buildings. 57 automobiles in the unoccupied building were damaged or destroyed. (March 12, 1986)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_29_33.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622095948/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_29_33.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1986 A new water main was being installed in [[Chicago Heights, Illinois]] on March 13. While excavating, an active gas service line was snagged. Gas company crews responded to the wrong site, causing delays in getting the leaking gas line shut down. Just as crews finished closing the valve on the leaking line, a nearby house exploded, and began to burn; One of the two persons inside that house was killed, and the other was injured. Two neighboring houses were damaged, and one gas company employee, two construction crew members, and four persons in the general area, were injured by the explosion and subsequent fire. Although gas company personnel arrived on the scene approximately 10&nbsp;minutes before the explosion and shut off the gas at the meter, neither they nor the contractor's crew had made an effort to warn or evacuate the residents of the house.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_35_38.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007163131/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1987/P87_35_38.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1986 A gravel company endloader ruptured a Lakehead Pipeline crude oil pipeline on April 12 near [[Elgin, Illinois]], spill about 525,000 gallons of crude, and causing a "geyser" of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=HN&p_theme=hn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB0964F5939AD84&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date%3AD&s_trackval=GooglePM|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130129211248/http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=HN&p_theme=hn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB0964F5939AD84&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date%3AD&s_trackval=GooglePM|deadurl=yes|title=Suburban Chicago Newspapers - Search Results|date=29 January 2013|archivedate=29 January 2013|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1986 A backhoe ruptured an Olympic Pipeline line on May 8, south of [[Seattle, Washington]]. About 1,974 barrels of diesel fuel were spilled, with some of it entering the [[Green River (Duwamish River)|Green River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1345&dat=19860512&id=hkJYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=z_kDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3867,2803687|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1986 On May 14, a 6-inch [[Amoco]] pipeline, damaged by some type of arcing, leaked about 380 barrels of gasoline in [[Elmhurst, Illinois]]. Some of the gasoline fumes exploded in a nearby home, causing serious damage. Concerns about the lack of evacuations were raised later on. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1986-05-22/news/8602060804_1_pipeline-amoco-evacuation | work=Chicago Tribune | first=Neil H | last=Mehler | title=Probe Urged In Elmhurst Gasoline Leak | date=May 22, 1986}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266230|title=May 14, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On June 28, a pipeline ruptured and spilled diesel fuel into [[Trail Creek (Lake Michigan)|Trail Creek]] in [[Michigan City, Indiana]]. The fuel later ignited. Thousands of fish were killed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=56tUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tDsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2711,2893734&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Rochester Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 Early on July 8, a [[Williams Companies]] petroleum products pipeline ruptured in [[Mounds View, Minnesota]]. Gasoline at 1,434 psi sprayed a residential area around 4:20&nbsp;am local time, then ignited. A woman and her 7-year-old daughter suffered fatal burns, at least two others were injured, and many homes damaged or destroyed. Confusion by the pipeline company led to a delay in shutting down the pipeline. Electrical resistance welded ([[Electric resistance welding|ERW]]) seam failure caused the rupture. Prior to this accident, this pipeline, installed in 1957, had 16 seam failures during hydrostatic testing, and 7 seam failures during operations until 1984. In 1984, 16 more seams failed during a hydrostatic test. Problems with cathodic protection were also noted before the 1986 accident. During a hydrostatic test of this pipeline following the accident, 3 ERW seams failed. Studies of available data by OPS staff in early 1988 showed that ERW seams have been involved in 145 service failures in both hazardous liquid and natural gas pipelines since 1970 to early 1988, and that of these failures, all but 2 occurred on pipe manufactured prior to 1970.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR8702.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board : Pipeline Accident Report |date=July 8, 1986 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.startribune.com/local/12564991.html |title=July 9, 1986: Gasoline pipeline explodes in Mounds View|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150427142920/http://www.startribune.com/local/12564991.html |archivedate=April 27, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Advisory%20Bulletin%20Files/xALN-88-01.pdf |format=PDF |title=Alert Notice : Recent findings relative to factors contributing to operational failures of pipelines constructed with ERW prior to 1970. |website=Phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.startribune.com/templates/Print_This_Story?sid=12564991|title=July 9, 1986: Gasoline pipeline explodes in Mounds View|work=startribune.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="mycommittees.api.org">{{cite web|url=http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/electricresistanceweldfailures.pdf |format=PDF |title=Electric Resistance Weld Pipe Failures on Hazardous Liquid and Gas Transmission Pipelines |website=Mycommittees.api.org |accessdate=2016-01-18 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304094851/http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/electricresistanceweldfailures.pdf |archivedate=2016-03-04 |df= }}</ref>
* 1986 A [[Southern Natural Gas]] transmission pipeline failed and burned, in a compressor station, near [[Prattville, Alabama]], on July 12. The fire spread by melting flange gaskets on 2 other gas transmission pipelines in the station. 4 homes and several cars were destroyed in the following fire, with flames reaching {{convert|300|ft|m}} high. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Z5ItAAAAIBAJ&sjid=F8kEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4307,1957194&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On July 22, a leak at an underground propane storage facility in [[Petal, Mississippi]] exploded, causing a massive fire, injuring 14 people, and forcing 200 people to evacuate. A crater 260 feet in diameter and 37 feet deep was made by the explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=e_QaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Y0cEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5337,4268109&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=qbBOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=cPsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7010,2867730&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Lakeland Ledger - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.osha.gov/pls/imis/establishment.inspection_detail?id=101557098|title=Inspection Detail|work=osha.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 Between 800 and 1200 residents were evacuated in [[East Chicago, Indiana]], after a gasoline tank at a pipeline Terminal ruptured on September 4. 28 people were overcome by gasoline fumes. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=W49TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oIYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4801,1802743&dq=phillips+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 A CENEX 8 inch petroleum products pipeline failed near [[Billings, Montana]] on September 4, spilling gasoline, and causing the evacuation of nearby businesses. About 29,400 gallons of gasoline spilled. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ekJYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=zPkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7003,1306572&dq=yellowstone+pipeline+leaks&hl=en|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="projects.propublica.org">{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266320|title=Sept. 4, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="projects.propublica.org"/>
* 1986 On September 4, a tank failed at a [[Phillips Petroleum Company]] facility in [[East Chicago, Indiana]], forcing 800 to 1,200 residents near by to evacuate, and spilling 55,000 barrels of gasoline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19860905&id=W49TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oIYDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4801,1802743|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On September 8, an [[Amoco]] gas condensate pipeline failed under the [[Red River of the South|Red River]] near [[Dexter, Texas]]. Fumes from the leaking pipeline sent 14 people to hospitals for treatment.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=F5I9AAAAIBAJ&sjid=4DUMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5284,272093&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Bonham Daily Favorite - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsok.com/leak-in-pipeline-blamed-for-fumes/article/2159247|title=Leak in Pipeline Blamed for Fumes|work=NewsOK.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 In October, a 21-inch long crack on an 14-inch [[Sunoco]] petroleum products pipeline in [[King of Prussia, Pennsylvania]] spilled about 220,000 gallons of gasoline, forcing evacuations, including about 900 students from a middle school. The failure was near a previously repaired area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19861011&id=iXRiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=E3cNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5709,1578649|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266349|title=Oct. 7, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19861008&id=pV4tAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TtoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3177,1690511|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On November 13, a gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Stinnett, Texas]], killing one person. The pipeline has been installed in 1982.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266387|title=Nov. 13, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On December 6 in the early morning hours a 30-inch natural gas pipe line exploded on the north edge of the [[Ross Barnett Reservoir]] (Pelahatchie Bay) in Mississippi, near [[Jackson, Mississippi|Jackson]]. There were no casualties. The blast was seen by airline pilots as far away as Houston TX and Nashville TN.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://thereznews.blogspot.com/2011/01/explosion.html|title=Ross Barnett Reservoir|work=thereznews.blogspot.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1986 On December 25, an [[Amoco]] pipeline ruptured, and spilled furnace oil into the [[Des Plaines River]] near [[Chicago, Illinois]]. About 429 barrels of furnace oil were spilled. External corrosion was the cause of the pipeline failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=pblQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qvMMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5006,3701180&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Lewiston Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266426|title=Dec. 25, 1986 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
===1987===
* 1987 On January 30, natural gas leaking from a pipeline under repair in [[Colorado Springs, Colorado]], ignited, sending flames 45 feet into the air, and injuring four people.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.apnewsarchive.com/1990/Other-Recent-Pipeline-Accidents-With-AM-Pipeline-Explosion/id-4ddc2e27adf7538512f63be3a726e138|title=Other Recent Pipeline Accidents With AM-Pipeline Explosion|work=apnewsarchive.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A petroleum pipeline ruptured and burned, near [[Corsicana, Texas]] on March 12, forcing the closure of an Interstate highway, and cause some evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KShAAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uVgMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3718,5358666&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Vindicator - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A work crew burning the remains of a house near [[Ladysmith, Virginia]] ruptured a nearby petroleum products pipeline with a bulldozer on March 26, igniting diesel fuel from the line. 2 of the worker were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=zzgwAAAAIBAJ&sjid=hIsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3925,888188&dq=pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On April 4, an LPG pipeline exploded at a Terminal in [[Iowa City, Iowa]]. Due to the fire spreading to a pipeline for nearby underground gas storage, residents within a 2 1/2 mile radius of the Terminal were evacuated for a time. The fire burned until April 20. The cause was an [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure in a pipeline. During a hydrostatic test of that pipeline, 20 more pipeline segment seams failed.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=ASFRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=K88MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1518,670078&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=DCFRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=K88MAAAAIBAJ&pg=3030,3587912&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 In [[Odessa, Texas]], on April 18, a crude oil pipeline burst into flames, destroying nine mobile homes and two cars. The fire started under a mobile home on Andrews Highway. The Texas Railroad Commission stated that gases within the crude corroded and weakened the 10-inch 60-year-old pipe. When the line split, it spewed oil into the fire, fueling the blaze and causing dense black smoke that choked firefighters and bystanders.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oaoa.com/75th_anniversary/article_47fdc83a-5332-11e5-bca5-7717d7feedac.html|title=1987: Meet Baby Jessica, economy improves|work=Odessa American|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 A [[Mobil]] pipeline ruptured near [[Lebec, California]] on June 8, spilling about 2,500 barrels of crude oil. The failure was from external corrosion of the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266572|title=June 8, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1987 On June 11, a "rock ripper" at a construction site punctured a 32-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] petroleum products pipeline in [[Centreville, Virginia]]. Gasoline sprayed from the rupture, but there was no fire. More than {{convert|15,500|USgal|L}} of gasoline were released. Thirteen emergency response personnel suffered from exposure to the gasoline fumes.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1996/SIR9602.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101205073217/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1996/SIR9602.pdf |archivedate=December 5, 2010 }}</ref>
* 1987 An [[Amoco]] pipeline failed in [[Florence, Michigan]] on June 11, spilling 24,000 barrels of petroleum.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266574|title=June 11, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On June 12, a petroleum products pipeline ruptured near [[Harwood, North Dakota]]. 289 barrels of fuel oil were spilled. There were no injuries. Investigation showed this pipeline failed at a low frequency Electric Resistance Welding ([[Electric resistance welding|ERW]]) seam. Further testing after this accident lead to 5 other LF-ERW failures along this pipeline in Minnesota and North Dakota.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf|title=VIA CERTIFIED MAIL (RETTJRI). RECEIPT REOUESTED |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028014558/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266577|title=June 12, 1987 - ProPublica|work=Propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1987 Construction equipment hit a LPG/NGL pipeline near [[Rochester, Iowa]] on June 26, killing one person, and injuring 2 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266589|title=June 26, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 3, a Yellowstone Pipeline Company line failed from an unspecified flaw in the pipe, in [[Montana]]. About 162,000 gallons of petroleum product were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266597 |title=July 3, 1987 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1987-07-03 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 24, a fishing vessel, working in shallow waters off of [[Empire, Louisiana]], the Fishing vessel Sea Chief, struck and ruptured an 8" natural gas liquids pipeline operating at 480 psi. The resulting explosion killed two crew members. Divers investigating found that the pipe, installed in 1968, was covered with only 6" of soft mud, having lost its original {{convert|3|ft|m|adj=on}} cover of sediments.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epd.gov.hk/eia/register/report/eiareport/eia_1252006/html/eiareport/Part2/Section13/Sec2_13_AnnexB.htm|title=EIA Report - Part 2 Section13 Annex B|work=epd.gov.hk|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On July 23, a construction crew working on an Interstate 90 project east of [[Coeur d'Alene, Idaho]] struck the 10-inch diameter Yellowstone Pipeline, causing a leak that sprayed out over 27,000 gallons of gasoline. The pipeline was supposed to have 30&nbsp;inches of soil cover, but had only 2&nbsp;inches of cover. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=o5ZMAAAAIBAJ&sjid=svoDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5890,1950592&dq=yellowstone+pipeline+leaks&hl=en|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266613|title=July 23, 1987 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1987 On August 5, gas leak on a busy road in [[Wilmington, North Carolina]] suddenly ignited, while gas company workers were trying to plug that leak, burning them and firefighters on standby. 19 people were burned, with a Fire Department Assistant Chief later dying from the burns he received.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.starnewsonline.com/article/20120110/ARTICLES/120119970/-1/news38?Title=Firefighters-raise-money-for-local-memorial#fb-root |title=Firefighters raise money for local memorial |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266628 |title=Aug. 5, 1987 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1987-08-05 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1987 On September 8, 3 pipeline workers were hurt, when a butane pipeline they were working on exploded near [[Kemah, Texas]].<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/><ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1987-09-10/news/mn-7201_1_pipeline-blast | work=Los Angeles Times | title=3 Hurt in Pipeline Blast | date=September 10, 1987}}</ref>
* 1987 4 pipeline workers were hurt while working on a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline in [[Martin, Kentucky]] on October 19. A rubber seal inside a steel collar failed, allowing 2 sections of pipeline to separate. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=266&dat=19871029&id=xR8uAAAAIBAJ&sjid=h9wFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3343,7204741|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
===1988===
* 1988 On January 5, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] mainline ruptured, spilling about 100,000 gallons of home heating oil in [[Deptford, New Jersey]]. The cause of the pipeline failure was corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://articles.philly.com/1988-01-15/news/26282729_1_oil-pipeline-colonial-pipeline-pipeline-burst|title=Deptford To Check Process Behind Pipeline's Permit|work=philly-archives|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pipelinesafetytrust.com/docs/ops_doc2.pdf |format=PDF |title=1996 Colonial Pipeline Task Force : Final Report |website=Pipelinesafetytrust.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1988 The rupture of a large interstate gas line at Pocono Ridge development in [[Lehman Township, Pike County, Pennsylvania|Lehman Township, Pennsylvania]], left a crater about {{convert|8|ft|m}} deep and ejected a {{convert|6|ft|m|adj=on}} section of pipe over the treetops before it landed 50&nbsp;yards away. One hundred thirty people were evacuated. No one was injured.<ref name="poconorecord1"/>
* 1988 On January 18, a natural gas explosion destroyed the building housing the K&W Cafeteria and the lobby of the Sheraton Motor Inn at [[Winston-Salem, North Carolina]].
