Two adjoining motel wings suffered structural damage. Of the four persons in the lobby/cafeteria building at the time of the explosion, three sustained minor injuries. The fourth person sustained a fractured ankle. One motel guest also sustained minor cuts.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1988/P88_10.pdf |title=Safety Recommendation|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007170305/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1988/P88_10.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1988 On February 8, an offshore pipeline near [[Galveston, Texas]], that may have been damaged by an anchor, ruptured, spilling about {{convert|15576|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil into the Gulf.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gomr.boemre.gov/PDFs/1989/89-0102.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120316112409/http://www.gomr.boemre.gov/PDFs/1989/89-0102.pdf |archivedate=March 16, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266825|title=Feb. 8, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On February 17, a [[Sunoco]] pipeline near [[Pleasant Township, Seneca County, Ohio]] ruptured, spilling over 200,000 gallons of [[toluene]], with about 173,000 gallons of it being lost. 4,200 people had to evacuate their homes for a time.  The cause was previous third party damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19880224&id=aj5QAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5g0EAAAAIBAJ&pg=7048,3828963|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266843|title=Feb. 17, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19880313&id=hFBPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=6gIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1808,2576831|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On March 19, 130 people were evacuated from their homes, after a vehicle hit a valve on a [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline in [[Hempfield, Pennsylvania]]. There was no gas ignition.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1129&dat=19880321&id=l9RRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=8m0DAAAAIBAJ&pg=3650,6512245|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On April 9, a 20-inch crude oil pipeline failed in a [[Peoria County, Illinois]] subdivision. About {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} of crude were spilled, contaminating 2 private lakes.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=gqFdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=51wNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6734,2215943&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A backhoe hit a 10 gas pipeline in [[Springfield, Massachusetts]], on April 18. Two Interstate freeways were shut down, and, 125 to 150 people were evacuated for a time from bearby businesses.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1928&dat=19880419&id=uDspAAAAIBAJ&sjid=fWUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3091,3674834|title=The Lewiston Daily Sun - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1988 A Kaneb Pipeline Terminal had a spill of 20,000 gallons of gasoline, on April 26, in [[Milford, Iowa]]. Operator error was given as the cause of the spill.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1907&dat=19880525&id=pVsrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qdgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1360,5277238|title=The Daily Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/266898|title=April 26, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A pair of MAPCO LPG/NGL pipelines failed in an explosion south of [[Topeka, Kansas]], on July 22. 200 nearby residents had to be evacuated, and there was serious damage to US Route 75 nearby from the explosion & following fire. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam selective corrosion failure in one of the pipelines caused the failure.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=S4oyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uOYFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5501,4570580&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On August 31, a gas company crew struck and ruptured a fitting on a 4-inch plastic gas main in [[Green Oaks, Illinois]]. While the crew was attempting to excavate a nearby valve to shut off the flow of gas, the backhoe struck an unmarked power cable. The gas ignited and four gas company employees were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/recs/letters/1989/P89_7_8.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100612084408/http://www.ntsb.gov/Recs/letters/1989/P89_7_8.pdf |archivedate=June 12, 2010 }}</ref>
* 1988 A crude oil pipeline ruptured, spilling about 132,000 gallons of crude oil in [[Encino, California]] on September 10. The crude flowed into storm drains, and then into the [[Los Angeles River]]. Electrical interference to [[Cathodic protection]] from other pipelines was suspected to have cause the corrosion that caused the failure. The crude oil pipeline was on top of a steel water pipeline, which would directly interfere with Cathodic protection efforts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.is/20120723163831/http://news.google.com/newspapers?id=jEYjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5csFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6111,2547117&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en |title=Pipe leak slimes river|website=Archive.is|accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| | title=Local News in Brief Exterior Corrosion Blamed in Oil Leak | date=September 15, 1988}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| * 1988 On September 16, a natural gas explosion in Overland Park, Kansas, involved gas leaking from corrosion holes in the customer-owned line. Gas migrated underground to the house and was ignited. The house was destroyed and the four residents were injured.<ref name="ReferenceB">{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/_layouts/ntsb.research/Recommendation.aspx|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=May 8, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150528231014/http://www.ntsb.gov/_layouts/ntsb.research/Recommendation.aspx |archivedate=May 28, 2015 }}</ref>
* 1988 On October 9, third party damage to a Yellowstone Pipeline Company line caused the line to fail, near [[Garrison, Montana]]. About 260,000 gallons of petroleum products were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267027 |title=Oct. 9, 1988 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1988-10-09 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1988 On October 11, corrosion caused a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] LPG pipeline to fail, in [[Martin County Texas]]. One person was killed.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print</ref>
* 1988 On November 8, corrosion of a 14-inch underground pipeline owned and operated by the [[Shell Oil Company]], a predecessor of Shell Pipeline Corporation (Shell), resulted in the release of an estimated {{convert|120,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline. A pool of gasoline about {{convert|450|ft|m}} by {{convert|50|ft|m}} appeared among fields of corn and soybeans. The site of the release was in Limestone Township in Kankakee County, about {{convert|4|mi|km}} west of [[Kankakee, Illinois]]. Approximately 2,100 people live within a {{convert|1|mi|km|adj=on}} radius of the November 1988 release point.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.atsdr.cdc.gov/HAC/pha/pha.asp?docid=609&pg=1#back|title=ATSDR-PHA-HC-Shell Oil Pipeline Spill-p1|work=cdc.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 On November 18, thousands of air travelers were temporarily stranded after a construction crew at [[San Francisco International Airport]] accidentally ruptured an underground jet fuel pipeline. The break, which spilled 50,000 gallons before the pipeline was shut down, cut off fuel supplies to all three of the airport's airline terminals. More than 200 flights were disrupted, officials said.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SJ&s_site=mercurynews&p_multi=SJ&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB72EDDCFCB2B2A&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=San Jose Mercury News (CA) - November 19, 1988 - 1A Front : FUEL ACCIDENT DELAYS JETS AT S.F. AIRPORT |website=Nl.newsbank.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1988 On November 25, a natural gas explosion and fire in Kansas City, Missouri, involved a break in a customer owned service line, at a threaded joint that was affected by corrosion. One person was killed and five persons injured in the explosion that severely damaged the residence.<ref name="ReferenceB"/>
* 1988 A mower hit a propane pipeline & ruptured it in [[Friendswood, Texas]] on November 28. About 4,836 barrels of propane were lost. 2 people were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267072|title=Nov. 28, 1988 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1988 A [[Koch Industries]] and [[Ashland Oil]] subsidiary 16 inch crude oil pipeline failed near [[Dellwood, Minnesota]], spilling about {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} of crude on a farm. Snow complicated the cleanup. The leak occurred late December 1, but was not discovered until early December 2. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam fatigue crack caused the failure.<ref name="mycommittees.api.org"/><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=PD&s_site=twincities&p_multi=SP&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB5D8018D83D82B&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=December 3, 1988 |title=PIPELINE RUPTURES, SPILLING CRUDE OIL |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=PD&s_site=twincities&p_multi=SP&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB5D803B2A21399&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=December 4, 1988 |title=PIPELINE PLACED BACK IN SERVICE |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1988 On Dec. 11, a natural gas pipeline outside [[Carthage, Texas]], exploded and burned, forcing residents of two nearby subdivisions to evacuate. No injuries were reported.<ref name="apnewsarchive.com"/>
* 1988 A 22-inch [[Shell Oil Company]] crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Vienna, Missouri]] on December 24, spilling more than {{convert|860,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil into the [[Gasconade River]]. A pipeline worker in Oklahoma failed to notice the pipeline's plummeting pressure gauges for at least two hours. 1,000 workers at a brewery were idled for 3 days, due to the pollutionof the breweries' water source. An [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam defect in the pipe was determined to be the cause of the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.columbiamissourian.com/stories/2010/06/21/missouri-residents-recall-gasconade-river-oil-spill/|title=Missouri residents recall Gasconade River oil spill |archive-url=https://archive.is/20130119130634/http://www.columbiamissourian.com/stories/2010/06/21/missouri-residents-recall-gasconade-river-oil-spill/ |dead-url=yes |archive-date=January 19, 2013 |accessdate=February 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SL&p_theme=sl&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB04C03916EEDAA&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM | work=St. Louis Post-Dispatch | title=Shell Says Pipeline Had Defect | date=February 11, 1989}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/ecs/sc5/Technical%20Papers/assmentoftheperformanceofoldererwpipelines.pdf |format=PDF |title=An Assessment of the Performance and Reliability of Older ERW Pipelines |website=Mycommittees.api.org |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1908&dat=19890420&id=HkQrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=LtUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3599,1516440|title=The Nevada Daily Mail - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
===1989===
* 1989 A [[Texaco]] crude oil pipeline ruptured on January 24 in [[Winkler County, Texas]] spilling over {{convert|23000|oilbbl|m3}} of oil. {{convert|6|acre|m2}} of land were covered in oil, and groundwater was contaminated.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=jCsEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA157&lpg=PA157&dq=texaco+pipeline+spill+june+1989&source=bl&ots=r90DKVtYKy&sig=kTlgb4BY5XTvMdx9g2HsJ3c7jqA&hl=en&ei=EV05TYjBMM_pgQeuu8TYCA&sa=X&oi=book_result&ct=result&resnum=1&sqi=2&ved=0CBYQ6AEwAA#v=onepage&q=texaco%20pipeline%20spill%20june%201989&f=false|title=Texas Monthly|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267116|title=Jan. 24, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On January 25, a 12-inch pipeline owned by Delhi Gas Pipeline exploded and burned near [[Lolita, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890126&id=IzVSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5324,4526753|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1989 On February 10, a natural gas explosion and fire in [[Oak Grove, Jackson County, Missouri|Oak Grove, Missouri]], involved the failure of a customer owned service line at a threaded joint. Two persons were killed and their house was destroyed in the explosion.<ref name="ReferenceB"/>
*1989 A leaking gas distribution line caused an explosion in [[Topeka, Kansas]] on March 25, killing one person. This was the latest in a string of gas distribution line failures that lead to an NTSB investigation into the regional gas company. 600,000 gas services lines were replaced as a result of the investigation.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=xcsfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=l9gEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1290,351942&dq=gathering+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A 34-inch Lakehead Pipeline ruptured on March 28, near [[Sanders, Minnesota]], spilling 300 barrels of crude oil, of which 270 were recovered.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&p_theme=mn&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EFE47EB0D0FD286&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=Star Tribune Archives |website=Nl.newsbank.com |date=1989-03-28 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1989 On April 10, a [[Dow Chemical Company]] NGL pipeline in [[Amber Township, Michigan]] was being purged, by passing a plastic pipeline pig propelled by compressed air. Iron sulfide residue inside the pipeline reacted, causing an explosion that burst 20 holes through the pipeline. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19890414&id=5BRQAAAAIBAJ&sjid=61UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2787,1143511|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19890419&id=Y-8LAAAAIBAJ&sjid=61UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3754,1462156|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* '''[[San Bernardino train disaster]]''': On May 25, 1989, a [[Calnev Pipeline]] petroleum products pipeline failed, when cleanup performed after the train derailment caused damage to a petroleum products pipeline, spraying nearby homes with gasoline, which ignited shortly after the failure. Two people were killed, 31 were injured, 18 automobiles were destroyed, and 15 homes were damaged or destroyed in following fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1989/P89_5_6.pdf |title=Safety Recommendation|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007170536/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1989/P89_5_6.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.trainweb.org/KernJunction/cross.htm|title=The story behind "The Cross at the Loop"|work=trainweb.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1989-06-10/local/me-1370_1_pipeline-safety-calnev-san-bernardino | work=Los Angeles Times | first1=Kenneth | last1=Reich | first2=Marcida | last2=Dodson | title=Pipeline That Triggered Fire Reactivated : Judge in Santa Ana Says He Lacks Jurisdiction to Halt Flow | date=June 10, 1989}}</ref>
* 1989 An [[Amoco]] 6 inch crude oil gathering pipeline ruptured, near [[Craig, Colorado]] on June 2, spilling {{convert|10,000|USgal|L}} of crude into the [[Yampa River]]. Federal maintenance oversight of gathering pipelines ended in 1985.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=gP8gAAAAIBAJ&sjid=PXMFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4382,1324930&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Day - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1982&dat=19890604&id=-IZGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=zTMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=5648,248796|title=The Evening News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On June 6, a road grader hit a Conoco LPG pipeline, in [[Laclede COunty, Texas]]. One person was killed.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print</ref>
* 1989 A [[Mobil]] petroleum gathering pipeline spilled about 40 barrels of light oil into [[Lake Texana]] near [[Edna, Texas]] on June 27. The failure was caused by corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890627&id=gjlSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3218,5793078|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19890628&id=gzlSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1851,5959427|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On July 13, an [[Enbridge]] pipeline failed in [[Pembina County, North Dakota]], resulting in 31,300 barrels of crude oil being spilled, and about $2.4 million in damages & cleanup.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267223|title=July 13, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On July 24, excavation equipment hit a petroleum products pipeline in [[Kansas City, Kansas]] neatI-70. About 693,000 gallons of product were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267231|title=July 24, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A bulldozer hit a petroleum products pipeline in a stream bed in [[Salem, Oregon]] on September 13. Gasoline entered a creek, killing fish, and forcing evacuations. About 23,000 to 30,000 gallons of gasoline were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1310&dat=19990803&id=y91WAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pusDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5128,544608|title=Eugene Register-Guard - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267266|title=Sept. 13, 1989 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On October 3, the United States menhaden' fishing vessel NORTHUMBERLAND, owned and operated by the Zapata Haynie Corporation (vessel owner), was backing and maneuvering in 9 to {{convert|11|ft|m}} of water when the stern of the vessel struck and ruptured an offshore 16-inch natural gas transmission pipeline. Natural gas under 835 pounds per square inch pressure was released. An undetermined source on board the vessel ignited the gas, and within seconds, the entire vessel was engulfed in flames. The fire on the vessel burned until 4:30&nbsp;a.m. on October 4, when it burned itself out. Leaking gas from the pipeline also continued to burn until the flow of gas subsided and the fire self-extinguished about 6&nbsp;a.m. on October 4. Eleven of fourteen crew members died as a result of the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9002.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Brief |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1989 An explosion at a valve in a natural gas processing station on October 25 near [[Evanston, Wyoming]] kills one worker, and injures 4 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=2oFUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Wo8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=1977,6997775&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On November 16, propane from a storage cavern for a pipeline escaped and ignited in [[Jasper, Missouri]], forcing 1,000 people to evacuate. A rail line and a highway were also closed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=nlFPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AwMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6857,6112793&dq=propane+pipeline&hl=en|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 A farmer hit a propane pipeline near [[Butler, Illinois]] on December 8, forcing evacuation of that town. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=hNwhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=v2MEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5684,186244&dq=phillips+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On December 18, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] petroleum pipeline failed near [[Locust Grove, Orange County, Virginia|Locust Grove, Virginia]]. {{convert|212,000|USgal|L}} of kerosene spilled into the Rapidan and Rappahannock Rivers. On New Year's Eve, following a rapid thaw and heavy rains, containment dams broke and kerosene flowed downstream toward [[Fredericksburg, Virginia]]. Fish and game were killed, the City's water supply was cut off, and drinking water had to be hauled from Stafford County for seven days. The failure was caused by cracking caused during railroad shipping of the pipe before being installed. This was the seventh major leak from Colonial Pipeline in Virginia since 1973.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.vce.org/LoosePages/OutofSight/localgovpipeline5.html|title=Out Of Sight, Out Of Mind V|work=vce.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/washingtonpost/access/72360010.html?dids=72360010:72360010&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Jan+03%2C+1990&author=Brooke+A.+Masters&pub=The+Washington+Post+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=There%27s+%60Trouble+With+That+Pipeline%27%3BKerosene+Spill+Near+Fredericksburg+Is+Latest+of+Seven+Leaks&pqatl=google | first=Brooke A. | last=Masters | title=There's 'Trouble With That Pipeline';Kerosene Spill Near Fredericksburg Is Latest of Seven Leaks | date=January 3, 1990}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1298&dat=19900915&id=KbFYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NosDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2506,3104471|title=The Free Lance-Star - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 On December 29, shock waves from an explosion ruptured a 30-inch gas transmission pipeline operating at 350 psi in the [[Hell Gate]] section of [[New York City, New York]]. The rupture was 11 feet long, and escaping gas ignited, killing 2 people, injuring one other person, and destroying 2 buildings and 50 automobiles.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/texaseasterntran00netc#page/62/mode/2up|title=Texas Eastern Transmission Corporation natural gas pipeline explosion and fire, Edison, New Jersey, March 23, 1994|work=archive.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1989 New York City Con Edison Steam Pipe explosion, rupture killing three people in the 3rd Ave./Gramercy Park area.
==1990s==

===1990===

* 1990 On January 2, an [[ExxonMobil]] underwater pipeline, located at the mouth of Morse Creek, discharged approximately 567.000 gallons of No. 2 heating oil into the Arthur Kill waterway, between [[New Jersey]], and [[Staten Island, New York]]. Later, it was disclosed that the pipeline controlling system had been giving false leak alarms before, and had automatically shut down that day, for a leak being detected, but was restarted twice after that.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://response.restoration.noaa.gov/book_shelf/26_spilldb.pdf |title=Safety Recommendations|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111121222456/http://response.restoration.noaa.gov/book_shelf/26_spilldb.pdf |archivedate=November 21, 2011 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://www.nytimes.com/1990/01/04/nyregion/coast-guard-says-oil-spill-off-si-exceeds-.html | work=The New York Times | first=Dennis | last=Hevesi | title=Coast Guard Says Oil Spill Off S.I. Exceeds {{convert|200,000|USgal|L}} | date=January 4, 1990}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1982&dat=19900110&id=9llGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=oSMNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4928,876396|title=The Evening News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 An [[ExxonMobil]] 18 inch pipeline failed near [[Crane, Texas]] on February 13, spilling 20,027 barrels of petroleum. The pipe failed from external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267401|title=Feb. 13, 1990 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 A bank was destroyed in [[Crested Butte, Colorado]] from a leaking propane gas main on March 6. 3 employees were killed, and 14 others injured. A ruptured pipe coupling and a pipe separated from a coupling were found on the gas main during the investigation into the explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19900318&id=SEUyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=_uQFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5234,5214924|title=Lawrence Journal-World - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 A [[TEPPCO Partners]] propane pipeline ruptured, send out propane vapors that later caught fire, in [[North Blenheim, New York]], on March 13. Stress from previous work done on the pipeline caused the pipeline rupture and vapor cloud that moved downhill into a town. Two people were killed, seven persons injured, 8 homes destroyed, and more than $4 million in property damage, and other costs resulted when the cloud ignited.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/recs/letters/1991/P91_1_4.pdf |title=Safety Recommendation|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100618153512/http://www.ntsb.gov/Recs/letters/1991/P91_1_4.pdf |archivedate=June 18, 2010 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://un-naturalgas.org/weblog/2010/03/pipelines-eminent-domain-twenty-years-later-the-tragedy-persists/|title=Pipelines eminent domain: Twenty years later, the tragedy persists |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101129072035/http://un-naturalgas.org/weblog/2010/03/pipelines-eminent-domain-twenty-years-later-the-tragedy-persists/ |dead-url=yes |archive-date=November 29, 2010 |accessdate=February 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=XXUhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=AokFAAAAIBAJ&pg=1613,3505122&dq=family+killed+by+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Daily Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/details/liquidpropanepip00netc|title=Liquid propane pipeline rupture and fire, Texas Eastern Products Pipeline Company, North Blenheim, New York, March 13, 1990|work=Internet Archive|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On March 30, a [[Buckeye Partners]] 10-inch pipeline ruptured from overstress, due to a landslide in [[Freeport, Pennsylvania]], resulting in the release of approximately {{convert|1300|oilbbl|m3}} of mixed petroleum products. Spilled petroleum products entered Knapp's Run, a small creek emptying into the [[Allegheny River]] and, eventually, the [[Ohio River]]. The product release resulted in extensive ground and water pollution and interrupted the use of the Allegheny River as a water supply for several communities, causing severe water shortages in those areas. Damage to the pipeline and environmental cleanup and restoration costs exceeded $12 million. A 6-hour delay in Buckeye contacting the federal [[National Response Center]] were also noted.<ref name="ReferenceA"/><ref>{{cite news| url=https://www.nytimes.com/1990/04/04/us/concern-abates-as-oil-in-river-passes-pittsburgh.html | work=The New York Times | title=Concern Abates as Oil in River Passes Pittsburgh | date=April 4, 1990}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=799&dat=19900403&id=iDIhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DlcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6713,132368|title=The Bryan Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1129&dat=19900517&id=8rYzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=124DAAAAIBAJ&pg=6679,5711900|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On April 1, a Mid-Valley crude oil pipeline failed, due to external corrosion, near [[Leitchfield, Kentucky]]. About 3,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1696&dat=19900404&id=DA0bAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IkgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3334,1044834|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267429|title=April 1, 1990 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On May 6, a spool on a [[Texaco]] pipeline off of the Louisiana coast ruptured. {{convert|13600|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil were estimated to have spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.boemre.gov/incidents/PDFs/MMS91_0066.pdf|title=The Bureau of Ocean Energy Management, Regulation and Enforcement HomePage|work=boemre.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1876&dat=19900506&id=wqYeAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Qs4EAAAAIBAJ&pg=3434,2855582|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On August 13, a 10-inch [[Koch Industries]] pipeline failed in [[Linwood, Wisconsin]], spilling about 7,980 gallons of gasoline, forcing 12 nearby families to evacuate, and shutting down a nearby railroad.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19900814&id=BaAaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=YywEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6717,6234161|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On August 29, a private contractor laying conduit for underground power lines ruptured a pipeline that fouled a Western Branch creek with diesel fuel in [[Chesapeake, Virginia]]. Over {{convert|67,000|USgal|L}} of fuel were spilled.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=VP&p_theme=vp&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EAFF3594FC8A7DB&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=FIRM BLAMED FOR LEAK OF DIESEL FUEL IN CREEK |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1990 On August 29, a natural gas explosion and fire destroyed two row houses and damaged two adjacent houses and three parked cars in [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]]. One person was killed, and nine people, including two firefighters, were injured. A cracked gas main, that was stressed by soil erosion from a nearby broken water line, was the cause of the gas leak.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P91_12.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=July 10, 1992 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1990 On November 5, an [[Amoco]] crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Ethel, Missouri]] on a farm, fouling over {{convert|35|mi|km}} of the [[Chariton River]]. About 2,400 barrels of crude were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=f9ozAAAAIBAJ&sjid=RI8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=6850,992087&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1908&dat=19901113&id=LNkhAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vJ4FAAAAIBAJ&pg=4768,2940823|title=The Nevada Daily Mail - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267573|title=Nov. 5, 1990 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1990 On November 8, a {Williams]] LPG pipeline failed in [[Whiteside County, Illinois]], from a drain valve leak, killing 1 person and injuring 1 other.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print</ref>
* 1990 At least 3 leaks that spilled over a thousand gallons of oil were found in a pipeline in [[Cerritos, California]], it was announced on November 23. One of the failed section of pipeline was 6 to 7 years old.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=LB&p_theme=lb&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EAE8CB6E99B00A0&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=THREE MORE OIL PIPELINE LEAKS FOUND |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1990 On December 9, a gas system valve between one of [[Fort Benjamin Harrison]], near [[Indianapolis, Indiana]], gas distribution systems and a discontinued steel gas system segment was inadvertently opened, allowing natural gas to enter residential buildings that had previously received their gas from the discontinued segment. Gas accumulating in Building 1025 of Harrison Village was ignited by one of many available sources, and the resulting explosion killed 2 occupants and injured 24 other persons. One building was destroyed, and two others were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1992/P92_14.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007223808/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1992/P92_14.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1990 A bulldozer hit a pipeline supplying jet fuel from a West Texas refinery, to [[Carswell Air Force Base]] in [[Fort Worth, Texas]], on December 18, spilling 20,000 gallons of jet fuel. 100 people in nearby apartments were evacuated for a time.<ref>[http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_action=list&p_topdoc=51 ]{{dead link|date=June 2017}}</ref>

===1991===
* 1991 A crew installing a water main hit a 6-inch gas main at 450 psi of pressure in [[Novi, Michigan]] on January 2. Gas company workers were trying to install a sleeve over the failure when the gas exploded and burned, injuring 6 of the Gas Company crew. A telephone cable was also damaged, knocking out phone service for about 5-- customers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19910103&id=o9ILAAAAIBAJ&sjid=5lUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4518,86327|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 On January 31, a Mobil Company crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Valencia, California]], spilling up to 75,000 gallons of crude oil. The same day, a report was released showing that particular pipeline had a 99.8% chance of a leak in the next 5 years.<ref name="articles.latimes.com"/><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/latimes/access/61032414.html?dids=61032414:61032414&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Feb+02%2C+1991&author=MICHAEL+CONNELLY%3B+JULIO+MORAN&pub=Los+Angeles+Times+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=Pipe+Rupture+May+Fuel+Case+for+Replacement+Oil%3A+The+Valencia+break+occurred+the+same+day+that+Mobil+released+an+environmental+report+warning+of+a+99.8%25+chance+of+such+an+accident+on+the+aging+line.&pqatl=google | first=Michael | last=Connelly | title=Pipe Rupture May Fuel Case for Replacement Oil: The Valencia break occurred the same day that Mobil released an environmental report warning of a 99.8% chance of such an accident on the aging line |website=Pqasb.pqarchiver.com| date=February 2, 1991}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=LA&p_theme=la&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EF6120C39A17542&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=CLEANUP OF OIL TO GO A MONTH |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1991 On February 5, a backhoe hit a gas distribution line, next to apartments in [[Greendale, Wisconsin]], causing an explosion & fire that killed 3 and injured 6 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1499&dat=19910206&id=h3YfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ICwEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6489,4182608|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267667|title=Feb. 5, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 Construction crews ruptured a propane pipeline, on March 2, forcing the evacuation of 2,500 from several subdivisions in [[Richland County, South Carolina]] for a time. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267682|title=March 2, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 A Lakehead (now [[Enbridge]]) crude oil pipeline near [[Grand Rapids, Minnesota]], ruptured on March 3. More than 40,500 barrels of crude went into the Prairie River, of which 39,800 barrels were eventually recovered. About {{convert|4|e6USgal|m3}} of oil had spilled from that pipeline from the early 1970s to 1991, per Minnesota records. A resident in the area noticed the smell of oil and alerted the local fire department. Approximately 300 people living in homes near the site were evacuated for safety, but were allowed to return to their homes later in the night.<ref>{{cite web|author=September 17, 2016 |url=http://www.walkermn.com/news/this-week-in-history/article_39840266-e224-11e5-8c44-7f55501c9082.html |title=This Week in History - The Pilot Independent: News |publisher=Walkermn.com |date=2016-03-05 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Q1lYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=_vkDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3829,387617&dq=lakehead+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Spokane Chronicle - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=K2pFAAAAIBAJ&sjid=UbwMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5194,2089098&dq=lakehead+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 On March 16, an anchor from a ship ruptured a [[Chevron Corporation]] pipeline offshore of [[El Segundo, California]], spilling about 55,000 gallons of light oil. Wildlife was affected.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1665&dat=19910318&id=W1YaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XiQEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6663,3950364|title=The Times-News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 A [[Diamond Shamrock]] 10 inch crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Knox City, Texas]] on June 8, spilling about 84,000 gallons of crude oil, with much of it entering the [[Brazos River]]. Heavy rains caused the pipeline to fail.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19910609&id=yVNSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=qDYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=7071,1646314|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 A bulldozer hit a [[Chevron Corporation]] crude oil pipeline near [[Park City, Utah]], on June 27. About 126,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=336&dat=19910704&id=0wwpAAAAIBAJ&sjid=gIQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3348,872816|title=The Deseret News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267762|title=June 27, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 On June 29, about 54,222 gallons of fuel oil and gasoline leaked from a 10-inch [[Koch Industries]] pipeline in [[Portage County, Wisconsin]], from a 3-inch crack. A previous significant leak had occurred on this pipeline in that area the year before. Local officials urged Koch to upgrade its leak monitoring equipment, and, the Office of Pipeline Safety ordered this pipeline to be shut down until tested. Koch later replaced {{convert|12|mi|km}} of that pipeline in the area. The original pipe was installed in 1988.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=l8EaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NSwEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3878,1006602&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=mcEaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NSwEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1700,2441022&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267765|title=June 29, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1368&dat=19910709&id=kbUyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=wBIEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6872,1925613|title=The Milwaukee Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 On June 30, an [[Amoco]] pipeline failed near [[Denver City, Texas]], spilling 28,200 barrels of petroleum. The failure was caused by internal corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267766|title=June 30, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1991 On July 17, workers were removing a corroded segment of the Consumers Power Company's (CP) 10-inch transmission line pipeline in [[Mapleton, Michigan]]. As a segment of the pipeline was being removed, natural gas at 360-psig pressure exerted about 12 tons of force on an adjacent closed valve (H-143), causing it and a short segment of connected pipe to move and separate from an unanchored compression coupling. The force of the escaping gas killed one worker (a welder), injured five other workers, and collapsed a steel pit that housed valve H-143.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1992/P92_21_22.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130622083225/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1992/P92_21_22.pdf |archivedate=June 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1991 On August 30, an earth mover hit a 16-inch [[ExxonMobil]] pipeline near [[Beaumont, Texas]], causing a leaking that spilled about 19,000 gallons of crude oil. Nearby businesses were evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19910831&id=o5szAAAAIBAJ&sjid=sjIHAAAAIBAJ&pg=6971,7593170|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267810|title=Aug. 30, 1991 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 About {{convert|42,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil spilled from a broken [[Amoco]] pipeline at a barge facility at [[High Island, Texas]] on September 5.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=9TQdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pKUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2670,1617845&dq=high+island+texas+pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=The Tuscaloosa News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1243&dat=19910908&id=tJtTAAAAIBAJ&sjid=c4YDAAAAIBAJ&pg=3493,6042112|title=The Bulletin - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1991 On December 19, a 36-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] ruptured from prior excavation damage about {{convert|2.8|mi|km}} downstream of the pipeline's [[Simpsonville, South Carolina]], pump station. The rupture allowed more than {{convert|500,000|USgal|L}} of diesel fuel to flow into Durbin Creek, causing environmental damage that affected {{convert|26|mi|km}} of waterways, including the [[Enoree River]], which flows through [[Sumter National Forest]]. The spill also forced Clinton and Whitmire, South Carolina, to use alternative water supplies.<ref name="ReferenceA"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.iosc.org/papers_posters/00305.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714182210/http://www.iosc.org/papers_posters/00305.pdf |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* 1991 On December 28, two explosions in rapid succession occurred in apartment No. 3 of a two-story, eight-apartment, wood-frame structure in [[Santa Rosa, California]]. Two people were killed and three others were injured. Fire after the explosions destroyed that apartment and three other apartments in the front of the building.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/safety/safety-recs/recletters/P92_16_18.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=May 21, 1992 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>

===1992===
* 1992 On January 3, an 8-inch [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline in [[West Finley Township, Washington County, Pennsylvania]] failed from earth subsidence, caused by a coal mine. Leaking gas entered a nearby home, causing it to explode. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2519&dat=19920108&id=RyxiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=s3YNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1981,1309219|title=Observer-Reporter - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267910|title=Jan. 3, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 A pipeline carrying a mixture of crude oil and water burst on January 5 in [[Anchorage, Alaska]], spilling 16,900 gallons of crude oil into [[Cook Inlet]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1144&dat=19920106&id=x3UcAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dGQEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6929,2582269|title=The Pittsburgh Press - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 On January 6, an [[ExxonMobil]] pipeline offshore of [[Grand Isle, Louisiana]] in the Gulf of Mexico leaked about 4200 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267913|title=Jan. 6, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* A spill from a [[Williams Companies]] pipeline was discovered on January 13, in a soybean field, near [[Renner, South Dakota]]. The cause of the leak was identified as a hairline crack in the seam. About 400,000 gallons of petroleum products was lost. The leak may have started as long as 6 months before.<ref>{{cite web|author=Oklahoman |url=http://newsok.com/article/2384939 |title=South Dakota Suing State Firm Over Pipeline Leak |publisher=News OK |date=1992-02-14 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1992 On January 17, while a gas company crew was doing routine annual maintenance work at a regulator stations in [[Chicago, Illinois]], high-pressure gas entered a low-pressure gas system. The gasunder as much as 10 psig of pressureescaped through gas appliances into homes and other buildings, where it was ignited by several unidentified sources. The resulting explosion and fires killed 4 people, injured 4, and damaged 14 houses and 3 commercial buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1993/P93_1_5.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121010040934/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1993/P93_1_5.pdf |archivedate=October 10, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1992 On March 4, a gas distribution pipeline failed in [[Utica, New York]], killing 2 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267966|title=March 4, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 Construction equipment ruptured a Sun Co. petroleum products pipeline in [[Edgemont, Pennsylvania]] on March 4, spilling about 933 barrels of heating oil, that reached Chester Creek.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1992-03-06/news/mn-3437_1_spill-fouls-creek | work=Los Angeles Times | title=Oil Pipe Spill Fouls Creek | date=March 6, 1992}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267965|title=March 4, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19920305&id=blpPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=RAMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3160,1236866|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|website=news.google.com}}</ref>
* 1992 On March 11, a crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Leitchfeild, Kentucky]], then the crude oil was ignited, causing a fire at a pump station that forced the evacuation of 69 families. About 3,780 barrels of crude were lost. The cause of the rupture was external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=266&dat=19920313&id=dtorAAAAIBAJ&sjid=WGQFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3268,1037674|title=Kentucky New Era - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1992 Two [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] lines exploded and burned in [[White Bluff, Tennessee]] on March 15, destroying 3 homes, and burning 400 acres. 100 people in a 4 square miles area nearby were evacuated, and 2 people treated at a hospital for injuries from the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19920315&id=LU4eAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NMcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3004,2286161|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/267970|title=March 15, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 On April 7, a salt dome cavern used to store LPG & similar products was overfilled, leading to an uncontrolled release of highly volatile liquids (HVLs) from a salt dome storage cavern near [[Brenham, Texas]], formed a large, heavier-than-air gas cloud that later exploded. Three people died from injuries sustained either from the blast, or in the following fire. An additional 21 people were treated for injuries at area hospitals. Damage from the accident exceeded $9 million.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9301.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Report |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=rjpSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=VzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2878,4742843&dq=i+70+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/safetystudies/SS0502.pdf |title=Safety Recommendations|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140611022527/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/safetystudies/SS0502.pdf |archivedate=June 11, 2014 }}</ref>
* 1992 On April 27, a 6-inch petroleum products pipeline ruptured, in [[Lakeland, Florida]], spilling about 1,674 gallons of jet fuel. The cause was third party damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1755&dat=19920603&id=sTgeAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Kb8EAAAAIBAJ&pg=3547,2179192|title=Sarasota Herald-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 A contractor planting tree hit a gas pipeline, in [[Rochester, Michigan]], on May 20. The gas later exploded, destroying a 2-story building, killing one person, and injuring 14 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1901&dat=19920521&id=QwwqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NNMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=2344,2345564|title=The News-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 On June 19, an 8-inch ARCO petroleum products pipeline ruptured, due to control problems, spraying a neighborhood in [[Victoria, Texas]] with gasoline. Some residents were evacuated as long as 3 days afterwards. There was no fire. ABout 6700 gallons of gasoline were released.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268026|title=June 19, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19930422&id=vTpSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=VzYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2719,1847952|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* On September 6, an [[Amoco]] pipeline spilled about 12,000 gallons of petroleum product, in [[Hammond, Indiana]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268090 |title=Sept. 6, 1992 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1992-09-06 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1992 A gas transmission pipeline that was being moved on October 9 exploded & burned, near [[Elwin, Illinois]], killing one worker. 2 firefighters were also injured in controlling the situation.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1290&dat=19921010&id=iOg0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=wYwDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5940,4617991|title=The News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 On October 13, a bulldozer hit a [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline in [[Moon, Pennsylvania]], spilling about 105 barrels of jet turbine fuel.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268122|title=Oct. 13, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19921014&id=E7giAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JLUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3713,3036050|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 On October 14, a heavy equipment operator hit a 10-inch Gulf Coast Natural Gas Company line carrying gas at 420 psi near [[Wharton, Texas]]. The escaping gas exploded, then burned, but the operator was unhurt.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19921015&id=s0dSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=czYNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6133,3174767|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268124|title=Oct. 14, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1992 A natural gas explosion destroyed a house, in [[Catskill (town), New York]], on November 6. The house had not had active gas service since 1969. The explosion killed a woman in the house, seriously injured her daughter, and slightly injured two children in a neighboring house. Gas had escaped from a nearby cracked gas main.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1993/P93_7_8.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121010040121/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1993/P93_7_8.pdf |archivedate=October 10, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1992 On December 3, pipeline company workers ruptured a [[natural gas liquid]] (NGL) pipeline, causing a vapor cloud to drift across I-70 near [[Aurora, Colorado]]. The Cloud later ignited, burning 6 motorists.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=RM&p_theme=rm&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB4DBB679E0EB22&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=EXPLOSION INJURES 6 MOTORISTS ON I-70 RUPTURED PIPE RELEASES NATURAL-GAS CLOUD THAT DRIFTED ACROSS HIGHWAY, THEN BURST INTO FIREBALL |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=DP&p_theme=dp&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EAF441B92B0F8A1&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=Woman burned in I-70 pipeline blast sues |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=aTdEAAAAIBAJ&sjid=968MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1088,4579216&dq=i+70+pipeline+explosion&hl=en|title=The Durant Daily Democrat - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268167|title=Dec. 3, 1992 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1993===
* 1993 On March 28, a 36-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] Company petroleum products pipeline ruptured near [[Herndon, Virginia]]. The rupture created a geyser which sprayed diesel fuel over {{convert|75|ft|m}} into the air, coating overhead power lines and adjacent trees, and mist covering adjacent Virginia Electric Power Company buildings. The diesel fuel spewed from the rupture into an adjacent storm water management pond and flowed overland and through a network of storm sewer pipes before reaching Sugarland Run Creek, a tributary of the [[Potomac River]]. The cause was latent third party damage. About 400,000 gallons of diesel were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://archive.org/stream/colonialpipeline00unit/colonialpipeline00unit_djvu.txt|title=Full text of "Colonial Pipeline rupture : hearing before the Subcommittee on Investigations and Oversight of the Committee on Public Works and Transportation, House of Representatives, One Hundred Third Congress, first session, May 18, 1993"|work=archive.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/washingtonpost/access/72133309.html?dids=72133309:72133309&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Mar+30%2C+1993&author=D%27Vera+Cohn%3B+Patricia+Davis&pub=The+Washington+Post+%28pre-1997+Fulltext%29&desc=Damage+by+Equipment+May+Have+Weakened+Pipeline%3B+Most+Oil+Recovered%3B+Drinking+Water+Considered+Safe&pqatl=google | first=D'Vera | last=Cohn | title=Damage by Equipment May Have Weakened Pipeline; Most Oil Recovered; Drinking Water Considered Safe | date=March 30, 1993}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268258 |title=March 28, 1993 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1993-03-28 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1993 On April 6, a 16-inch crude oil pipeline ruptured, spilling up to 125,000 gallons of crude oil into a stream bed in [[Kern County, California]], forcing a temporary closure of the nearby Golden State Freeway.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1993-04-07/news/mn-20212_1_oil-leak | work=Los Angeles Times | first=Aaron | last=Curtiss | title=Leak Spills Oil Into Creek Bed, Closes I-5 | date=April 7, 1993}}</ref>
* 1993 A fire at Transco/[[Williams Companies]] gas compressor station, in [[Billingsley, Alabama]], on June 3 injured one worker. The cause was from equipment failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=19930605&id=B9UdAAAAIBAJ&sjid=a8cEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6043,537515|title=Times Daily - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268305|title=June 3, 1993 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1993 On June 9, a cinder block duplex in [[Cliffwood Beach, New Jersey]], exploded as a New Jersey Natural Gas Company (NJNG) contractor was trenching in front of the building. The gas explosion killed 3 residents of the duplex, and seriously injured 3 others.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1994/P94_1_3.pdf|title=Safety Recommendation |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130624210026/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1994/P94_1_3.pdf |archivedate=June 24, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1993 On June 24, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] line failed just next to a gas compressor station in [[West Monroe, Louisiana]], causing a massive fire that forced evacuations of homes & businesses with in a mile of the failure. Internal corrosion of the pipeline was the cause.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1957&dat=19930625&id=XVlGAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NukMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5741,5906153|title=The Daily Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268325|title=June 24, 1993 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>  
* 1993 On July 22, a city of St. Paul Department of Public Works backhoe hooked and pulled apart a Northern States Power Company (NSP) high-pressure gas service line in [[St. Paul, Minnesota]]. An explosion and natural gas-fueled fire resulted about 20&nbsp;minutes after the backhoe hooked the service line. The explosion force caused part of the building to land on and flatten an automobile traveling southwest on East Third Street, and the driver died instantly. The explosion and ensuing fire also killed an apartment occupant and a person outside the building and injured 12 people.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1995/P95_26_27.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130626022712/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1995/P95_26_27.pdf |archivedate=June 26, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1993 On July 26, a 6-inch pipeline in Nebraska was exposed by scour in a creek bed and its banks, and was struck by flood debris, which caused it to rupture. The rupture resulted in the release of {{convert|2203|oilbbl|m3}} of anhydrous ammonia<ref>{{cite web|url=http://pstrust.org/library/docs/ntsb_doc24.pdf|title=PIPELINE REPORT |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120316112558/http://pstrust.org/library/docs/ntsb_doc24.pdf |archivedate=March 16, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1993 An ammonia pipeline failed in [[Sperry, Oklahoma]] on August 20. 80 homes in the area were evacuated. Several people were treated for ammonia inhalation injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=aDtbAAAAIBAJ&sjid=7k8NAAAAIBAJ&pg=6198,5530384&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Durant Daily Democrat - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1993 A trencher being used in golf course construction hit a petroleum productions pipeline in [[Berwick Township, Pennsylvania]] on September 2, causing a leak of about 26,250 gallons of gasoline. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268385|title=Sept. 2, 1993 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2202&dat=19940218&id=LRAmAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pv0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=5647,2632669&hl=en|title=Gettysburg Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1993 On September 15, an 8-inch NORCO Pipeline Co. line ruptured in east [[Indiana]], just west of [[Edgerton, Ohio]], spilling about 30,000 gallons of diesel fuel. There was a 4 foot long rupture in the pipeline, and some of the diesel entered Fish Creek, killing wildlife. The rupture was caused by pumping against a closed valve. Later, NORCO and [[ARCO]] agreed to pay $2.8 million for the spill in US District Court.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19930917&id=lW0xAAAAIBAJ&sjid=VwMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6743,4518087|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268395|title=Sept. 15, 1993 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=799&dat=19960719&id=8JoqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=MlgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6515,2407628|title=The Bryan Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1993 On November 3, Amoco Pipeline was fined $12,500 for a 1971 pipeline leak that contaminated a drinking well and caused other pollution problems for people living near [[Garfield, Minnesota]].<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=PD&s_site=twincities&p_multi=SP&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB5DD4F3549B608&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=November 4, 1993 |title=PIPELINE LEAK IN 1971 DRAWS $12,500 FINE |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1993 On December 2, a 10-inch Conoco pipeline ruptured, spilling {{convert|8400|USgal|L}} of gasoline into a creek in [[Washington, Missouri]].<ref>{{cite news| url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SL&p_theme=sl&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB04E586383C551&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM | work=St. Louis Post-Dispatch | title=Briefs | date=December 3, 1993}}</ref>
* 1993 On December 8, a [[Sunoco]] pipeline was detected to be leaking by pressure loss, but, it took several days to find the leak point in [[Upper Leacock Township, Lancaster County, Pennsylvania]]. About 2,369 barrels of transmix were lost. The cause was from a backhoe hitting the pipeline in a cornfield.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19931219&id=NKpUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=nDsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1272,4250540|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268469|title=Dec. 8, 1993 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1993 An explosion and fire on a gas transmission pipeline on December 20, near [[Mellen, Wisconsin]], cut off the gas supply to 3,500 customers in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=oQ1eAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9l8NAAAAIBAJ&pg=6056,4754150&dq=phillips+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1993 In [[Ventura County, California]], on December 22, a leak occurred from a crude oil pipeline. This spill released an estimated 92,000 gallons of crude oil. The oil flowed through a culvert, traveled through 150 feet of woodland and brush, to McGrath Creek, then flowed another 1,200 feet into [[McGrath Lake]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://osfm.fire.ca.gov/pipeline/pdf/publication/lowstresspipeline.pdf |format=PDF |title=An Assessment of Low Pressure Crude Oil Pipelines and Crude Oil Gathering Lines in California |website=Osfm.fire.ca.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>

===1994===
* 1994 In January, a pipeline ruptured, dumping almost {{convert|162,500|USgal|L}} of oil in a river, the Marais des Cygnes River in [[Osawatomie, Kansas]]. In addition to a $804,700 fine, BP Amoco agreed to spend at least $145,300 on a supplemental environmental project involving reconstruction improvements to Osawatomie's water intake.<ref name="ukopa.co.uk">{{cite web|url=http://www.ukopa.co.uk/publications/pdf/020035.pdf|title=WORLDWIDE PIPELINE INCIDENTS - APRIL 2002  |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20080517110500/http://www.ukopa.co.uk/publications/pdf/020035.pdf |archivedate=May 17, 2008 }}</ref>
* 1994 On January 16, a pipeline burst, at a tank farm in [[Saint Louis, Missouri]], spilling gasoline during a transfer operation. The company knew that some gasoline was missing, but, waited until January 18 to confirm and report the loss. About 240,000 gallons of gasoline was spilled, with about 100,000 gallons entering the [[Mississippi River]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1893&dat=19940127&id=j7UfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JdcEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3133,3432776|title=The Southeast Missourian - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1994 The January 17 [[Northridge earthquake]] caused a crude oil pipeline to crack near [[Piru, California]], spilling about 173,000 gallons of crude into the [[Santa Clara River (California)|Santa Clara River]]. The cleanup took more than 600 workers six weeks to complete and cost more than $14 million.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://articles.latimes.com/1994-03-03/local/me-29326_1_oil-spill | work=Los Angeles Times | first=Jeff | last=McDonald | title=PIRU : River Oil Spill Cleanup Completed | date=March 3, 1994}}</ref>
* 1994 On February 1, the third explosion in 7 years hit a LPG/NGL pipeline Terminal in [[Iowa City, Iowa]]. 11 workers at the Terminal escaped injury, and 6 families within 1 1/2 miles of the Terminal were evacuated. The 2 previous explosions were in 1987 and 1989.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=pU9FAAAAIBAJ&sjid=57sMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5293,199089&dq=midamerican+pipeline+fire&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* '''[[Edison, New Jersey natural gas explosion]]''': March 23, 1994, previous damage caused a 36-inch diameter natural gas transmission pipeline to rupture at [[Edison, New Jersey]]. Several apartment buildings and a number of automobiles were destroyed in the massive fire. One woman died of a heart attack, and at least 93 others had minor injuries. Delays in shutting off one of the pipeline's valves was cited as contributing to the damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9501.pdf|title=Accident Reports |accessdate=February 6, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150404031901/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9501.pdf |archivedate=April 4, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR9501.aspx|title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-95-01|work=ntsb.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1994 On May 8, a [[Sunoco]] pipeline leaked gasoline in [[Indiana County, Pennsylvania]], forcing the evacuation of 50 homes. About 537 barrels of gasoline were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2004&dat=19940506&id=zb0iAAAAIBAJ&sjid=R7YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5921,2280466|title=Allegheny Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268631|title=May 8, 1994 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1994 On June 2, a [[Koch Industries]] pipeline spilled gasoline in [[Wichita, Kansas]]. About 79,000 galons were spilled, and, some of it caused interruptions in local water supply.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=348&dat=20000114&id=-ngvAAAAIBAJ&sjid=NTUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6708,3560869|title=Rome News-Tribune - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1994 A 2-inch steel gas service line that had been exposed during excavation separated at a compression coupling about {{convert|5|ft|m}} from the wall of a retirement home in [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]] on June 9. The escaping gas flowed underground, passed through openings in the building foundation, migrated to other floors, and exploded. The accident resulted in 1 fatality, 66 injuries, and more than $5 million in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAR9601.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board : Pipeline Accident Report |date=June 9, 1994 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1994 A residents near [[O'Fallon, Missouri]] detected a petroleum smell, early on September 22. The local Fire Department was called several hours later, and noticed an oily mist in the area, and found a leaking pipeline. The owner of the 10-inch petroleum products later claimed the spill volume was less than {{convert|1,000|USgal|L}}, but later calculations and batch volume measurements indicate a spill of 29,000 to {{convert|37,000|USgal|L}}. EPA officials later admit someone lied about the spill volume. Over the next 10 years, 8 attempts at remediation were made, before the O'Day Creek was cleaned of all petroleum products.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://webofconspiracy.com/CleanUp.htm|title=Web of Conspiracy - Remediation / clean up attempts-8 official-1 illegal|work=webofconspiracy.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://webofconspiracy.com/TestResults2.htm|title=Web of conspiracy - Test Results Two|work=webofconspiracy.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1994 On October 8, a lightning strike shut a valve on a [[Koch Industries]] crude oil pipeline crossing Gum Hollow Creek, while oil was flowing, triggering a pressure buildup that ripped a 50-square-inch hole in a section of the pipe that was already weakened by corrosion. Pipeline employees  unaware of the rupture in the pipe  turned the pipeline pumps back on after the pipeline shut down automatically, sending oil pouring into the creek for about an hour. The spill created a {{convert|12|mi|km|adj=on}}-long slick on Nueces and Corpus Christi bays along the Texas Gulf Coast. Nearly seven years later, delicate coastal marshes that serve as a nursery for shrimp, flounder, crabs and other marine life had not fully recovered. The estimated spill size was {{convert|2151|oilbbl|m3}}, but that was debated as being too small a size. The pipeline eventually agreed to pay more than $45 million in damages. Koch reported to PHMSA that the spill cost zero dollars in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.fws.gov/southwest/es/Docs/NRDAR_SiteInformation/Texas/KochGH.pdf |format=PDF |title=Koch Pipeline - Gum Hollow Oil Spill |website=Fws.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Associated |first=The |url=http://cjonline.com/stories/072401/bus_kochviolations.shtml |title=Court records point to violations |publisher=CJOnline.com |date=2001-07-24 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268735 |title=Oct. 8, 1994 - ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=1994-10-08 |accessdate=2016-09-17}}</ref>
* 1994 In October, record high flooding along the [[San Jacinto River (Texas)|San Jacinto River]] in Texas lead to the failure of 8 pipelines crossing that river. Due to the flooding many other pipelines were also undermined. More than {{convert|35000|oilbbl|m3}} of petroleum and petroleum products were released into the river. Ignition of the released products resulted in 547 people receiving (mostly minor) burn and inhalation injuries. Spill response costs exceeded $7 million, and estimated property damage losses were about $16 million.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1996/P96_23.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130624222224/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/recletters/1996/P96_23.pdf |archivedate=June 24, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://ncsp.tamu.edu/reports/NTSB/ntsbPipeStudy/SIR9604.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140811114143/http://ncsp.tamu.edu/reports/NTSB/ntsbPipeStudy/SIR9604.pdf |archivedate=August 11, 2014 }}</ref>
* 1994 A natural gas explosion and fire destroyed a one-story, wood frame building in [[Waterloo, Iowa]] on October 17. The force of the explosion scattered debris over a {{convert|200|ft|m|adj=on}} radius. 6 persons inside the building died, and one person sustained serious injuries. 3 persons working in an adjacent building sustained minor injuries when a wall of the building collapsed inward from the force of the explosion. The explosion also damaged nine parked cars. A person in a vehicle who had just exited the adjacent building suffered minor injuries. Additionally, two firefighters sustained minor injuries during the emergency response. Two other nearby buildings also sustained structural damage and broken windows.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pipelinesafetytrust.com/docs/P98_1_5.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=April 30, 1998 |website=Pipelinesafetytrust.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB9802.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board : Pipeline Accident Brief |date=October 17, 1994 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>
* 1994 On November 21, a [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline ruptured from incorrect operation in [[Moon Township, Pennsylvania]]. About 38,000 gallons of kerosene were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19941121&id=37kiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=TbUFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3978,4940604|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/268773|title=Nov. 21, 1994 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1994 A leak of at least {{convert|20,000|USgal|L}} of diesel fuel was discovered on a [[Koch Industries]] pipeline near [[Plover, Wisconsin]] on November 29. The leak brought this pipeline's total spill volume to {{convert|100,000|USgal|L}} on a {{convert|91|mi|km}} pipeline section through several years.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iEEgAAAAIBAJ&sjid=N38EAAAAIBAJ&pg=4797,7710320&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Milwaukee Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1995===
* 1995 Since starting operations in 1954 until 1995, Yellowstone Pipeline had 71 leaks along the Flathead Indian Reservation in Montana, spilling {{convert|3,500,000|USgal|L}} of petroleum products. Eventually, the Flathead refused to sign a new lease with Yellowstone.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://missoulanews.bigskypress.com/missoula/a-pipeline-to-the-past/Content?oid=1131791|title=A pipeline to the past|work=Missoula News|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1995 A 26-inch gas transmission pipeline ruptured and burned near [[Castle Rock, Washington]] on March 6.
