There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=2dhYAAAAIBAJ&sjid=SvEDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6776,4578656&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1995 On March 20, a natural gas transmission pipeline leaked and burned near [[Chipola, Louisiana]]. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/theadvocate/access/23646229.html?dids=23646229:23646229&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Mar+20%2C+1995&author=RICH+LOUP&pub=Advocate&desc=Gas+line+explodes+***+Blast+frightens+rural+residents%3B+no+injuries+noted&pqatl=google | work=Advocate | first=Rich | last=Loup | title=Gas line explodes *** Blast frightens rural residents; no injuries noted | date=March 20, 1995}}</ref>
* 1995 On March 27, a bulldozer operator ruptured a 40-inch gas transmission pipeline in [[Huntersville, North Carolina]], causing an explosion. The operator was knocked off the bulldozer, then was run over by the driverless bulldozer.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=VLBOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ARUEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4978,5638063&dq=pipeline+rupture&hl=en|title=Star-News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1995 On March 30, a [[Koch Industries]] pipeline ruptured in the parking lot of a church in [[Port Lavaca, Texas]], spilled oil and benzine. Businesses nearby were evacuated. About 100 gallons of the mix was spilled. The failure was caused by Koch employees testing the pipeline under pressure, who thought the pipeline was full of only water.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19950331&id=TeVHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=iIAMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2571,159426|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1995 Two Native Tribes of the [[Flathead Nation]] shut down the Right of Way agreements of Yellowstone Pipeline in [[Montana]] on April 21. Past spills on Tribal lands were cited as the reason. In 1999, it was revealed that Yellowstone had 78 leaks in the previous 45 years.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=19950421&id=6royAAAAIBAJ&sjid=p_EDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2581,98573|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=19991105&id=Ko9XAAAAIBAJ&sjid=KPIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6047,4155985|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1995 On December 2, 3 contractors were killed, and another injured, when a vacuum used to control flammable fumes accidentally reversed during welding at a pipeline facility near [[McCamey, Texas]].<ref name="pstrust1">{{cite web|url=http://pstrust.org/library/docs/ops_doc23.pdf|title=Pipeline Report|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120316112548/http://pstrust.org/library/docs/ops_doc23.pdf |archivedate=March 16, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1995 A bulldozer hit a 16-inch gas pipeline in [[North Attleboro, Massachusetts]] on December 9, forcing evacuations of a nearby shopping mall. An estimated 40,000 people were evacuated.<ref name="pqasb.pqarchiver.com">{{cite news| url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/projo/access/31837326.html?dids=31837326:31837326&FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Dec+10%2C+1995&author=Christian+Berg%2C+Ellen+Lieberman%2C+Thomas+J.+Morgan+Bill+Ostendorf+and+Doug+Riggs&pub=The+Providence+Journal&desc=Massive+gas+leak+forces+mall+evacuation+*A+bulldozer+ruptures+a+buried+pipe+near+the+Emerald+Square+Mall%2C+releasing+a+jet+of+high-pressure+gas+that+disrupts+20%2C000+people.&pqatl=google | work=Providence Journal | first1=Christian | last1=Berg | first2=Ellen | last2=Lieberman | title=Massive gas leak forces mall evacuation *A bulldozer ruptures a buried pipe near the Emerald Square Mall, releasing a jet of high-pressure gas that disrupts 20,000 people | date=December 10, 1995}}</ref><ref name="pqasb.pqarchiver.com"/>
* 1995 On December 19, a gas explosion at a twin dwelling in [[Norristown, Pennsylvania]], killed 2 people and injured another person. Gas had migrated from a crack in a 6-inch cast iron gas main in the street.<ref name="pstrust1"/>

===1996===
* 1996 A gas pipeline failure excised a {{convert|30|ft|m|adj=on}} section of pipe, and the gas later ignited, causing a vegetation fire in [[East Stroudsburg, Pennsylvania]] on January 6. Later inspections found numerous flaws on this pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120021004H/120021004H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06202002.pdf|title=Corrective Action Order |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028024147/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120021004H/120021004H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06202002.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1996 On January 9, farm equipment pierced a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] crude oil pipeline near [[Coalinga, California]], spilling about 210,000 gallons of crude oil, covering about 4 acres of land.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19960111&id=E4o1AAAAIBAJ&sjid=QiEGAAAAIBAJ&pg=4585,977949|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1996 A backhoe hit a 6-inch [[Amoco]] gas pipeline on January 12, in [[Andrews, Texas]]. The pipeline then exploded and burned, causing severe burns to 2 workers, & minor injuries to 2 others. One of the severely burned died a few days later.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19960115&id=yh9SAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4DUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=4220,2916042|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1996 On February 5, a pipeline ruptured and spilled diesel fuel into a creek in [[Fairview Heights, Missouri]].<ref>{{cite news| url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SL&p_theme=sl&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB04F8094F4322B&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM | work=St. Louis Post-Dispatch | title=Pipeline Rupture Spills Fuel Into Creek | date=February 6, 1996}}</ref>
* 1996 A [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] Corp. worker was killed in [[West Finley, Pennsylvania]] on February 7, when a coupling on a pipeline being pressure tested broke loose & hit him.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1129&dat=19960208&id=LdRRAAAAIBAJ&sjid=eW8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=4870,3962371|title=Pittsburgh Post-Gazette - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 On February 17, a [[Diamond Shamrock]] propane pipeline was severed by a trenching machine in [[Parker County, Texas]]. US Highway 377 was shut down while fumes dissipated. 6,355 barrels of propane were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19960218&id=tShSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=4zUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=2249,2228412|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269117|title=Feb. 17, 1996 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1996 On February 18, a 20-inch natural gas line near [[South Point, Ohio]] failed, causing a massive fire. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1696&dat=19960218&id=bvoeAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GUgEAAAAIBAJ&pg=5057,1867670|title=Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 An oil sheen in a canal in [[Salt Lake City]], [[Utah]] seen on March 1 was eventually traced back to a leaking 4 inch [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] diesel fuel pipeline. The pipeline had been damaged by previous excavation. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.deseretnews.com/article/476707/CHEVRON-CHECKS-DAMAGE-FROM-SL-PIPELINE-LEAK.html?pg=all|title=CHEVRON CHECKS DAMAGE FROM S.L. PIPELINE LEAK|date=11 March 1996|work=DeseretNews.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 On April 23, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] line failed near [[Gaffney, South Carolina]], spilling gasoline. At first it was reported to be only 250 gallons spilled, but, later it was reported as 1,386 gallons. Rock abrasion was cited as the cause for the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1876&dat=19960504&id=igYqAAAAIBAJ&sjid=ac8EAAAAIBAJ&pg=6861,600888|title=Herald-Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269165|title=April 23, 1996 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 On May 8, a 20-inch [[Columbia Gas]] pipeline was ruptured by a crew installing a water pipeline in [[Oregon, Ohio]]. One business nearby was evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19960509&id=6k8xAAAAIBAJ&sjid=awMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1393,2514027|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1996 A [[Marathon Petroleum]] 20-inch pipeline ruptured at a location near [[Gramercy, Louisiana]], on May 23, 1996. The ruptured pipeline ultimately released about {{convert|475,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline into a common pipeline right-of-way and marsh land. Gasoline also entered the Blind River, causing environmental damage and killing fish, wildlife, and vegetation in the area. The pipeline controller did not at first recognize the pipeline had failed, and continued to ignore alarms from the pipeline SCADA system.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB9801.pdf |format=PDF |title=Pipeline Accident Brief |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref>
* 1996 In May, the largest penalty in an environmental case since the 1989 Exxon Valdez oil spill, the Connecticut-based Iroquois Pipeline Operating Company will pay $22 million in criminal and civil fines for violating federal environmental and safety laws, the United States announced today. The violations stem from the construction of one of the country's longest natural gas pipelines running 370 miles from Canada through upstate New York and Connecticut to Long Island. Backfill of the pipeline was one of the issues cited. 4 individuals also received jail time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.justice.gov/archive/opa/pr/1996/May96/233.enr.htm|title=#233: 1996-05-23 - Builder of Vast Northeastern Gas Pipeline Pleads Guilty|work=justice.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 On June 17, an Olympic Pipeline products line near [[Everett, Washington]], sprung a leak from a buckled area of pipe. About 1,000 gallons of gasoline were spilled into North Ebey Slough. The spill was discovered by a crew installing a water line nearby.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=860&dat=19960625&id=Zh1VAAAAIBAJ&sjid=KZQDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6727,4018773|title=Ellensburg Daily Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269214|title=June 17, 1996 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 A 36-inch [[Colonial Pipeline]] ruptured at the [[Reedy River]], near [[Fork Shoals, South Carolina]], on June 26. The ruptured pipeline released about {{convert|957,600|USgal|L}} of fuel oil into the Reedy River and surrounding areas. The spill polluted a {{convert|34|mi|km|adj=on}} stretch of the Reedy River, causing significant environmental damage. Floating oil extended about {{convert|23|mi|km}} down the river. Approximately 35,000 fish were killed, along with other aquatic organisms and wildlife. The estimated cost to Colonial Pipeline for cleanup and settlement with the State of South Carolina was $20.5 million. No one was injured in the accident. The pipeline was operating at reduced pressure due to know corrosion issues, but pipeline operator confusion led to an accidental return to normal pressure in that pipeline section, causing the rupture.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1998/PAR9801.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007135920/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1998/PAR9801.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref><ref name="epa.gov"/>
* 1996 On August 4, {{convert|420,000|USgal|L}} of unspecified petroleum product spilled from a Lakehead pipe near [[Donaldson, Minnesota]].<ref name="duluthnewstribune.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.duluthnewstribune.com/event/article/id/175781/group/Investigations/|title=Pipeline Report : Investigations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130121183236/http://www.duluthnewstribune.com/event/article/id/175781/group/Investigations/ |archivedate=January 21, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1996 A Koch butane pipeline ruptured, causing an explosion and fire, near [[Kemp, Texas]], on August 24. Two teenagers were killed after driving into the unseen butane cloud while going to report the pipeline leak. A mobile home was also destroyed by the fire. The leak was caused by external corrosion. The pipeline was only 15 years old at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/23pipelively.html|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101015212611/http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/23pipelively.html |archivedate=October 15, 2010 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/23pipelively2.html|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101016231606/http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/23pipelively2.html |archivedate=October 16, 2010 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=LTxIAAAAIBAJ&sjid=doEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3192,1044453&dq=koch+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1998/PAR9802.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140611014017/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1998/PAR9802.pdf |archivedate=June 11, 2014 }}</ref>
* 1996 On September 26, a bulldozer operator in [[Grand Haven, Michigan]] hit & ruptured a Wolverine pipeline. Petroleum ignited, burning the bulldozer operator. About 43,000 gallons of petroleum product were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=110&dat=19960926&id=JQ9QAAAAIBAJ&sjid=O1UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5718,8419468|title=Ludington Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269294|title=Sept. 26, 1996 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 In October, the Yellowstone Pipeline was found to be leaking in [[Spokane County, Washington]]. An unknown amount of petroleum products has contaminated soil in the area, requiring soil remediation.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=20040523&id=y89YAAAAIBAJ&sjid=0_IDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4946,1644450|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 A leaking [[Amoco]] pipeline caused traffic to be shut down on an industrial area street in [[Hammond, Indiana]], starting on October 17. About 1,250 barrels of gasoline were spilled. The leak was caused by external corrosion of the pipeline, installed in 1928.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nwitimes.com/uncategorized/amoco-pipeline-may-have-sprung-a-leak/article_97f130ee-ec84-5b0d-af16-b7103f07a274.html|title=Amoco pipeline may have sprung a leak|author=DEBRA GRUSZECKI|work=nwitimes.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269313|title=Oct. 17, 1996 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1996 On October 23, in [[Tiger Pass, Louisiana]], the crew of a Bean Horizon Corporation dredge dropped a stern spud into the bottom of the channel in preparation for dredging operations. The spud struck and ruptured a 12-inch submerged natural gas steel pipeline. The pressurized natural gas released from the pipeline enveloped the stern of the dredge and an accompanying tug, then ignited, destroying the dredge and the tug. No fatalities resulted from the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/summary/par9801s.htm|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140220043240/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/summary/PAR9801S.htm |archivedate=February 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>[http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1998/par9801s.pdf ]{{dead link|date=June 2017}}</ref>
* 1996 A [[Colonial Pipeline]] stubline in [[Murfreesboro, Tennessee]] was undergoing maintenance on November 5. The pipeline was returned to service, but a valve on that pipeline was accidentally left closed from the maintenance, causing pressure from restarting to rupture the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1999/PAB9903.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007135931/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1999/PAB9903.pdf |archivedate=October 7, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1996 On November 21, an explosion occurred in a shoe store and office building in [[Rio Piedras, Puerto Rico]]. Thirty-three people were killed, and at least 69 were injured. Crews from the local gas provider, Enron, had not found any gas leaks previously, despite complaints of propane odor in the buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1997/PAR9701.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140123230106/http://www.ntsb.gov/doclib/reports/1997/PAR9701.pdf |archivedate=January 23, 2014 }}</ref>
* 1996 On December 11 a natural gas line operated by Williams ruptured just north of Tonganoxie Kansas. Corrosion around a fitting called a "T-Drip" failed which allowed gas to escape.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=19961212&id=_HQyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=k-cFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5193,853275 |title=Investigation continues into natural gas pipeline explosion |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www2.ljworld.com/news/1996/dec/11/gas_line_fireball_visible/ |author=Ric Anderson |date=December 11, 1996 |title=GAS LINE FIREBALL VISIBLE FOR MILES |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1996 on December 26, a bulldozer ruptured a 10-inch LPG pipeline near [[Maringouin, Louisiana]], forcing the evacuation of nearby resident. There was no explosion or fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=AD&p_theme=ad&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB4783E03D1A89E&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=90 ordered to evacuate after pipeline rupture |date=December 27, 1996 |website=Nl.newsbank.com |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269366 |title=Dec. 26, 1996 - ProPublica |website=Projects.propublica.org |date=1996-12-26 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref>

===1997===
* 1997 On February 6, a seal on a pump at a pump station, on a MAPCO natural gasoline pipeline, near [[Molville, Iowa]] failed, allowing the product to leak. fire then broke out, forcing all residents within a mile of station to evacuate for a time. There were no injuries. About 200 gallons of natural gasoline burned<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1066&dat=19970213&id=3LA4AAAAIBAJ&sjid=1RIGAAAAIBAJ&pg=1333,844221|title=Moville Record - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269406|title=Feb. 6, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 A 26-inch gas transmission pipeline failed on February 8, near [[Everson, Washington]], lighting up the night sky, visible for 40 miles. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1914&dat=19970210&id=YMkgAAAAIBAJ&sjid=32oFAAAAIBAJ&pg=1206,1200677|title=Sun Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1997 On February 9, a gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Kalama, Washington]], causing a massive fire. A few people were evacuated for a time. There were no injuries. It was the second failure of a Northwestern Pipeline Corp. gas transmission pipeline in 2 days in the state of Washington.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=19970209&id=yG1XAAAAIBAJ&sjid=dPEDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6434,7974065&hl=en|title=The Spokesman-Review - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269409|title=Feb. 9, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1997 On March 1, an 8-inch SFPP (now Kinder Morgan) petroleum products pipeline was discovered to be leaking near [[Truckee, California]]. Some of the spilled product reached Summit Creek. While there were efforts to keep the leaked product from reaching [[Donner Lake]], the spill size of this leak was listed as zero, in the report given to PHMSA.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19970306&id=XsM0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=SSEGAAAAIBAJ&pg=3574,691316|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269421|title=March 1, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>   
* 1997 A leak was detected on a 12-inch pipeline near [[Mount Morris, Illinois]] on May 9. Between 125,000 and {{convert|130,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline were spilled. A month later, gasoline was till being extracted from the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=epBSAAAAIBAJ&sjid=1cQMAAAAIBAJ&pg=2975,1495723&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Telegraph-Herald - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 A [[Koch Industries]] crude oil pipeline was spotted leaking by a pipeline patrol aircraft on May 12, near [[Bayside, Texas]]. About 75,600 gallons of crude spilled, affecting marshlands.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19970513&id=_DIKAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IUsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5213,2510921|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269477|title=May 12, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 On May 30, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] spilled approximately {{convert|18,900|USgal|L}} of gasoline, some of which entered an unnamed creek and its adjoining shoreline in the Bear Creek watershed near [[Athens, Georgia]]. During the spill, a vapor cloud of gasoline formed, causing several Colonial employees to flee for safety. This spill resulted from a calculation error related to a regular procedure. No one checked the calculations, nor did Colonial have a procedure in place to check such calculations.<ref name="epa.gov">{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/colonial.html|title=Compliance Resources : Colonial Pipeline Report |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028062657/http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/colonial.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* 1997 Two different sections of a [[Conoco]] pipeline were ruptured by earth movement just a few days apart. On June 20, the pipeline ruptured near [[Lodge Grass, Montana]], on the [[Crow Indian]] reservation, spilling 1,612 barrels of gasoline. On June 26, the same pipeline again failed from earth movement near [[Banner, Wyoming]], spilling 704 barrels of gasoline. The Lodge Grass section of pipeline resulted in 3,400 feet of new pipeline being buried 6 to feet deep to avoid soft soil, deeper than the required 3 feet of soil coverage. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://mtstandard.com/news/state-and-regional/cleanup-investigation-underway-after-phillips-pipeline-leaks-gas-on-crow/article_95f61dd6-2768-5db1-a10d-b25d368738f6.html|title=Cleanup, investigation underway after Phillips 66 pipeline leaks gas on Crow land|author=Cindy Uken|work=Montana Standard|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269510|title=June 26, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 A gas pipeline was ruptured and caused an explosion and fire, in [[Indianapolis, Indiana]], on July 21. A 20-inch steel natural gas transmission pipeline was ruptured by a contractor for the gas company, and released natural gas near an intersection adjoining the Charter Pointe subdivision. The gas ignited and burned, killing one resident and injuring another. About 75 residents required temporary shelter. Six homes were destroyed, and about 65 others sustained damage significant enough to be documented by the local investigation team. A nearby [[directional drilling]] operation had hit & weakened the pipeline before the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/fulltext/pab9902.htm|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=June 15, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140220045516/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/fulltext/PAB9902.htm |archivedate=February 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thestarpress.com/article/20121115/NEWS06/121115014|title=Updates - The Star Press - thestarpress.com|work=The Star Press|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 On August 11, a [[Chevron Corporation]] LPG pipeline leaked in [[Dayton, Texas]], forcing the evacuation of 3,500 inmates from nearby correctional facilities. 5,041 barrels of LPG were lost. There were no injuries, and the failure caused was listed as "Miscellaneous".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19970813&id=uHxOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=XUsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=7051,2287648|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269534|title=Aug. 11, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>  
* 1997 In August, residents in [[Vacaville, California]] noticed petroleum fumes, but a leaking pipeline was not found until September 10. A hairline crack from the pipe's manufacturing was the cause, and 20,000 to {{convert|60,000|USgal|L}} of petroleum products had leaked by the time the source was found.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.co.solano.ca.us:80/depts/bos/meetings/agendas/displaydoc.asp?NavID=473&ID=1172|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120303115953/http://www.co.solano.ca.us/depts/bos/meetings/agendas/displaydoc.asp?NavID=473&ID=1172 |archivedate=March 3, 2012 }}</ref>
* 1997 Construction equipment ruptured a [[Plantation Pipeline]] line in [[Fairfax, Virginia]] on September 9, releasing over 2,000 gallons of petroleum products.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269554|title=Sept. 9, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.homefacts.com/environmentalhazards/Virginia/Fairfax-County.html#|title=Fairfax County, VA Hazardous Waste Superfund Sites|work=homefacts.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 Over a period of years, more than {{convert|420,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline spilled from small leaks in [[Colonial Pipeline]] near Darling Creek in [[St. Helena Parish, Louisiana]], before Colonial finally discovered the leak in December 1997. As of September 1999, a plume of gasoline, including leaded gasoline, extended over approximately {{convert|14|acre|m2}} on the groundwater surface, more than {{convert|60|acre|m2}} of groundwater had been contaminated, and some of the gasoline had entered Darling Creek.<ref name="epa.gov"/>
* 1997 On December 12, a Mid-Valley pipeline leaked at a pump station in [[Cygnet, Ohio]], spill ing about 4200 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19971213&id=-kpPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=kQMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=3895,5160397|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269621|title=Dec. 12, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1997 A [Plains All American Pipeline] pipe ruptured from external corrosion, on December 13, in rural [[San Bernardino County, California]], spilling about 541,000 gallons of crude oil. About 322,000 gallons of crude were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.co.coos.or.us/portals/0/planning/luba/572-674.pdf |format=PDF |title=Exhibit N : Pipeline Tragedies Across the U.S. |website=Co.coos.or.us |accessdate=2017-06-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269622|title=Dec. 13, 1997 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mlive.com/news/kalamazoo/index.ssf/2015/07/oil_spill_database.html?appSession=816163679213103&RecordID=140&PageID=8&PrevPageID=2&cpipage=1&CPIsortType=&CPIorderBy=&cbCurrentRecordPosition=2|title=Database: Compare Kalamazoo River oil spill to other U.S. pipeline spills|work=MLive.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>

===1998===
* 1998 On January 22, at least 41,000 gallons of light crude oil was spilled into the [[Gulf of Mexico]] {{convert|50|mi|km}} south of [[Galveston, Texas]] by a leaking [[Amoco]] pipeline. The pipe had been damaged by third party activity.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QwNZAAAAIBAJ&sjid=9koDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6590,4180568&dq=amoco+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269650|title=Jan. 22, 1998 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 On February 14, a landslide during a serious storm ruptured a [[Shell Oil Company]] pipeline in [[Ventura County, California]], spilling about 10,000 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2245&dat=19980217&id=-sM0AAAAIBAJ&sjid=LyEGAAAAIBAJ&pg=5362,5401625|title=Lodi News-Sentinel - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269667|title=Feb. 14, 1998 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 On March 4, a backhoe hit a natural gas pipeline in [[Attleboro, Massachusetts]]. The gas later exploded and burned, killing 2 people, injuring 6 others, and causing extensive property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1914&dat=19980305&id=StogAAAAIBAJ&sjid=UmsFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4862,529728|title=Sun Journal - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1998 A rupture in [[Colonial Pipeline]] in a landfill at [[Sandy Springs, Georgia]], discovered on March 30, resulted in the release of more than {{convert|30,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline. When the pipe was excavated, it was found to be buckled and cracked. The NTSB found that the pipeline ruptured because of settlement of soil and trash underneath the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1999/PAB9901.htm|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110225085145/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/1999/PAB9901.htm |archivedate=February 25, 2011 }}</ref>
* 1998 On April 4, a tow of the M/V Anne Holly, comprising 12 loaded and 2 empty barges, which was traveling northbound on the Mississippi River through the St. Louis Harbor, struck the Missouri-side pier of the center span of the Eads Bridge. Three of these barges drifted toward the President Casino on the Admiral, a permanently moored vessel below the bridge on the Missouri side of the river. A natural gas leak resulted when the natural gas supply line to the Admiral was severed in the course of the accident. When the line broke, natural gas began escaping. Although the escaping gas did not ignite, the gas leak had continued for about 3 hours before being stopped.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/recs/letters/2000/P00_14.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090830154441/http://ntsb.gov/Recs/letters/2000/P00_14.pdf |archivedate=August 30, 2009 }}</ref>
* 1998 In [[South Riding, Virginia]], on July 7, a natural gas explosion and fire destroyed a newly constructed residence in the South Riding community in [[Loudoun County, Virginia]]. A family consisting of a husband and wife and their two children were spending their first night in their new home at the time of the explosion. As a result of the accident, the wife was killed, the husband was seriously injured, and the two children received minor injuries. Five other homes and two vehicles were damaged.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2001/PAR0101.htm|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110225091526/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2001/PAR0101.htm |archivedate=February 25, 2011 }}</ref>
* 1998 On July 14, an earth mover hit an 8-inch LPG pipeline, near [[Placedo, Texas]]. The operator of the equipment was killed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19980715&id=-yFOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GEsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4622,2752934&hl=en|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|website=news.google.com}}</ref>
* 1998 Lightning struck a Florida Gas Transmission Co. natural gas compressor plant near [[Perry, Florida]] on August 13, causing an explosion and massive fire. A second explosion later followed, injuring 5 firefighters & pipeline company employees. 6 nearby homes were also destroyed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://sites.google.com/site/taylorcountyhistory/home/2a-taylor-county/gas-plant-fire|title=Gas Plant Fire - Taylor County & Perry, Florida History|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 A bulldozer operator on July 14 hit an 8-inch LP gas pipeline in [[Placedo, Texas]]. The gas caught fire, and the operator was burned to death. 100 acres of nearby brush were burned from the fire. 2 charred pipeline warning signs were within 10 yards of the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19980715&id=-yFOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GEsDAAAAIBAJ&pg=4622,2752934|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 On September 22, a {{convert|8810|oilbbl|m3}} crude oil spill from a Lakehead (now Enbridge) pipeline near [[Plummer, Minnesota]] was caused by an excavator hitting that pipeline.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=GF&s_site=grandforks&p_multi=GF&p_theme=realcities&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EB6EC8FA00A810B&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |date=September 22, 1998 |title=OIL SPILL CLEANUP CONTINUES, COSTS MOUNT AREA EXCAVATOR INVESTIGATED AS POSSIBLE CAUSE OF 256,000-GALLON CRUDE OIL PIPELINE LEAK |accessdate=August 28, 2013}}</ref>
* 1998 On October 1, a break in a [[BP]] pipeline near the Mississippi Canyon in the [[Gulf of Mexico]], off of the [[Louisiana]] coast, spilled about 155,000 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2026&dat=19981002&id=Cb8jAAAAIBAJ&sjid=49AFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3058,152293|title=Moscow-Pullman Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 On December 3, crews installing a new pipeline hit a [[natural gas liquids]] (NGL) pipeline near [[Moab, Utah]], with escaping product igniting near Highway U-191, injuring 4 pipeline workers. Asphalt in the road was melted, and traffic was stopped.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1891&dat=19981204&id=1zdHAAAAIBAJ&sjid=v_0MAAAAIBAJ&pg=2650,326613|title=Gadsden Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1998 On December 8, a gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned, forcing a dozen families within a 2-mile radius of the fire to evacuate, near [[Essex Township, Kankakee County, Illinois|Essex Township, Illinois]]. The fire was 15 stories tall. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1998-12-09/news/9812090220_1_natural-gas-pipeline-explosion-propane-tank|title=Gas Explosion Shakes Rural Area|work=tribunedigital-chicagotribune|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
*'''[[1998 St. Cloud explosion]]''': On December 11, while attempting to install a utility pole support anchor in a city sidewalk in St. Cloud, Minnesota, a communications network installation crew struck and ruptured an underground, 1-inch, high-pressure plastic gas service pipeline, thereby precipitating a natural gas leak. About 39&nbsp;minutes later, while utility workers and emergency response personnel were taking preliminary precautions and assessing the situation, an explosion occurred. As a result of the explosion, 4 persons were fatally injured; 1 person was seriously injured; and 10 persons, including 2 firefighters and 1 police officer, received minor injuries. Six buildings were destroyed. Damage assessments estimated property losses at $399,000.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2000/PAR0001.htm |title=Pipeline Report|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110225085434/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2000/PAR0001.htm |archivedate=February 25, 2011 }}</ref>

===1999===
* 1999 On January 2, a natural gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned at a pipeline facility near [[Pendleton, Oregon]]. Flames reached 500 feet high, and several town lost gas service for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=19990104&id=_CJOAAAAIBAJ&sjid=T4UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5793,666681|title=The Victoria Advocate - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1999 Natural Gas Explosion and Fire at a gas pressure station, [[Wytheville, Virginia]], destroying a home and motorcycle store.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1P1-22246627.html|title=Pipeline Report |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121104153326/http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1P1-22246627.html |archivedate=November 4, 2012 }}</ref> (January 3, 1999)
* 1999 On January 8, a leak in a 12-inch pipe at a [[Koch Industries]] tank farm in [[Benavides County, Texas]] spilled about 10,500 barrels of crude oil. The cause was internal corrosion of the pipe.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/269938|title=Jan. 8, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="phmsa.dot.gov"/>
* 1999 In [[Bridgeport, Alabama]], on January 22, while digging a trench behind a building, a backhoe operator damaged a 3/4-inch steel natural gas service line and a 1-inch water service line. This resulted in two leaks in the natural gas service line, which was operated at 35 psig. One leak occurred where the backhoe bucket had contacted and pulled the natural gas service line. The other was a physical separation of the gas service line at an underground joint near the meter, which was close to the building. Gas migrated into a building nearby, where it ignited. An explosion followed, destroying three buildings. Other buildings within a two-block area of the explosion sustained significant damage. Three fatalities, five serious injuries, and one minor injury resulted from this accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2000/PAB0001.htm |title=Pipeline Report|accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110225084216/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2000/PAB0001.htm |archivedate=February 25, 2011 }}</ref>
* 1999 On January 23, a construction crew ruptured a 10-inch diameter petroleum products pipe near [[Germantown, Wisconsin]], spilling about 41,000 gallons of gasoline.<ref name="phmsa.dot.gov">{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.ebdc7a8a7e39f2e55cf2031050248a0c/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print|title=PHMSA - Data & Statistics  - Distribution, Transmission & Gathering, LNG, and Liquid Accident and Incident Data|work=dot.gov|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304042351/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320125016H/320125016H_Corrective+Action+Order_07202012.pdf|title=Wayback Machine|date=4 March 2016|publisher=}}</ref>
* 1999 A pipeline ruptured in [[Knoxville, Tennessee]], and released over {{convert|53,000|USgal|L}} of diesel fuel into the Tennessee River on February 9. A brittle-like crack was found on the pipe in an area of coating failure. The NTSB expressed concern that the material's toughness had a role in this rupture. Two days before the rupture, an in-line inspection device was run through the pipe segment, with no anomalies in the rupture area reported. Contributing to the severity of the accident was [[Colonial Pipeline]] Company's failure to determine from the SCADA system that a leak had occurred, with the result that the pipeline controller started and restarted the pipeline, increasing the amount of diesel fuel that was released.<ref name="epa.gov"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2001/PAB0101.pdf|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101205090435/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2001/PAB0101.pdf |archivedate=December 5, 2010 }}</ref>
* 1999 On May 1, excavation equipment damaged a [[Koch Industries]] pipeline in [[Pleasant Hill, Iowa]], spilling 3,663 barrels of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270017|title=May 1, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1999 A pipeline in a [[Bellingham, Washington]] park ruptured and leaked gasoline, and later vapor from the leak exploded and burned, killing two 10-year-old boys and an 18-year-old man on June 10, 1999. Issues causing the rupture were found to be previous pipe damage by excavation, an incorrectly set up pressure relief valve, unexpected repeated remote valve closures, and new software tests on the live controlling computer.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2002/PAR0202.htm|title=Safety Recommendations |accessdate=February 4, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110520050951/http://www.ntsb.gov/publictn/2002/PAR0202.htm |archivedate=May 20, 2011 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ens-newswire.com/ens/may2002/2002-05-31-06.html|title=Negligence Caused Pipeline Explosion, Suit Charges|work=ens-newswire.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=http://www.seattlepi.com/news/article/In-deal-Olympic-Pipe-Line-3-workers-admit-guilt-1103162.php | work=Seattle Post-Intelligencer | first1=Tracy | last1=Johnson | first2=Vanessa | last2=Ho | title=In deal, Olympic Pipe Line, 3 workers admit guilt in blast | date=December 11, 2002}}</ref>
* 1999 On June 24, about 100 barrels of gasoline spilled in a [[Buckeye Partners]] Terminal in [[Breinigsville, Pennsylvania]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270040|title=June 24, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=19990627&id=2qUuAAAAIBAJ&sjid=EdoFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4361,6108242|title=Beaver County Times - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1999 On August 10, an auger being used to install utility poles hit a 14-inch ethane-propane pipeline, causing an explosion & fire that killed the auger operator, and forcing evacuations near [[Liberty Hill, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://madmax.lmtonline.com/textarchives/0811/s14.htm|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130717082828/http://madmax.lmtonline.com/textarchives/0811/s14.htm|deadurl=yes|title=Man killed in pipeline explosion|date=17 July 2013|archivedate=17 July 2013|publisher=}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270085|title=Aug. 10, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref> 
* 1999 On August 29, a pump on Olympic Pipeline failed in [[Renton, Washington]], spilling about 3,360 gallons on gasoline and aviation fuel. ABout 950 tons of soil were removed due to contamination.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2026&dat=19990916&id=ubsjAAAAIBAJ&sjid=kdAFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6430,1582306|title=Moscow-Pullman Daily News - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270105|title=Aug. 29, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1999 A Lakehead Pipeline (now [[Enbridge]]) was damaged by outside force on November 1, near [[Crystal Falls, Michigan]]. 400 people were evacuated from the area. Fire was used to burn some of the released substances, so, of about 223,000 gallons of NGL's and crude oil spilled, only about 115,000 gallons were recovered, with over 2,100 yards of contaminated soil removed in just the first 2 weeks of cleaning. The pipe broke where it was on a rock in the pipeline trench.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=19991112&id=zQ0wAAAAIBAJ&sjid=3wMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=4565,3957948|title=Toledo Blade - Google News Archive Search|work=google.com|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
* 1999 On November 19, 2 men were injured in [[Salt Flat, Texas]], when a leaking 8-inch propane pipeline exploded. 2 school buses had passed through the area moments before the explosion. About 6,195 barrels of propane were leaked. The pipeline failed from external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://lubbockonline.com/stories/111999/sta_1119990083.shtml |title=Liquid propane gas pipeline explosion injures two truck drivers near El Paso &#124; Lubbock Online &#124; Lubbock Avalanche-Journal |publisher=Lubbock Online |date=1999-11-19 |accessdate=2016-01-18}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270175|title=Nov. 17, 1999 - ProPublica|work=propublica.org|accessdate=18 January 2016}}</ref>
